| `determ test-governance-param-determinism` | A5 PARAM_CHANGE staging/activation/validator-forwarding determinism (E1 R40; FA-Apply-8 companion). 21 assertions across eight blocks: staging records a pending entry keyed by `effective_height` and is byte-stable across replays; off-whitelist param names silently rejected at staging with no state drift; activation drains on the height match and mutates the chain field deterministically (insertion-order resolution within a height bucket); **validator-field forwarding** — the apply path mutates chain state AND propagates the change into the active validator config so consensus uses the new value on the next block (the chain/validator-config-sync contract T-G6); future-effective-height entries preserve staging across intervening blocks; idempotent activation under restore + replay; A1 unitary-supply invariance across all PARAM_CHANGE transitions (no balance/stake/receipt fields touched); and byte-identical `compute_state_root` across two independent replays of the same staging+activation sequence. Pins the FA-Apply-8 (`GovernanceParamChange.md`) apply-path contract at unit-test cost; complements network-level `tools/test_governance.sh` + apply-level `tools/test_param_change_apply.sh`. | `tools/test_governance_param_determinism.sh` |
| `determ test-state-proof-composite-key` | Asserts Chain::state_proof over the three composite-key namespaces (i: applied receipts, m: merge_state, p: pending_param_changes): each reconstructed binary key body re-verifies against compute_state_root() via crypto::merkle_verify; cross-namespace value_hashes are distinct; wrong/absent keys, a little-endian (non-big-endian) m: body, and a tampered value_hash all return nullopt/reject; proofs are deterministic across calls. | `tools/test_state_proof_composite_key.sh` |
| `determ test-state-proof-value-hash` | Light-client VALUE-ENCODING contract for Chain::state_proof — pins that a proof's value_hash EQUALS the SHA-256 of the documented per-namespace field encoding (src/chain/chain.cpp::build_state_leaves), not merely that it verifies under the root (the membership-only coverage of test-state-proof-namespaces / test-state-proof-composite-key). 11 assertions over four simple namespaces: a: SHA256(u64(balance)\|\|u64(next_nonce)), s: SHA256(u64(locked)\|\|u64(unlock_height)), k:min_stake SHA256(u64), c:genesis_total SHA256(u64) at on-tree key "k:c:genesis_total". For each, an external verifier recomputes the expected value_hash from raw getters (balance/next_nonce/stake/stake_unlock_height/min_stake/genesis_total) and confirms it equals the proof's value_hash AND re-verifies via crypto::merkle_verify under compute_state_root(). Also asserts a:-field-order sensitivity (nonce\|\|balance diverges), s:-fixture sanity (locked==500), cross-namespace value distinctness, tamper rejection (value_hash from a wrong balance 9999 fails verify), and recomputation determinism. Protects every off-node light client that reconstructs value_hash to learn the meaning (balance/nonce/stake/constant) of a proven leaf. | `tools/test_state_proof_value_hash.sh` |
| `determ test-dapp-registry-trustless-read` | v2.18 trustless d:-namespace DApp-registry reader — reconstruct the `d:` + domain key, recompute the d: leaf value_hash off-node from the entry's canonical fields (service_pubkey/endpoint_url/topics/activity), bind it to the state_proof, and merkle_verify under the committed state_root; field-tamper (endpoint_url, service_pubkey), op=1 deactivation re-binding, absent-domain + wrong-namespace rejection, determinism (10 assertions) | `tools/test_dapp_registry_trustless_read.sh` |
| `determ test-rpc-auth-hmac` | S-001 / v2.16 RPC HMAC-SHA-256 authentication contract (S-035 Option 1 seed). The production verifier `RpcServer::verify_auth` and client signer `rpc_call` live in `src/rpc/rpc.cpp` behind an asio io_context + Node, so this test re-implements the identical auth-field algebra in-process: `canonical_for_hmac(method, params) = method + "\|" + params.dump()`, `auth = hex(HMAC-SHA-256(secret, canonical))`, and the constant-time compare. 17 assertions: canonical message format (single `\|` separator, method first, empty-object params → `method\|{}`); HMAC digest shape (64 lowercase hex chars / 32 bytes); determinism over identical inputs; constant-time compare accept on equal + reject on single-nibble difference; length-guard rejection for shorter / longer / empty `auth` field (no out-of-range indexing); client/server agreement across a `dump()`/`parse()` round-trip (the load-bearing nlohmann key-order stability property flagged in rpc.cpp); tamper/replay sensitivity (wrong secret, wrong method, any params-field change each yield a rejected tag); empty-secret auth-disabled signal. Pure-function counterpart to `tools/test_rpc_hmac_auth.sh` (which exercises the same surface end-to-end through a live 3-node cluster) | `tools/test_rpc_auth_hmac.sh` |
| `determ test-unstake-eligibility` | Trustless UNSTAKE-eligibility reader — Merkle-verifies the `s:` stake leaf under the anchored `state_root`, reconstructs the `SHA256(u64_be(locked)‖u64_be(unlock_height))` leaf from claimed cleartext, evaluates `eligible = unlock_height != UINT64_MAX && head_height >= unlock_height`, and rejects a lied `unlock_height`/`locked`. 12 assertions. | `tools/test_unstake_eligibility.sh` |

## Forensics / governance

| Command / RPC | Purpose |
|---|---|
| RPC `submit_equivocation { event }` | External submission of equivocation evidence (validates two-sig proof, gossips for slashing) |

There's no built-in CLI wrapper for the equivocation RPC — see `tools/test_equivocation_slashing.sh` for a Python template that synthesizes evidence and submits via raw JSON-RPC.

### Governance (A5)

| Command | Purpose |
|---|---|
| `determ submit-param-change --priv <hex> --from <domain> --name <NAME> --value-hex <hex> --effective-height <N> --keyholder-sig <idx>:<priv_hex> [--keyholder-sig ...] [--fee N] [--rpc-port N]` | Sign + submit a `PARAM_CHANGE` tx. `--name` must be on the validator whitelist (MIN_STAKE, SUSPENSION_SLASH, UNSTAKE_DELAY, bft_escalation_threshold, tx_commit_ms, block_sig_ms, abort_claim_ms, param_keyholders, param_threshold). Each `--keyholder-sig` supplies one signature; threshold must be met. Sender (`--from`) is a registered domain that pays the fee. See `tools/test_governance_param_change.sh` for an end-to-end example. |

Genesis fields enabling governance:
- `governance_mode: 0` (uncontrolled, default) or `1` (governed)
- `param_keyholders: [<hex pubkey>, ...]` (Ed25519 founder set)
- `param_threshold: <N>` (default N-of-N when keyholders are set)

### Under-quorum merge (R4)

| Command | Purpose |
|---|---|
| `determ submit-merge-event --priv <hex> --from <domain> --event {begin\|end} --shard-id N --partner-id N --effective-height N --evidence-window-start N [--refugee-region <region>] [--fee N] [--rpc-port N]` | Sign + submit a `MERGE_EVENT` tx. Requires `sharding_mode == EXTENDED`. Operator-driven for v1.x; auto-detection on the beacon is a v1.1 work item. See `tools/test_under_quorum_merge.sh`. |

Genesis thresholds:
- `merge_threshold_blocks` (default 100) — consecutive blocks of `eligible_in_region < 2K` before `MERGE_BEGIN` validates.
- `revert_threshold_blocks` (default 200) — 2:1 hysteresis on the way back.
- `merge_grace_blocks` (default 10) — gap between block height and `effective_height`.

## Common flags

- `--rpc-port N` — connect to an RPC port other than the config default (useful when running multiple nodes locally).
- `--data-dir D` — point at a non-default data directory.

## Operator config fields (`config.json`)

The node's `config.json` (generated by `determ init`) carries the runtime knobs. Live values are visible at `determ status` → `protections` block. The most operationally-relevant entries:

### Network / consensus

| Field | Default | Purpose |
|---|---|---|
| `domain` | (required) | This node's registered identity (must match a `genesis.initial_creators` entry) |
| `data_dir` | (CWD) | Root for chain.json / keyfile / snapshot output |
| `listen_port` | 7777 | Gossip listen port |
| `rpc_port` | 7778 | RPC listen port |
| `bootstrap_peers` | `[]` | Initial intra-chain peers (e.g. `["127.0.0.1:7771","127.0.0.1:7772"]`) |
| `beacon_peers` | `[]` | Cross-chain peers for SHARD-role nodes (beacon addresses) — role-filtered, isolated from `bootstrap_peers` traffic |
| `shard_peers` | `[]` | Cross-chain peers for BEACON-role nodes (shard addresses) — role-filtered |
| `m_creators` | 3 | Committee size K (genesis-pinned at chain init; per-node override rejected) |
| `k_block_sigs` | 3 | Phase-2 threshold (genesis-pinned; K = M = strong BFT, K < M = weak hybrid) |
| `bft_enabled` | true | Per-height BFT escalation after `bft_escalation_threshold` aborts |
| `bft_escalation_threshold` | 5 | Round-1 + Round-2 abort count that triggers BFT mode (governance-mutable) |
| `tx_commit_ms` / `block_sig_ms` / `abort_claim_ms` | 200/200/100 | Round timer durations |
| `chain_role` / `sharding_mode` / `shard_id` / `committee_region` | `single`/`current`/0/`""` | Sharding posture (genesis-pinned) |
| `initial_shard_count` | 1 | Number of shards S in this deployment (genesis-pinned) |
| `epoch_blocks` | 1000 | Committee re-seeding period (genesis-pinned) |
| `region` | `""` | This validator's self-declared region tag (R1 — mirrored into REGISTER payload). Must match the chain's `committee_region` to be selected for committees under EXTENDED sharding |

### RPC security (S-001 / S-014 / v2.16)

| Field | Default | Purpose |
|---|---|---|
| `rpc_localhost_only` | `true` | Bind RPC to 127.0.0.1 only (S-001) — flip to `false` ONLY with `rpc_auth_secret` set, or behind a reverse proxy with auth |
| `rpc_auth_secret` | `""` | Hex-encoded shared secret for HMAC-SHA-256 RPC auth (v2.16); empty = no auth. Generate with `openssl rand -hex 32` |
| `rpc_rate_per_sec` | 0 | RPC calls/sec per peer-IP token bucket (S-014 RPC side); 0 = disabled. Suggested external-bind: 100 |
| `rpc_rate_burst` | 0 | Bucket capacity; 0 = disabled. Suggested external-bind: 200 |

### Gossip security (S-014 / S-022 / S-026)

| Field | Default | Purpose |
|---|---|---|
| `gossip_rate_per_sec` | 0 | Inbound-message rate cap per peer-IP (S-014 gossip side); 0 = disabled. Suggested external-bind: 500 |
| `gossip_rate_burst` | 0 | Bucket capacity; 0 = disabled. Suggested external-bind: 1000 |

(S-022 per-message-type body cap and S-026 TCP keepalive are unconditional — no operator knob; see `docs/SECURITY.md` §S-022 + §S-026.)

### Operator hygiene (S-027)

| Field | Default | Purpose |
|---|---|---|
| `log_quiet` | `false` | When `true`, suppress per-block / per-bundle / per-connection diagnostic lines. WARN/ERROR diagnostics surface regardless. Production deployments wanting fewer logs set this to `true` |

### Paths

| Field | Purpose |
|---|---|
| `domain` | This node's registered identity (must match a `genesis.initial_creators` entry) |
| `genesis_path` / `genesis_hash` | Authoritative genesis file + pinned hash for eclipse defense |
| `chain_path` | On-disk chain.json — wrapped `{head_hash, blocks}` form post-S-021 |
| `key_path` | Node's Ed25519 keypair (0600 permissions) |
| `snapshot_path` | If set on a fresh node, bootstrap from this snapshot instead of replaying from genesis |
| `shard_manifest_path` | BEACON-role nodes: per-shard committee_region map (required in EXTENDED mode) |

A live readback of which protections are active is in `determ status` → `protections` (see top of this doc). Wallet keys live separately in `determ-wallet` keyfiles (encrypted at rest via v2.17 AES-256-GCM envelope; see `determ-wallet` section below).

## determ-wallet binary (A2)

Separate executable from the `determ` daemon. Secret material never enters the chain daemon's address space — by design. The wallet handles the user's Ed25519 seed and threshold recovery; the daemon never sees them.

### Primitive layers

| Command | Purpose |
|---|---|
| `determ-wallet shamir split <hex> -t T -n N` | Split a secret into N Shamir shares with threshold T. Shares print one per line as `<x_hex>:<y_hex>`. |
| `determ-wallet shamir combine <share> [<share> ...]` | Reconstruct from ≥ T shares. Returns the original secret hex. |
| `determ-wallet envelope encrypt --plaintext <hex> --password <str> [--aad <hex>] [--iters N]` | AEAD-wrap arbitrary data (AES-256-GCM, PBKDF2-HMAC-SHA-256 keying, default 600k iters). |
| `determ-wallet envelope decrypt --envelope <blob> --password <str> [--aad <hex>]` | Unwrap. Returns plaintext hex; exit code 2 on AEAD tag failure. |
| `determ-wallet shard-route --address <addr> (--salt <hex64> --shard-count <N> \| --genesis <file\|-> \| --snapshot <file\|->) [--my-shard <N>] [--json]` | OFFLINE address-to-shard router. Reproduces consensus `crypto::shard_id_for_address` (src/crypto/random.cpp) byte-for-byte — the deterministic map every node/beacon/wallet agrees on (rev.9 B3). `shard_count<=1 => shard 0`; else `h = SHA-256(salt[32] \|\| "shard-route" \|\| addr)`, fold `h[0..7]` big-endian into a u64, `shard = u64 mod shard_count`. salt+count from genesis (`shard_address_salt`/`initial_shard_count`); supply explicitly or read a genesis/snapshot JSON (explicit flags override file values). `--my-shard` reports `cross_shard = (route != N)`, the `src/chain/chain.cpp::is_cross_shard` predicate. Pure local SHA-256 + modulo; no RPC/daemon/network. `--json` emits {address, shard_count, shard, digest_hex, my_shard?, cross_shard?}. Exit 0 success, 1 args/parse/IO/range error. |
| `address-classify` | `(--address <id> [--address <id> ...] \| --addresses <id,id,...\|@file>) [--json]` | OFFLINE classifier + S-028 canonicalizer for on-chain account identifiers (anon bearer addresses + domain names). Reproduces `is_anon_address` / `normalize_anon_address` (include/determ/types.hpp) byte-for-byte: anon = `0x`+64 hex (case-insensitive on input), canonical lowercases ONLY the 64-hex tail; domains pass through verbatim; a malformed `0x`-attempt or empty id is `invalid`. Per identifier: `input`, `kind` (anon\|domain\|invalid), `canonical`, `changed` (canonical != input), `submit_tx_ok` (the chain's `submit_tx` anon strict gate would admit it as-is — it REJECTS a non-canonical anon `from` rather than rewriting it, keeping the signature bound; always true for a domain), and `pubkey_hex` (anon only — the 64-hex Ed25519 pubkey the address decodes to). `--address` repeatable; `--addresses` takes a comma list or `@<path>` (one per line, blank + `#` lines skipped); both combine, order preserved. `--json` (auto for >1 id) emits `{count, results:[...], summary:{anon,domain,invalid,changed,submit_tx_ok}}`. Pure local string work; no SHA-256, no RPC, no daemon (only reads an `@file` when given). Use cases: screen a payroll/airdrop recipient list for the strict gate before signing; canonicalize user-pasted addresses for a UI. Exit 0 all classified (anon/domain), 1 args/IO/parse error, 2 at least one identifier invalid. |

### Recovery flows

| Command | Purpose |
|---|---|
| `determ-wallet create-recovery --seed <hex> --password <str> -t T -n N --out <file> [--scheme {passphrase\|opaque}]` | Persist a T-of-N recovery setup as a single JSON document. Scheme `passphrase` (default) uses PBKDF2 directly off the password; scheme `opaque` routes through the OPAQUE adapter. |
| `determ-wallet recover --in <file> --password <str> [--guardians <i,j,k,...>]` | Reconstruct the seed from ≥ T envelopes. Scheme is auto-detected from the setup. Optional pubkey checksum gate prevents silent corruption. |

### OPAQUE primitives (diagnostic)

| Command | Purpose |
|---|---|
| `determ-wallet oprf-smoke` | Smoke-test libsodium primitives (ristretto255 scalar/point ops + Argon2id). Outputs sample scalars + a blinded point + a stretched key. |
| `determ-wallet opaque-handshake --mode {register\|authenticate} --password <str> --guardian-id <0..255> [--record <hex>]` | Exercise the OPAQUE adapter directly. Currently the **development stub** adapter; the real `libopaque` integration is tracked as **v2.14** (real OPAQUE wallet recovery) in `docs/V2-DESIGN.md`. See `wallet/PHASE6_PORTING_NOTES.md` for the MSVC porting status that gates the v2.14 ship. |
| `determ-wallet version` | Print version banner including current adapter suite name. |

### Adapter status check

The wallet's `is_stub()` flag exposes whether the linked OPAQUE adapter is the development stub or the real `libopaque` implementation (v2.14). The stub is offline-grindable against a compromised guardian — see `docs/proofs/WalletRecovery.md` (FA12) for the concrete-security bounds. The v2.14 ship replaces the stub with the real construction; once that lands, this `is_stub()` returns `false` for production builds. The wallet binary's `version` command surfaces the active suite tag.

## Exit codes

- `0` — success
- `1` — parsing error, missing argument, RPC failure, or assertion failure
- `2` — cryptographic failure (AEAD tag mismatch, OPAQUE authentication rejected, recovery reconstruction failed)

## Operator analytical scripts (tools/operator_*.sh)

Lightweight bash wrappers that compose multiple `determ` CLI/RPC calls into single-purpose operator diagnostic workflows. All are read-only (RPC only), require a daemon already listening on the supplied `--rpc-port` (default `7778`), source `tools/common.sh` for the platform-detected binary path, and accept `--help` for inline usage. Distinct from `tools/test_*.sh` (regression tests with embedded fixtures + assertions): operator scripts target a live production/staging daemon and emit a 1-line digest plus a meaningful exit code suitable for monitoring-system alert gates.

| Script | Purpose |
|---|---|
| `tools/operator_supply_check.sh [--rpc-port N] [--verbose]` | Verifies the A1 unitary-supply invariant on a running daemon. Calls `determ supply --json` and inspects `a1_invariant_ok`. Default mode emits a 1-line summary (`A1 OK (live=… expected=…, port N)` or `A1 VIOLATED (…)`); `--verbose` additionally prints the full supply JSON envelope. JSON parsing prefers `jq`; falls back to `grep`/`sed` when `jq` is unavailable. **Exit codes**: 0 invariant holds, 2 invariant VIOLATED (operator alert gate), 1 RPC error / malformed response. |
| `tools/operator_chain_health.sh [--rpc-port N] [--json]` | Multi-RPC "health digest" — checks (a) daemon responding via `determ head --json`, (b) A1 invariant via `determ supply --json` (tolerates supply exit 2 — that's a red flag, not an RPC error), (c) at least 1 peer via `determ peers --count`. Default human output prints `[OK]`/`[X] ` marks per check plus height/head_hash/peer count; `--json` emits a single-line `{daemon_responding, a1_invariant_ok, peers_ok, height, head_hash, peer_count, rpc_port}` envelope. **Exit codes**: 0 all green, 2 any red (operator alert gate), 1 RPC error. |
| `tools/operator_fork_watch.sh --node-a host:port --node-b host:port [--window N] [--field NAME]` | Cross-node fork detection wrapper around `determ check-fork`. Resolves each node's current head independently via `determ head --field height`, picks the smaller as the window's upper bound, computes `from = max(0, head - window + 1)` (default `--window 10`), then invokes `check-fork` on the resulting range comparing `--field` (default `state_root`; other allowed values: `block_hash`, `prev_hash`, `index`, `timestamp`). On divergence, re-queries with `--json` to extract the exact divergence height for the diagnostic. **Exit codes**: 0 nodes in sync over the window (1-line `divergence=NONE` summary), 2 fork detected at height H (1-line `divergence=AT H` summary, operator alert gate), 1 RPC error / unreachable node / bad args. |
| `tools/operator_light_anchor_audit.sh --genesis <file> [--state <path>]…` | **OFFLINE** read-only persisted-anchor fleet audit (no daemon) for the `determ-light verify-chain --persist` cache. For each `--state <path>` (repeatable; defaults to the determ-light default cache when none given) it runs `determ-light state --show` then `state --verify-anchor --genesis <file>` and classifies the target: **ABSENT** (no cache — informational, never a failure), **VALID+PINNED** (`--show` ok AND `--verify-anchor` PASS — the anchor is for this chain), **VALID+WRONG-CHAIN** (`--show` ok but `--verify-anchor` MISMATCH exit 2 — a stale/wrong-chain cache), **CORRUPT** (`--show` exit 1). Prints a per-target line + a fleet summary. Composes the LSP-1/LSP-2 gates (`docs/proofs/LightStatePersistenceSoundness.md`, spec `tla/LightStatePersistence.tla` FB57) into an operator pre-flight — "is every cached anchor present, valid, and pinned to MY chain before a resume trusts it?". SKIPs (exit 0) when determ-light is absent; `--help` works with no binary. **Exit codes**: 0 every present anchor VALID+PINNED (absent informational), 1 any CORRUPT / VALID+WRONG-CHAIN / usage error. |
| `tools/operator_anchor_audit.sh [--state <path>] [--genesis <file>] [--rpc-port <N>]` | Single-target **DEPTH** audit of the determ-light persisted anchor cache — the companion of `operator_light_anchor_audit.sh` (the OFFLINE multi-target fleet classifier above): breadth there, depth + live cross-check here. Parses the state JSON **independently of the binary** (works with no determ-light built): file exists + valid JSON, `schema_version` matches `light/persist.cpp`, 64-hex `genesis_hash`/`head_block_hash`, numeric `head_height`; with `--genesis`, the LSP-2 re-pin via `determ-light state --verify-anchor`; with `--rpc-port`, the **live monotonicity cross-check** — the operator-side view of the LSP-7 `anchored_head` gate: the daemon's current head must be ≥ the cached committee-verified height, else `bad: daemon head regressed below verified anchor (stale/truncated state)`; plus a 7-day mtime staleness warning (warn, never fail). **Exit codes**: 0 all ok (warns allowed), 1 any bad finding / usage error, 2 no cache / missing prerequisite (audit incomplete; bad findings dominate). |
| `tools/operator_light_freshness_probe.sh --rpc-port <N> [--interval <secs>] [--probes <count>] [--min-advance <blocks>]` | Operationalizes the **F-1 "stale-but-attested head"** limitation (`docs/proofs/LightClientThreatModel.md` §5 — per-invocation undetectable: a daemon consistently serving an old-but-committee-attested head makes every individual read sound yet stale). Samples the daemon's head height `--probes` times (default 2) at `--interval` seconds (default 10) and **FAILS unless the head advanced by `--min-advance`** (default 1) across the window — a stalled chain or stale/eclipsed daemon surfaces as `daemon head is NOT advancing`. Fail-fast (exit 2, clear message) when the binary is absent or the daemon unreachable on the first probe. **Exit codes**: 0 advancing, 1 not advancing (operator alert gate), 2 prerequisites missing. |
| `tools/operator_light_fleet_crosscheck.sh --genesis <file> (--rpc-port N \| --peer host:port) ×2+ [--json]` | Read-only monitoring wrapper around `determ-light cross-check` (the multi-peer divergence detector). Validates the ≥2-peer + `--genesis` usage locally (exit 1 before invoking), runs `cross-check` over the endpoint set, collapses the result to a single monitoring-friendly line `CROSSCHECK <verdict> peers=<n> genesis=<short>`, and PASSES THROUGH the determ-light exit code verbatim so a cron/monitor can gate on it; `--json` forwards the verified JSON. Soundness `docs/proofs/MultiPeerCrossCheckSoundness.md` (MPC-1..MPC-5) + spec `tla/MultiPeerCrossCheck.tla` FB58. The live AGREE/DIVERGENCE/INCONCLUSIVE path is cluster-bound (needs ≥2 reachable daemons); SKIPs (exit 0) when determ-light is absent; `--help` works with no binary. **Exit codes** (passthrough from `cross-check`): 0 AGREE, 2 DIVERGENCE, 3 INCONCLUSIVE, 1 UNVERIFIABLE / usage error. |
| `tools/operator_light_sync_loop.sh --rpc-port <N> --genesis <file> [--state <path>] [--cycles <K>] [--interval <secs>]` | Steady-state operator sync loop wrapping `determ-light verify-chain --resume --persist` (the LSP-6 resume-then-advance loop). Runs a **bounded** (non-infinite, cron/CI-safe) `--cycles K` loop (default 3): cycle 1 is a full from-genesis verify (no anchor yet), each later cycle resumes from + advances the persisted anchor; prints a one-line `cycle i: height=… verdict=OK/RESUMED/FAIL` status per cycle, sleeps `--interval` (default 0) between cycles, and **exits non-zero on the FIRST failing cycle** (a fork-below-anchor or verify error — stops, does not loop past a hard error). Composes the persistence + resume features into an operator monitor for a long-lived light client. Args validated before the binary is invoked (deterministic offline contract); the live verify loop is cluster-bound; SKIPs (exit 0) when determ-light is absent; `--help` works with no binary. **Exit codes**: 0 all cycles OK, 1 first failing cycle (fork/verify error) / usage error. |
| `tools/operator_stake_audit.sh [--rpc-port N] [--json] [--anomalies-only] [--threshold N]` | Comprehensive stake-position audit. Enumerates validators via `determ stakes --json`, then fetches per-domain detail via `determ stake_info <domain>` to recover `locked` + `unlock_height` (the `stakes` RPC returns the active-validator shape, not the locked-state shape — the script bridges the two). Flags anomalies: `unlock_height_past` (unlock_height ≤ current_height but still in stakes map), `below_threshold` (locked < `--threshold`), `zero_locked` (post-slash zombie entry). Default human output is a sorted table + summary footer; `--json` emits `{stakers: [...], summary: {total_stakers, total_locked, locked_count, unlocking_count, anomaly_count}}`. **Exit codes**: 0 (or 2 only when `--anomalies-only` AND anomalies present — design choice documented in script header), 1 RPC error. |
| `tools/operator_dapp_audit.sh [--rpc-port N] [--json] [--active-only\|--inactive-only] [--prefix STR] [--topic STR]` | DApp-registry audit. Enumerates DApps via `determ dapp-list --json` then fans out to `determ dapp-info --domain D` per entry to recover full `registered_at` + `inactive_from` (the `dapp-list` RPC returns compact entries without these fields). Computes status: ACTIVE (`inactive_from == UINT64_MAX`), DEACTIVATING (`UINT64_MAX > inactive_from > current_height`, DAPP_GRACE_BLOCKS pending), INACTIVE (`inactive_from ≤ current_height`). UINT64_MAX comparison uses string equality FIRST to avoid bash int-overflow on the sentinel literal. Default human table + summary footer; `--json` emits `{dapps: [...], summary: {total, active, deactivating, inactive, oldest_height, newest_height, current_height}}`. Tolerates dapp-info race-deregister silently. **Exit codes**: 0 success (zero DApps is success), 1 RPC error. |
| `tools/operator_equivocation_digest.sh [--rpc-port N] [--json] [--from H] [--to H] [--by-offender]` | FA6 equivocation-event aggregator. Scans block headers via `determ block-range --json` (which retains `equivocation_events` per `node.cpp` headers RPC; `chain_summary` strips this field, so the script uses `block-range` instead). Default window: last 1000 blocks; `--from H --to H` overrides. Aggregates per offender_domain on `--by-offender`. Disambiguates `containing_block_index` (block carrying the evidence) from `height` (offense block) since they can differ by many heights. Per-event `slashed_amount` is reported as 0 because EquivocationEvent doesn't carry it in JSON — the actual slash amount is reflected in the chain's `accumulated_slashed` delta; footer note points operators there. **Exit codes**: 0 success (zero equivocations is also success), 1 RPC error. |
| `tools/operator_genesis_inspect.sh [<genesis.json>]` | **R42** — read-only human-readable summary of a local genesis file: chain_id, chain_role, sharding_mode + shard config, M/K committee, timing profile, supply params (genesis_total / subsidy / pools), and v2 activation heights. Delegates to the shipped parser (`determ verify-genesis --in <f> --json`) and augments with a raw-JSON pass for fields the parser does not surface. Local-file tool — no RPC, no cluster, no mutation. Prints a usage/notice and exits cleanly when no genesis file is supplied. |
| `tools/operator_config_lint.sh [<config.json>]` | **R42** — read-only node-config linter. WARNs on risky/permissive production settings (RPC auth disabled / missing auth secret, `log_quiet` off, rate-limiting disabled, permissive bind address, unencrypted keyfiles, …) checked against the **real** `Config` field names (grepped from the config struct, not invented). Advisory: prints a per-finding `WARN:` list + a finding count for operator review; never mutates; not a hard gate. |
| `tools/operator_keyfile_audit.sh [<keyfile>] [--json]` | **R43** — read-only keyfile security-posture auditor. Reports whether a keyfile is ENCRYPTED (passphrase envelope) or PLAINTEXT, the KDF + params + cipher if encrypted, and the address — delegating to `determ-wallet keyfile-info` plus a read-only JSON augment. WARNs on a plaintext (unencrypted) private key at rest. No mutation, no cluster; advisory exit when no keyfile is given. |
| `tools/operator_genesis_diff.sh [<genesis-a.json> <genesis-b.json>]` | **R43** — read-only field-by-field diff of the consensus-critical genesis parameters (chain_id, chain_role, sharding_mode, shard config, m_creators/k_block_sigs, timing, subsidy, v2 activation heights) between two genesis files. Catches fleet config drift / a mismatched genesis before it causes a genesis-hash mismatch. Parses via the shipped `determ verify-genesis --json` + raw read; prints only differing fields + a SAME/DIFFER verdict. Sibling of `operator_genesis_inspect.sh`. |
| `tools/operator_slashing_ledger.sh [--rpc-port N] [--json] [--from H] [--to H] [--by-offender]` | Slashing-forensics ledger (F4 R40) — the consolidated slashing-event view that joins the FA6 equivocation stream + the FA5 Round-1 abort-slash stream into a single per-offender forensic record, cross-checked against the A1 unitary-supply accounting. Walks the block range (default last 1000 blocks; `--from/--to` overrides) via `determ block-range --json`, partitioning every slash-bearing event (`EquivocationEvent` per FA-Apply-10, Round-1 `AbortEvent` per FA-Apply-11) by offender domain, and reconciles the summed per-event effect against the chain's `accumulated_slashed` delta over the window (the apply-layer A1-invariance cross-check per FA-Apply-10 T-E5 + FA-Apply-11 T-A4). Includes the **A1 identity gate**: confirms the live supply invariant holds (`determ supply --json` `a1_invariant_ok`) so a forensic read is never taken against a daemon already in supply violation — **exit 2 on A1 violation** (operator alert gate), distinguishing a genuine accounting break from ordinary slashing activity. `--by-offender` aggregates per offender_domain; `--json` for monitoring ingestion. Sibling of `operator_supply_check.sh` (A1-invariant-only) + `operator_equivocation_digest.sh` (FA6-equivocation-only) — `operator_slashing_ledger.sh` is the joint forensic + A1-gated view across both slash streams. Exercised by `tools/test_operator_slashing_ledger.sh`. **Exit codes**: 0 healthy ledger (slashing activity is not itself an alert), 2 A1 invariant VIOLATED (operator alert gate), 1 RPC error / unreachable daemon / bad args. |
| `tools/operator_liveness_posture.sh --genesis <gen.json> [--config <config.json>] [--json]` | **OFFLINE S-044/S-045 liveness-posture audit** (no RPC, no daemon, read-only). Reads the genesis (and optionally a node config.json — config keys override genesis where present, mirroring `check_if_selected` reading `cfg_`), computes the committee/abort arithmetic the findings derive from — K, M, claim quorum `q = K−1`, `k_bft = ⌈2K/3⌉`, single-abort margin `M−K`, escalation headroom `M−k_bft`, the minimum distinct-exclusion count that wedges (`M−K+1`) — and emits a tiered verdict: **CRITICAL EXPOSURE (S-044)** at K=2 (single-claim abort quorum → permanent wedge under ordinary timing skew; the shipped `web` init-default profile lands here; deploy K ≥ 3), **WARNING (S-045)** at K ≥ 3 with escalation headroom < 2 (two distinct straggles at one height = permanent halt; M=K=3 lands here — also flagged when `bft_enabled=false` makes escalation impossible outright), **OK** otherwise. `--json` emits all computed numbers + verdict + `exit_code` for fleet ingestion. Arithmetic pinned to `src/node/node.cpp::check_if_selected`; finding text in `docs/SECURITY.md` §S-044/§S-045; derivations in `docs/proofs/AbortCascadeLiveness.md` (FB67). **Exit codes**: 0 OK, 1 S-045 WARNING, 2 S-044 CRITICAL, 3 usage/file/parse error (deliberately distinct so a malformed genesis can never read as a healthy posture). |
| `tools/operator_suspension_watch.sh --rpc-port N [--suspended-only] [--json]` | Live FA6 abort-suspension registry forecast (Round 6, equivocation/slashing theme). Reconstructs which validators are CURRENTLY excluded from committee selection by the exponential-backoff abort-suspension cascade and until what height — the forward registry-eligibility view the daemon computes in `src/node/registry.cpp::build_from_chain` but never exposes. Reads only two cheap read RPCs (no block scan, no jq dependency): `determ status --field height` (current head) and `determ abort-records --json` (the S-032 abort_records cache), then mirrors the node's exact arithmetic byte-for-byte: `exp = min(count-1, MAX_ABORT_EXPONENT=10)`; `len = min(BASE_SUSPENSION_BLOCKS=10 * 2^exp, MAX_SUSPENSION_BLOCKS=10000)`; `suspended_until = last_block + len`; `suspended = head <= suspended_until` (constants per `include/determ/node/registry.hpp:19-21`). Classifies each abort-record domain as currently-SUSPENDED (with `blocks_remaining` + window-capped flag) or cooled-off (window elapsed → eligible again). `--suspended-only` row-prints only open windows and arms the alert gate; `--json` emits `{head, suspended:[...], cooled_off:[...], summary:{currently_suspended, cooled_off, total_with_aborts, constants}, rpc_port}`. Sibling of `operator_slashing_ledger.sh` (cumulative slashed counter + A1 reconciliation) and `operator_equivocation_digest.sh` (per-offender equivocation events) — this one is the unique forward registry-eligibility forecast (who is excluded NOW and for how long, the recoverable FA-Apply-11 abort path) rather than an event tally. **Exit codes**: 0 success (zero suspensions is also success), 2 `--suspended-only` AND >=1 domain currently suspended (operator alert gate), 1 RPC error / unreachable daemon / malformed response / bad args. |
| `tools/operator_supply_reconcile.sh [--rpc-port N] [--peer-ports P1,P2,…] [--json]` | Read-only **A1 supply-identity reconciliation** (R41 H4) — the reconciliation superset of `operator_supply_check.sh` (bare per-shard pass/fail). Single `--rpc-port` mode reconciles one shard's ledger (`live == genesis + subsidy + inbound − slashed − outbound`, using the server-stamped `a1_invariant_ok`); `--peer-ports` mode sums the six supply legs across the reachable fleet and reconciles the chain-wide conservation law `Σ(live + slashed + outbound) == Σ(genesis + subsidy + inbound)`, surfacing the cross-shard in-flight residual `in_flight = Σoutbound − Σinbound` (must be ≥ 0). Reads only `determ supply --json` (the six legs + `expected_total` + `live_total_supply` + `a1_invariant_ok`) and `determ status --json` (shard_id / sharding_mode for fleet labelling) — no mutating endpoints. One Python pass with an 8s per-RPC timeout (cannot hang regardless of `--peer-ports` count); single query then exit (no `--watch`). `--json` envelope. Complements `operator_receipt_flow.sh` (receipt legs only) by reconciling all six legs. **Exit codes**: 0 healthy, 2 A1 violation (per-shard `a1_violation`, fleet `fleet_double_credit` when Σ_in > Σ_out, or `fleet_conservation_violation` — operator alert gate), 1 RPC / unreachable peer / duplicate shard_id / args error. Verified node-free (`--help` + arg-rejection smoke). |
| `tools/operator_param_history.sh [--rpc-port N] [--json] [--from H] [--to H] [--include-pending]` | Chronological A5 PARAM_CHANGE audit log. Iterates blocks in range, filters transactions where `type == 6` (or string "PARAM_CHANGE"), decodes the canonical payload via Python: `[u8 name_len][utf8 name][u16 LE value_len][value][u64 LE effective_height]…`. Computes status: ACTIVE (`effective_height ≤ current_height`), PENDING (`effective_height > current_height`). `--include-pending` merges entries from `determ pending-params --json` (which IS pre-parsed by the RPC, unlike landed PARAM_CHANGE txs). Best-effort u64-LE value decoding for known parameter names; hex fallback otherwise. **Exit codes**: 0 success, 1 RPC error / decode failure. |
| `tools/operator_committee_audit.sh [--rpc-port N] [--json] [--threshold N] [--anomalies-only]` | Consensus-committee audit. Queries the current K-of-K (or BFT-mode) committee via `determ committee --json`, recovers per-member region + active-stake state via `determ stakes --json` + `determ stake_info <domain>`. Reports committee size K, member set, BFT/MD quorum arithmetic (`bft_required = ceil(2K/3)`, `md_required = K`), and regional distribution (members-per-region). Flags anomalies: `committee_below_threshold` (K < `--threshold`, default 3); `member_not_in_active_stakes` (committee includes a domain absent from the active-stake set — invariant violation worth alerting on); `regional_concentration` (one region holds > 50% of the committee — under-quorum-merge risk per FA8 R7). `--anomalies-only` suppresses healthy-state output; pair with `--json` for monitoring-system ingestion. Default human output is a sorted-by-domain table with status flags + summary footer; `--json` emits `{committee: [...], summary: {size, bft_required, md_required, regions: {...}, anomalies: [...]}}`. **Exit codes**: 0 healthy committee (or 0 when `--anomalies-only` AND no anomalies), 2 anomaly present (operator alert gate), 1 RPC error / unreachable daemon. |
| `tools/operator_constants_audit.sh --rpc-port N --genesis <file> --expected <file.json> [--light <path>] [--wait <seconds>] [--json]` | Trust-minimized **governance-parameter audit** — the only operator script that drives the `determ-light` trust-minimized reader (`verify-constant`) rather than the daemon's own RPC, so it proves what consensus/economic parameters the chain ACTUALLY commits (committee-signed `k:` leaves) rather than what the daemon's config/logs claim. Loops `verify-constant` over the constants named in `--expected` (a flat JSON object `{name: value}`; u64 constants take a number, `shard_salt` a 64-hex string; only the names present are audited, validated against the canonical 13 = 12 u64 + `shard_salt`, unknown names → usage error). Each row reports CONFIRMED / MISMATCH / UNVERIFIABLE (mapping `verify-constant`'s exit 0/2/3) and flags the three **governance-mutable** constants (`min_stake`, `suspension_slash`, `unstake_delay` — `PARAM_CHANGE` can change them post-genesis, so a MISMATCH there may be legitimate; cross-check via `verify-param-change` / `pending-params`). Resolves the light binary via `--light` / `$DETERM_LIGHT` / `build/Release/determ-light.exe`. `--json` emits `{audit, passed, mismatched, unverifiable, rows:[{name, verdict, expected, governance_mutable}]}`. The trust-minimized complement to config inspection; soundness inherited from `docs/proofs/ConstantProofSoundness.md` (CP-1..CP-4). **Exit codes**: 0 all CONFIRMED, 2 any MISMATCH (note: governance-mutable mismatches may be legitimate), 3 any UNVERIFIABLE (and no mismatch), 1 args / genesis / light-binary / setup error. |
| `tools/operator_committee_snapshot.sh --rpc-port N [--height H] [--json]` | Single-height committee composition forensic snapshot (R39+1 A4). Answers "at THIS block H, who are the K creators, with what pubkeys, which signed, and is the composition internally consistent?" — distinct from `operator_committee_audit.sh` (stake-proportional fairness OVER A WINDOW) and `operator_committee_membership_history.sh` (per-validator timeline). Queries the block at `--height H` (default: chain head - 1, the highest finalized block) via `determ block-info --json`, reads the K creators + `creator_block_sigs` parallel arrays, recovers per-creator pubkey via `determ validators --json` cross-lookup, computes the required-sigs gate (K-of-K = K in mutual-distrust mode, ceil(2K/3) in BFT mode), and counts observed sig presence. Reports: committee size K, consensus_mode (mutual_distrust / bft), bft_mode_enabled flag, required_sigs, observed_sigs, per-creator (domain, short pubkey, sig_present yes/no), partner_subset_hash (hex if R4 Phase 3 region-pinned selection was in effect, otherwise absent), and a duplicate_check pass/FAIL (a domain appearing more than once in `creators[]` is an invariant violation worth alerting on). Default human output is a structured table per the comment block in the script header; `--json` emits `{height, consensus_mode, bft_mode_enabled, committee_size, required_sigs, observed_sigs, creators: [{domain, pubkey, sig_present}, …], partner_subset_hash, duplicate_check}`. Use cases: operator-suspected committee misconfiguration drilldown ("what changed at block H?"), R4 Phase 3 partner_subset_hash spot-check, K-of-K-vs-BFT-mode parity verification against the observed `consensus_mode` field. | `tools/operator_inbound_reconciliation_audit.sh [--rpc-port N] [--f2-activation-height N] [--from H] [--to H] [--anomalies-only] [--json]` | Read-only v2.7 F2 / S-016 inbound-receipt reconciliation health audit. Probes `status` (shard_id + sharding_mode; single-shard `none` short-circuits to one INFO line, exit 0) and `head` (height — the `head` CLI reads it from the same `status` RPC), then walks a window of finalized blocks (default last 1000; `--from/--to` override) via `determ block-info <h> --json`, reporting per-block `inbound_receipts` admission counts. Because the genesis-pinned activation height `v2_7_f2_active_from_height` is not exposed by any RPC (it lives in `GenesisConfig` and is installed via `chain_.set_f2_active_from_height`), the operator supplies it with `--f2-activation-height N` (read from genesis.json) — mirroring how `operator_stake_audit.sh` bridges un-exposed locked-stake state. When supplied, each admitting block is classified F2-active (`idx ≥ H`, where inbound is reconciled via the committee-view INTERSECTION per `producer.cpp::build_body` + `validator.cpp::check_inbound_receipts`) vs pre-F2, and any below-activation admission raises the `below_activation_admission` anomaly (a config / genesis-pin drift signal, not a consensus violation). `--json` emits `{my_shard_id, sharding_mode, head_height, f2_activation_height, window:{…}, totals:{blocks_with_inbound, inbound_receipt_count, f2_active_admissions, pre_f2_admissions, below_activation_block_count}, blocks:[…], anomalies, rpc_port}`. | `tools/operator_genesis_verify_live.sh --genesis <file> [--rpc-port N] [--json] [--verbose]` | Live-daemon genesis cross-check. Computes the daemon's chain-id via `determ chain-id` on the running daemon (RPC), then computes the standalone-CLI genesis hash via `determ verify-genesis --in <file> --json` against the supplied file, and compares the two values byte-for-byte. Used to detect genesis-drift between a running operator daemon and an expected genesis artifact (rolling-upgrade verification, post-snapshot-bootstrap cross-check, multi-region operator coordination). `--verbose` prints both hashes + the file path + the daemon-side chain spec; default output is a 1-line `genesis_match=YES (hash=…)` or `genesis_match=NO (daemon=… file=…)` digest. `--json` emits `{match, daemon_hash, file_hash, genesis_file, rpc_port}`. **Exit codes**: 0 match, 2 mismatch (operator alert gate — daemon is on a different genesis than the expected file), 1 RPC error / file missing / `verify-genesis` failure / bad args. |
| `tools/operator_subsidy_audit.sh [--rpc-port N] [--json] [--from H] [--to H] [--anomalies-only]` | E1/E3/E4 subsidy-distribution concentration audit. Iterates blocks in `[from, to]` (default: last 100 blocks via `head - 99 .. head`), pulls per-block creator + reward data via `determ block-info --json`, aggregates `total_subsidy_minted` per creator across the window. | `tools/operator_snapshot_check.sh --in <file> [--rpc-port N] [--offline] [--state-root <hex64>] [--json]` | Snapshot integrity + daemon-state cross-check. Validates a snapshot artifact via `determ snapshot inspect --in <file> --json` (parses every field via the same path used at restore time — head_index / head_hash / state_root + all serialize_state collection fields), and (default mode) compares the snapshot's tail `head_index` + `head_hash` against the running daemon's current `head` via `determ head --json` for divergence detection. Anomaly classification: snapshot AT daemon's current height with `head_hash` mismatch is a hard fork (exit 2); snapshot AHEAD of daemon's height — i.e. snapshot's `head_index > daemon.head_index` — is exit 2 (operator could mis-bootstrap a daemon onto an artifact from a future fork); snapshot BEHIND daemon by ≥ 1 block is exit 0 (normal — operator is auditing an older artifact). `--offline` skips the daemon cross-check (snapshot-integrity-only mode — useful for cold artifacts on a separate host). `--state-root <hex64>` invokes externally-anchored verification: the snapshot's tail head's `state_root` must equal the supplied hex (the S-033 anchor — operator can pin via an out-of-band attestation from a sibling validator), exits 2 on mismatch. Default human output is a per-check pass/fail line + summary `snapshot_ok=YES (head=H hash=… state_root=…)` or `snapshot_ok=NO (reason=…)`; `--json` emits `{snapshot_ok, head_index, head_hash, state_root, daemon_head_index, daemon_head_hash, divergence, mode: {offline\|live\|anchored}, rpc_port}`. **Exit codes**: 0 snapshot valid + (where applicable) daemon-consistent, 2 fork-at-height / ahead-of-daemon / state_root-anchor-mismatch (operator alert gate — do not restore from this artifact), 1 missing/unreadable snapshot file / RPC error / bad args. |
| `tools/operator_chain_verify.sh [--rpc-port N] [--from H --to H \| --last N] [--genesis-hash <hex64>] [--json]` | Full-chain `prev_hash` integrity walker. Iterates blocks in the configured range (default: `0..TIP` — `--help` prints a clear cost warning that on a long chain this is O(N) RPC calls; `--last N` covers the spot-check case; `--from H --to H` covers ad-hoc audits) pulling each block's `compute_hash` + `prev_hash` via `determ block-info --json`, then asserts per-block invariants: (a) each non-genesis block's `prev_hash` equals the immediately-prior block's `compute_hash` (the chain-integrity contract that `Chain::load` enforces at startup via S-021); (b) block indices are strictly sequential (no gaps, no duplicates); (c) block 0 satisfies the genesis sentinel (`prev_hash == 32-zero-bytes` per `make_genesis_block`); (d) optionally, with `--genesis-hash <hex64>`, the chain-identity anchor: block 0's `compute_hash` matches the supplied hex (the operator-known canonical genesis hash for the deployment — defeats genesis-drift between operators running the "same" chain_id with different `m_creators` / `k_block_sigs` / etc per S-039). Reports any failed invariant with the offending block index + expected/actual hashes. Default human output is a final-status digest `chain_intact=YES (blocks=N)` or `chain_intact=NO (broken_at=H reason=…)`; `--json` emits `{chain_intact, block_count, from, to, broken_at, reason, genesis_hash_match, mode: {full\|range\|last-N\|anchored}}`. **Exit codes**: 0 chain intact across the audited range, 2 `prev_hash` mismatch / sequencing gap / genesis-sentinel failure / genesis-hash anchor mismatch (operator alert gate — chain file has been tampered with or operators are on divergent chains), 1 RPC error / unreachable daemon / bad args. |
| `tools/operator_account_growth.sh [--rpc-port N] [--json] [--from H] [--to H] [--anomalies-only]` | Account-set growth-metric tracker over a block window. Iterates blocks in `[from, to]` (default: last 1000 blocks via `head - 999 .. head`), queries the chain's account count at the window's start and end (via `determ chain-summary --json` or per-block introspection), computes the new-account delta per block, identifies the peak-growth block within the window, and attributes the growth by source (TRANSFER credit causing account auto-creation, inbound CrossShardReceipt admission, REGISTER, DEREGISTER per AccountStateInvariants invariant I-4 paths). Reports per-block delta sparkline (text histogram), peak block + count, by-source attribution percentages, and start-vs-end totals. Flags anomalies: `spike_in_block` (>50 new accounts in any single block — Sybil bulk-register signal), `growth_unbounded` (>100% growth across the entire window — sustained spam pressure). `--anomalies-only` suppresses healthy-state rows. Default human output is a per-block delta table + by-source breakdown + summary footer (start, end, delta, peak, peak-block); `--json` emits `{window: {from,to}, per_block_delta: [...], by_source: {transfer_credit, inbound_receipt, register, deregister}, summary: {start_count, end_count, total_delta, peak_block, peak_count, growth_pct}, anomalies: [...]}`. **Exit codes**: 0 healthy growth (or 0 when `--anomalies-only` AND no anomalies), 2 spike OR unbounded-growth anomaly (operator alert gate), 1 RPC error / decode failure / bad args. |
| `tools/operator_block_lag_check.sh [--rpc-port N] [--profile {cluster\|web\|regional\|global\|tactical}] [--threshold N] [--json]` | Liveness-gate operator script — detects when a running daemon's head has fallen stale relative to wall-clock. Reads `head.timestamp` via `determ head --json`, compares against `now()` (Unix epoch seconds), and compares the difference to a per-profile threshold (or an explicit `--threshold N` override). Per-profile defaults: `cluster=60s`, `web=300s`, `regional=600s`, `global=1800s`, `tactical=60s` (mirrors the params.hpp timing-profile tier names — see PROTOCOL.md §12.3 + README §13.1 profile tables for round-timer alignment; the lag threshold is a small multiple of the profile's expected block period). Reports current head height + head timestamp + wall-clock + computed lag + active threshold + peer count (for context: stale head with 0 peers is a network-isolation diagnosis, stale head with N peers is a chain-stall diagnosis). `--profile` without `--threshold` picks the default; `--threshold N` overrides any profile default; supplying neither defaults to the `regional` profile (600s). Default human output is a 1-line `head_fresh=YES (lag=Xs threshold=Ys peers=N)` or `head_fresh=NO (lag=Xs > threshold=Ys peers=N)` digest; `--json` emits `{fresh, lag_seconds, threshold_seconds, head_height, head_timestamp, wall_clock, peer_count, profile, rpc_port}`. **Exit codes**: 0 fresh (lag ≤ threshold), 2 stale (lag > threshold — operator alert gate; pair with `--threshold` in monitoring to escalate at custom thresholds), 1 RPC error / unreachable daemon / bad args. |
| `tools/operator_shard_diagnostic.sh [--rpc-port N] [--sample N] [--addresses <file>] [--genesis <file>] [--json] [--include-this-shard] [--anomalies-only]` | Multi-shard routing diagnostic. Reads `shard_count`, `my_shard_id`, and `shard_address_salt` from the running daemon (RPC) or from `--genesis <file>` when offline; samples `N` anon-addresses (default 100) — either from `--addresses <file>` (one per line) or generated freshly — then routes each through `shard_id_for_address(addr, salt, shard_count)` to compute the per-target-shard distribution. Reports the per-shard count, expected uniform count (`sample_size / shard_count`), and per-shard delta from uniform; flags anomalies: `salt_bias` (any shard ≥ 2× expected count — salt-bias signal worth a salt-rotation review), `empty_shard` (any shard with zero samples — extreme bias OR shard_count > sample_size). `--include-this-shard` highlights `my_shard_id` in the output table for cross-shard-flow context. `--anomalies-only` suppresses healthy-state rows. Default human output is a per-shard table + summary footer (sample size, my_shard_id, shard_count, salt, anomaly count); `--json` emits `{shard_count, my_shard_id, salt, sample_size, per_shard: [{shard_id, count, expected, delta_pct}, …], anomalies: [...]}`. **Exit codes**: 0 healthy distribution (or 0 when `--anomalies-only` AND no anomalies), 2 salt_bias OR empty_shard anomaly (operator alert gate), 1 RPC error / bad genesis file / missing args. |
| `tools/operator_mempool_diagnostic.sh [--rpc-port N] [--json] [--anomalies-only]` | Mempool-state diagnostic. Reports pending-tx count against the S-008 bound, per-type and per-sender breakdowns, mempool-pressure percentage (`pending / bound`), and flags anomalies: `pressure_high` (mempool > 80% of S-008 bound — sustained submission pressure worth alerting on), `sender_concentration` (any single sender > 30% of pending — Sybil-submission signal). **Forward-staged for v2.x mempool RPC**: mempool RPC is not currently exposed on the v1.x daemon (the script verifies presence via a tolerant RPC call and exits 1 with a clear diagnostic on the current daemon). The script ships now so it can be wired into v2.x once mempool RPC lands without further operator-tooling churn. Default human output is a 1-line summary plus a per-type + per-sender breakdown when present; `--json` emits `{pending, bound, pressure_pct, by_type: {...}, by_sender: [...], anomalies: [...], available}`. `--anomalies-only` suppresses healthy-state rows. **Exit codes**: 0 healthy (or 0 when `--anomalies-only` AND no anomalies), 2 pressure_high OR sender_concentration anomaly (operator alert gate), 1 mempool RPC unavailable / RPC error / bad args. |
| `tools/operator_config_audit.sh --config <file> [--json]` | Static configuration audit. Reads a local `config.json` (default `$HOME/.determ/config.json`; `--config <file>` overrides) and audits it against security best-practices. Checks: S-001 (`rpc_localhost_only` enabled — otherwise CRITICAL on a multi-tenant host), S-014 (rate-limit values nonzero on RPC + gossip), BFT enabled (`bft_enabled = true` for production deployments), K-of-K committee size strong (`m_creators ≥ 3` — K=1 / K=2 are degenerate), genesis path + key path existence on the filesystem, RPC + P2P port distinctness (port collision = silent failure-to-bind), and profile timing sanity (`round_phase1_ms`/`round_phase2_ms`/`round_bft_ms` within the profile's expected range — catches operator drift from the params.hpp tier defaults documented in PROTOCOL.md §12.3 + README §13.1). Each finding is classified CRITICAL (operator alert gate — exit 2), WARN, or INFO. Default human output is a per-check pass/fail line plus a summary footer (`config_secure=YES (checks=N pass=K warn=W critical=C)` or `config_secure=NO (reason=…)`); `--json` emits `{config_file, findings: [{check_id, severity, status, detail}, …], summary: {pass, warn, critical}}`. Pure local computation — no daemon RPC required. **Exit codes**: 0 all-pass + no warnings (or all WARN-or-better), 2 CRITICAL finding (operator alert gate — block deployment until resolved), 1 missing/unreadable config file / bad args. |
| `tools/operator_governance_audit.sh [--rpc-port N] [--genesis <file>] [--json] [--anomalies-only]` | A5 PARAM_CHANGE governance-state audit on a running daemon. Pulls the live `pending-params` RPC + `head` (current height) and, optionally, the `--genesis <file>` keyholder set + threshold for keyholder-context display. Categorizes every pending change by activation timing relative to `current_height`: SOON (`effective_height - current_height ≤ 100`), MID (`100 < Δ ≤ 1000`), LONG (`Δ > 1000`). Flags anomalies: `conflicting_param` (two or more pending changes target the same parameter name with different values — operator must resolve before lower-bound activates), `activation_cluster` (3+ changes activating within a 10-block window — coordinated-mutation pattern worth review), and `unauthorized_attempt` (only when the optional `--genesis <file>` supplies the keyholder set — pending entries signed by a key not in the set indicate a stale-cache or pre-rotation artifact). `--anomalies-only` suppresses healthy-state rows; pair with `--json` for monitoring-system ingestion. Default human output is a sorted-by-effective_height table grouped by timing bucket + summary footer (total pending, per-bucket counts, anomaly count, keyholder threshold when known); `--json` emits `{pending_changes: [...], summary: {total, soon, mid, long, current_height, keyholder_threshold}, anomalies: [...]}`. **Exit codes**: 0 healthy governance (or 0 when `--anomalies-only` AND no anomalies), 2 anomaly present (operator alert gate — conflicting params / cluster pattern / unauthorized signer), 1 RPC error / unreachable daemon / bad genesis file / bad args. |
| `tools/operator_validator_history.sh [--rpc-port N] [--from H] [--to H] [--domain D \| --all] [--json] [--anomalies-only] [--sort-by {appearances\|participation\|slashed}]` | Per-validator behavior-history audit. Operates on a single domain (`--domain D`) or audits every validator in `determ stakes --json` (`--all`). Walks the block range (default: last 1000 blocks via `head - 999 .. head`; `--from H --to H` overrides) counting per-validator: committee appearances (block creators / BFT participants), signature participation rate (signed-vs-eligible — the per-validator analog of FA1 finalization-cascade integrity), abort events authored (R1 + R2), equivocation events offended (FA6 evidence count), and cumulative `accumulated_slashed` delta. Classifies each validator as ACTIVE (in current `stakes`), PENDING-UNLOCK (`unlock_height > 0` but not yet matured), or DEREGISTERED (absent from current `stakes` but appearing in historical blocks within the window). `--sort-by` selects the table ordering: `appearances` (default; sees-most-activity first), `participation` (lowest sig-rate first — surfaces underperforming validators), `slashed` (largest slash first — surfaces FA6-flagged offenders). Flags anomalies: `low_participation` (participation < 80% of appearances — silent-validator signal), `repeat_aborter` (≥3 R2-abort events in window — pattern worth review), `slashed_in_window` (any slash event — always anomalous). `--anomalies-only` suppresses healthy-state rows. Default human output is a per-validator table + summary footer (window range, total validators audited, anomaly count, sort key); `--json` emits `{window: {from,to}, validators: [{domain, appearances, sig_rate, aborts_r1, aborts_r2, equivocations, slashed_total, classification}, …], summary: {audited, active, pending_unlock, deregistered, anomalies: [...]}}`. **Exit codes**: 0 healthy history (or 0 when `--anomalies-only` AND no anomalies), 2 anomaly present (operator alert gate — low_participation / repeat_aborter / slashed_in_window), 1 RPC error / unreachable daemon / bad args. |
| `tools/operator_receipt_audit.sh [--rpc-port N] [--from H] [--to H] [--json] [--anomalies-only]` | Cross-shard CrossShardReceipt-flow audit over an `[from, to]` block window (default: last 1000 blocks via `head - 999 .. head`). Walks the range pulling outbound receipts (constructed in source-shard block bodies) + inbound receipts (admitted into destination-shard chain state per the v2.7 F2 admission gate + `inbound_receipts_eligible_for_inclusion` helper); aggregates per-shard source/destination breakdown (origin shard → target shard counts), per-block flow rate, and a defensive A1-delta consistency check (window-aggregated outbound debits + inbound credits must zero-out across the K-shard set — FA7 unitary-supply preservation under cross-shard composition). Verifies the dedup-set invariant: every inbound receipt's `(origin_shard, origin_block, receipt_hash)` triple appears exactly once in the destination shard's `applied_inbound_receipts` set across the window (no double-credit). Flags anomalies: `a1_delta_mismatch` (per-shard outbound-vs-inbound delta != 0 across the window — FA7 violation worth immediate alert), `dedup_collision` (any triple seen twice — direct double-credit attempt), `latency_excess` (inbound admission > `CROSS_SHARD_RECEIPT_LATENCY` blocks after outbound emission — clock-skew or stalled bridge), `inbound_without_origin` (an admitted inbound receipt has no matching outbound in the source shard — fabrication signal). **Single-shard deployments**: exits 0 immediately with INFO "no cross-shard activity by construction" (the script verifies `shard_count == 1` via `chain-summary` before doing any work; deployment topology is detected via RPC). Default human output is a per-shard-pair flow table + per-anomaly detail block + summary footer (window range, total inbound, total outbound, A1 delta, dedup-set size); `--json` emits `{window: {from,to}, shard_count, per_pair: [{src,dst,outbound,inbound,latency_avg}, …], summary: {total_outbound, total_inbound, a1_delta, dedup_set_size}, anomalies: [...]}`. `--anomalies-only` suppresses healthy-state rows. **Exit codes**: 0 healthy receipt flow (or 0 when `--anomalies-only` AND no anomalies; single-shard topology emits 0 + INFO), 2 anomaly present (operator alert gate — a1_delta_mismatch / dedup_collision / latency_excess / inbound_without_origin), 1 RPC error / unreachable daemon / bad args. |
| `tools/operator_consensus_latency.sh [--rpc-port N] [--from H] [--to H] [--profile {cluster\|web\|regional\|global\|tactical}] [--expected-ms N] [--json] [--anomalies-only]` | Consensus-pace operator script — samples block timestamps over an `[from, to]` window (default: last 100 blocks via `head - 99 .. head`) via `determ block-info --json`, computes inter-block delta times, and reports descriptive statistics (mean / median / p95 / p99 / max) compared against a per-profile expected block period. Per-profile defaults: `cluster=50ms`, `web=300ms` (default if neither `--profile` nor `--expected-ms`), `regional=600ms`, `global=2000ms`, `tactical=20ms` (mirrors the params.hpp timing-profile tier names — see PROTOCOL.md §12.3 + README §13.1 profile tables). `--expected-ms N` overrides any profile default. Flags anomalies: `p95_exceeds_2x` (95th percentile delta > 2× expected — sustained slow-block pressure), `stall_detected` (any single delta > 3000ms — chain-stall signal worth immediate alert), `non_monotonic_timestamp` (delta ≤ 0 — block-timestamp regression, V14 timestamp-monotonicity violation worth FA1-cascade review). `--anomalies-only` suppresses healthy-state rows. Default human output is a sorted statistics table + delta histogram + summary footer (window range, sample count, mean / median / p95 / p99 / max, expected, profile); `--json` emits `{window: {from,to}, sample_count, stats: {mean_ms, median_ms, p95_ms, p99_ms, max_ms}, expected_ms, profile, anomalies: [...]}`. **Exit codes**: 0 healthy pace (or 0 when `--anomalies-only` AND no anomalies), 2 anomaly present (operator alert gate — p95_exceeds_2x / stall_detected / non_monotonic_timestamp), 1 RPC error / unreachable daemon / bad args. |
| `tools/operator_anon_address_usage.sh [--rpc-port N] [--from H] [--to H] [--json] [--anomalies-only]` | Anon-address usage-pattern operator audit. Walks blocks in `[from, to]` (default: last 1000 blocks via `head - 999 .. head`), enumerates TRANSFER `from` / `to` fields per `determ block-info --json`, applies the canonical `is_anon_address` predicate per S-028 (`0x` prefix + 64 lowercase hex characters; case-normalized at admission), and aggregates: total anon-address sightings, distinct anon-address count, by-direction breakdown (anon→anon, anon→domain, domain→anon), top-20 anon senders by tx count + total amount routed, average amount per anon-sent tx. Flags anomalies: `single_anon_sender_high` (any single anon-address > 30% of in-window anon-sent txs — Sybil concentration signal), `anon_to_anon_ratio_high` (anon-to-anon TRANSFER ratio > 80% of total anon activity — privacy-shielding pattern worth review for mixing-service detection), `mass_creation_spike` (> 50 distinct anon-addresses first-seen within a single block — bulk-mint pattern worth Sybil-detection review). `--anomalies-only` suppresses healthy-state rows. | `tools/operator_genesis_dump.sh --in <file> [--full\|--compact\|--security-posture] [--json]` | Local-file genesis inspector — operator-facing complement to `determ verify-genesis` (which computes the canonical chain_id hash but does not pretty-print the genesis content). Reads a local genesis.json file; calls `determ verify-genesis --json` for the canonical chain_id + structural validation, then parses the raw file for fields not exposed via `verify-genesis` (e.g., `shard_address_salt`, per-keyholder pubkeys, full operator allocation set). Modes are mutually exclusive: `--full` (default) emits every section (chain_id, role, sharding_mode, m_creators / k_block_sigs / bft_enabled / bft_escalation_threshold consensus knobs, profile timing fields, subsidy + NEF + min_stake economic knobs, allocations table, keyholders + threshold, validator-set if present); `--compact` emits a single line (`chain_id=… role=… shard_count=N m_creators=K bft=on/off allocations=N keyholders=K-of-N`); `--security-posture` emits only the security-relevant subset (m_creators ≥ 3, bft_enabled = true, k_block_sigs sane, governance threshold non-trivial, shard_address_salt presence, min_stake non-zero) — useful for pre-deployment audits. `--json` emits the same shape as `--full` but as a JSON envelope. **No `--rpc-port` flag**: pure local-file analysis (operator can run this offline, against a candidate genesis before bringing up the daemon). Required `--in <file>`. **Exit codes**: 0 file parses successfully + (in `--security-posture` mode) posture is acceptable, 1 file unreadable / missing / malformed JSON / `verify-genesis` parse failure / bad args. |
| `tools/operator_orphan_check.sh [--rpc-port N] [--json] [--anomalies-only]` | Chain-state orphan-reference audit. Cross-checks the live `accounts`, `stakes`, and `registrants` maps for dangling cross-references that should never exist in a healthy chain. Classifies each finding by severity: **CRITICAL** — `stake_without_registrant` (an entry in `stakes` whose domain has no corresponding row in `registrants`; this is a structural invariant violation worth immediate alert because every stake is established via REGISTER which writes both maps atomically). **INFO** — `registrant_without_stake_or_balance` (a registrant row whose domain has neither a `stakes` entry nor a non-zero `accounts` balance — possible in DOMAIN_INCLUSION mode where validators have no stake by design), `deregistered_with_locked_stake` (a registrant in DEREGISTERED state with `locked > 0` but `current_height < unlock_height` — expected within the UNSTAKE_DELAY window; the script tags it INFO so operators can verify timing), `deregistered_past_unlock_height` (a registrant in DEREGISTERED state with `current_height ≥ unlock_height` and `locked > 0` — anomalous; UNSTAKE_DELAY has matured but stake is not refunded), `account_with_zero_everything` (an `accounts` entry with `balance == 0` AND `next_nonce == 0` AND no `stakes` / `registrants` reference — auto-creation residue from a credit-then-debit cycle; not a bug, just residue). Pulls `validators`, `stakes`, and full account enumeration via `chain-summary`. `--anomalies-only` suppresses healthy-state rows; pair with `--json` for monitoring-system ingestion. Default human output is a categorized per-finding table + summary footer (CRITICAL / INFO counts + total); `--json` emits `{findings: [{severity, kind, domain, detail}, …], summary: {critical, info, total}}`. **Exit codes**: 0 no findings (or 0 when `--anomalies-only` AND no anomalies in scope), 2 any CRITICAL finding (operator alert gate — stake_without_registrant), 1 RPC error / unreachable daemon / bad args. |
| `tools/operator_chain_export.sh [--rpc-port N] [--format {ndjson\|json\|compact}] [--out <file>] [--from H --to H \| --last N] [--include {transactions\|none}] [--quiet]` | Portable chain-export operator script. Walks the requested block range (default: full chain `0..head`; `--last N` covers spot-checks; `--from H --to H` covers ad-hoc audits) and serializes the result in one of three formats: `ndjson` (newline-delimited per-block JSON — pipe-friendly into `jq` / `grep` / `awk` for ad-hoc analysis), `json` (single envelope `{height, head_hash, blocks: [...]}` — operator cold-archive shape; consumable as a single document), `compact` (one line per block `<index> <hash> <prev_hash> <state_root> <timestamp> <tx_count>` — SQL pre-stage / spreadsheet ingestion). `--include transactions` includes the per-block `transactions[]` array (richer payload, larger export); `--include none` (default) strips transactions for header-only export. `--out <file>` writes to disk; absent emits to stdout. `--quiet` suppresses the progress header (useful when stdout is being piped). Use cases documented for cold-archive (single-document `json` export), pipe-to-jq (`determ-style ndjson` for `jq '.transactions[]'`), SQL pre-stage (`compact` format for `LOAD DATA INFILE` into MySQL/Postgres). Default emits to stdout for compatibility with stream-based pipelines. **Exit codes**: 0 export complete, 1 RPC error / unreachable daemon / bad args / file-write failure. |
| `tools/operator_committee_rotation.sh [--rpc-port N] [--from H] [--to H] [--json] [--anomalies-only]` | Consensus-committee rotation tracker over a block window (default: last 1000 blocks via `head - 999 .. head`; `--from H --to H` overrides). Walks the range pulling per-block `creators[]` via `determ block-info --json`, aggregates per-creator participation rate (appearances / window-size), committee-size distribution (min / max / mean / mode), and rotation events (consecutive blocks where the `creators[]` set differs from the immediately-prior block's set). Classifies each creator: **core** (participation > 80%) or **rotating** (participation < 50%); creators in between are unclassified. Flags anomalies: `committee_size_variance` (committee-size standard deviation > 1.5 within the window — sustained committee instability worth review), `single_dominant_creator` (any single creator > 95% of all blocks in the window — Sybil concentration / validator-monoculture signal), `high_rotation_rate` (> 50% of block transitions exhibit committee-set changes — churn pattern worth review). `--anomalies-only` suppresses healthy-state rows; pair with `--json` for monitoring-system ingestion. | `tools/operator_dapp_balance_audit.sh [--rpc-port N] [--from H] [--to H] [--json] [--anomalies-only]` | Per-DApp accrued-balance + revenue audit. Enumerates DApps via `determ dapp-list --json`, fans out to `determ show-account <domain> --json` per DApp to recover the current accrued balance (DApp domains earn balance via the v2.19 DAPP_CALL fee-routing path — every DAPP_CALL credits the target DApp's account ledger), then walks the block range (default: last 1000 blocks via `head - 999 .. head`; `--from H --to H` overrides) pulling per-block transactions via `determ block-info --json` and aggregating DAPP_CALL inflows targeting each DApp (sum of `amount` field across in-window calls). Reports per-DApp current balance + revenue-in-window + call count + active/inactive status, sorted by revenue descending. Computes top-10 by revenue + top-10 by balance + concentration metrics. Flags anomalies: `inactive_with_revenue` (any DApp in INACTIVE status whose accrued balance is non-zero — operator-action needed to drain the account before re-allocation; UX gap worth alerting on), `concentration_high` (top-1 DApp revenue > 50% of total revenue in the window — Sybil-routing or monopoly-DApp signal worth review). `--anomalies-only` suppresses healthy-state rows; pair with `--json` for monitoring-system ingestion.
