| `tools/operator_block_size_audit.sh [--rpc-port N] [--from H] [--to H] [--json] [--anomalies-only]` | Block-size distribution operator audit. Walks the block range (default: last 1000 blocks via `head - 999 .. head`; `--from H --to H` overrides) pulling per-block transactions + sizes via `determ block-info --json`, computes per-block tx count + estimated bytes (sum of serialized-tx sizes per block + fixed header overhead), and aggregates descriptive statistics across the window: mean / median / p95 / max for both tx count and byte count, plus the tx-type distribution histogram (TRANSFER / REGISTER / STAKE / UNSTAKE / DEREGISTER / DAPP_REGISTER / DAPP_CALL / DAPP_DEREGISTER / PARAM_CHANGE / MERGE_EVENT counts). Compares observed sizes against the S-022 per-message-type cap (4 MB for BLOCK_RESPONSE / BUNDLE; 1 MB tight default for consensus chatter); reports the cap-utilization percentage at p95 + max. Flags anomalies: `block_size_high` (any single block > 50% of S-022 cap — operator warning), `block_size_critical` (any single block > 80% of S-022 cap — critical alert; runaway block growth signal worth immediate triage), `tx_count_spike` (any single block's tx count > 10× the window median — bulk-submission pattern signal), `empty_block_run` (> 100 consecutive blocks with zero transactions — chain idleness signal worth review, distinct from short empty-block runs which are healthy timing-profile artifacts). `--anomalies-only` suppresses healthy-state rows; pair with `--json` for monitoring-system ingestion. Default human output is a stats summary table + tx-type histogram + summary footer (window range, mean/median/p95/max for tx count + bytes, cap utilization, anomaly count); `--json` emits `{window: {from,to}, stats: {tx_count: {mean, median, p95, max}, bytes: {mean, median, p95, max}}, by_type: {...}, cap_pct: {p95, max}, anomalies: [...]}`. **Exit codes**: 0 healthy distribution (or 0 when `--anomalies-only` AND no anomalies), 2 block_size_critical OR tx_count_spike OR empty_block_run anomaly (operator alert gate), 1 RPC error / unreachable daemon / bad args. |
| `tools/operator_wire_budget_audit.sh --rpc-port N [--headers-from F] [--include-snapshot] [--warn-pct N] [--crit-pct N] [--json] [--anomalies-only]` | Per-message-type **S-022 wire-cap headroom audit** — the framing-robustness complement to `operator_block_size_audit.sh` (whole-block JSON over a window vs ONE configurable cap). Retrieves the actual sync/gossip wire artifacts a node emits and judges EACH against its OWN `max_message_bytes` cap (`include/determ/net/messages.hpp`), not a single shared ceiling: **HEADERS_RESPONSE** (4 MB) via `determ headers --from F --count 256` (the 256-header page is `HEADERS_PAGE_MAX`, the worst-case page; `Node::on_headers_request` wraps the byte-identical `rpc_headers` output in `make_headers_response`, so this is the exact gossip-wire envelope), the **BLOCK tip** (4 MB) via `determ block-info <tip> --json` (`make_block(b)` body), and optionally **SNAPSHOT_RESPONSE** (16 MB) via `determ snapshot create` (gated by `--include-snapshot`; serialization can be momentarily expensive). Each artifact's size is the canonical-JSON length `len(json.dumps(obj, separators=(',',':')))` — an upper bound on the binary (wire-version 1) envelope, and the cap that bites first since JSON (v0) is frequently the negotiated wire version per A3/S8 (`src/net/binary_codec.cpp`). Classifies each as **OK** (size ≤ `--warn-pct` of cap, default 75%), **WARN** (`--warn-pct`..`--crit-pct`, default 75%-90%), or **CRIT** (> `--crit-pct`, default > 90%). Rationale: an over-cap wire message is not merely shed — the receiving peer DROPS the connection (`Peer::read_body` oversize close, same disposition as the framing-layer overflow), so an over-cap HEADERS_RESPONSE silently breaks light-client header sync from this node and an over-cap BLOCK breaks block propagation; > 90% is the last warning before the producer emits unrelayable messages. `--headers-from F` pins the 256-header page start (default `max(0, tip-255)` so the page ends at the tip — the freshest window). Issues only read RPCs (`head` / `headers` / `block-info` / `snapshot` — never a mutating RPC). Default human output is a per-artifact table (type / size / cap / %cap / state / detail) + an `[OK]` / `[WARN]` / `[CRITICAL]` summary; `--json` emits `{artifacts: [{type, cap_bytes, size_bytes, pct_of_cap_bps, classification, detail}, …], warn_pct, crit_pct, anomalies: [...], ok, rpc_port, head_height}`. Anomalies: **`wire_cap_approach`** (any artifact in [warn-pct, crit-pct] of its cap), **`wire_cap_critical`** (any artifact > crit-pct — over-cap risk). `--anomalies-only` suppresses OK rows. **Exit codes**: 0 success / informational (no CRIT), 2 `--anomalies-only` AND ≥1 artifact classed CRIT (operator alert gate — the node risks emitting an over-cap wire message that peers will reject), 1 RPC error / unreachable daemon / malformed response / bad args. |
| `tools/operator_inbound_outbound_balance.sh [--rpc-port N] [--from H] [--to H] [--bucket-blocks N] [--json] [--anomalies-only]` | Net cross-shard receipt flow tracker over time-bucket aggregations. Walks the block range (default: last 1000 blocks via `head - 999 .. head`; `--from H --to H` overrides) pulling per-block inbound + outbound CrossShardReceipt counts via `determ block-info --json`, then aggregates into fixed-size buckets (default `--bucket-blocks 100` — 100-block buckets; configurable for finer / coarser grain). Per-bucket: inbound count + outbound count + net (inbound - outbound) per shard pair. Computes the linear-regression trend on the net series across buckets (slope + intercept; positive slope = sustained inflow growth, negative slope = sustained outflow growth). **Single-shard deployments**: exits 0 immediately with INFO "no cross-shard activity by construction" (the script verifies `shard_count == 1` via `chain-summary` before doing any work — same gating pattern as `operator_receipt_audit.sh`). Flags anomalies: `inbound_spike` (any bucket's inbound count > 3× the median bucket inbound — bulk-import signal worth review), `outbound_spike` (any bucket's outbound count > 3× the median bucket outbound — bulk-export signal worth review), `trend_slope_high` (absolute trend slope > 50% of the median bucket flow — sustained shard-imbalance worth review). `--anomalies-only` suppresses healthy-state rows; pair with `--json` for monitoring-system ingestion. Default human output is a per-bucket flow table + trend regression summary + summary footer (window range, bucket count, total inbound, total outbound, net delta, trend slope, anomaly count); `--json` emits `{window: {from,to}, bucket_blocks: N, buckets: [{from, to, inbound, outbound, net}, …], trend: {slope, intercept}, anomalies: [...]}`. **Exit codes**: 0 healthy flow (or 0 when `--anomalies-only` AND no anomalies; single-shard topology emits 0 + INFO), 2 inbound_spike OR outbound_spike OR trend_slope_high anomaly (operator alert gate), 1 RPC error / unreachable daemon / bad args. |
| `tools/operator_subsidy_lottery_audit.sh [--rpc-port N] [--from H] [--to H] [--json] [--anomalies-only]` | LOTTERY-mode subsidy fairness audit over an `[from, to]` window (default: last 1000 blocks via `head - 999 .. head`). Walks the range pulling per-block subsidy-winner attribution via `determ block-info --json`, aggregates per-creator win counts across the window, and computes a chi-squared statistic against the expected uniform distribution `expected_per_creator = total_lottery_blocks / committee_size` (with degrees-of-freedom = committee_size - 1). Reports per-creator win counts (sorted descending), expected uniform count, per-creator chi-squared contribution, total chi-squared, degrees of freedom, and an interpretation band against standard chi-squared critical values at p=0.05 / p=0.01. Flags anomalies: **`chi_squared_p_lt_05`** — observed chi-squared exceeds the p=0.05 critical value (distribution is unlikely to be uniform under the null hypothesis; worth review for systematic bias); **`chi_squared_p_lt_01`** — observed chi-squared exceeds the p=0.01 critical value (strong evidence of non-uniformity — operator alert gate for RNG-correctness review or Sybil-concentration detection); **`single_creator_dominant`** — any single creator wins > 30% of lotteries in the window (concentration signal worth review independent of chi-squared). `--anomalies-only` suppresses healthy-state rows; pair with `--json` for monitoring-system ingestion. **FLAT-mode chains short-circuit on detection**: the script reads `config.subsidy_mode` from the daemon and emits an INFO-class single-line diagnostic `subsidy_mode=FLAT (lottery audit not applicable; exit 0)` when not in LOTTERY mode, exiting 0 (no anomaly — the audit's premise doesn't apply). Default human output is a per-creator win-count table + chi-squared statistics block + p-value interpretation + summary footer (window range, total lottery blocks, committee size, observed chi-squared, p-value band, anomaly count); `--json` emits `{window: {from,to}, subsidy_mode, per_creator: [{domain, wins, expected, chi_sq_contribution}, …], chi_squared: {total, dof, p_value_band}, summary: {total_lottery_blocks, committee_size}, anomalies: [...]}`. **Exit codes**: 0 fair distribution (or 0 when `--anomalies-only` AND no anomalies; 0 on FLAT-mode short-circuit), 2 chi_squared_p_lt_05 / chi_squared_p_lt_01 / single_creator_dominant anomaly (operator alert gate — systematic non-uniformity in LOTTERY-mode subsidy distribution), 1 RPC error / unreachable daemon / bad args. |
| `tools/operator_nef_drain_audit.sh [--rpc-port N] [--json] [--genesis <file>] [--from H] [--to H] [--floor N] [--anomalies-only]` | Read-only **E1 Negative-Entry-Fee (NEF) drain reconciliation**. The Zeroth pool (canonical `ZEROTH_ADDRESS` pseudo-account) halves on each *first-time* REGISTER — `nef = pool/2` transferred to the newcomer per `src/chain/chain.cpp::apply_block` — so after F genuine first-times `live = floor(zeroth_pool_initial / 2^F)`. From the live ZEROTH balance the script recovers `halvings_observed = floor(log2(initial/live))` (exact repeated integer-floor inverse of the apply path), walks `[from..to]` via `determ block-info --json` counting REGISTER txs (`type==1`, `from != ZEROTH`) as an UPPER BOUND on first-times (re-REGISTERs are indistinguishable on the wire and do not drain — mirrors the silent-skip caveat in `operator_fee_distribution_audit.sh`), and at full-history scope asserts the sound relation `registers_in_window >= halvings_attributable` (since `halvings <= first_times <= registers`). Reports `granted_total = initial - live`, the geometric next-grant schedule `floor(live/2)`, and cross-checks that NEF is a pure intra-supply transfer leaving `accumulated_subsidy` / `accumulated_slashed` untouched (A1 internal-transfer invariant). Reads only `determ status / head / balance <ZEROTH> / supply --json / block-info` — no mutating endpoints. `zeroth_pool_initial` is genesis-pinned (not RPC-exposed); supply it via `--genesis <file>` to enable the halving reconciliation (otherwise reported not-checkable). One Python pass with a 15s per-block subprocess timeout (cannot hang); single window walk then exit (no `--watch`). `--json` envelope; `--anomalies-only` suppresses healthy rows. Complements `operator_subsidy_pool_health.sh` (which projects FORWARD exhaustion from a drain rate and reads ZEROTH once) by running the BACKWARD forensic reconciliation that ties the live pool to the REGISTERs that drained it. **Anomalies**: `nef_not_seeded` / `nef_inert` (next grant == 0) / `nef_floor` (next grant ≤ `--floor`) are INFO; `halving_underflow` (registers < attributable halvings over full history) + `a1_internal_violation` (live > initial — pool grew, impossible under halving-only drain) are operator alerts. **Exit codes**: 0 healthy / informational (or NEF not seeded), 2 reconciliation anomaly or `--anomalies-only` with ≥1 flag, 1 RPC / bad args / unreadable `--genesis`. Verified node-free (`--help` + arg-rejection smoke; embedded-Python compile check). |
| `tools/operator_payments_audit.sh [--rpc-port N] [--from H] [--to H] [--json] [--anomalies-only] [--top N]` | TRANSFER-payment pattern audit over an `[from, to]` window (default: last 1000 blocks via `head - 999 .. head`). Walks the range pulling TRANSFER transactions per block via `determ block-info --json`, aggregates amount-bucket distribution across five buckets (`≤1`, `2-99`, `100-9999`, `10000-999999`, `≥1000000`), top-`N` senders by transfer count + total amount (default `--top 20`), top-`N` receivers by transfer count + total amount, and an anon-vs-domain TRANSFER breakdown (anon→anon, anon→domain, domain→anon, domain→domain — applies the canonical `is_anon_address` predicate per S-028: `0x` prefix + 64 lowercase hex characters). Reports per-bucket totals (counts + summed amounts), top-N sender table (sorted by count descending; tie-break by amount descending), top-N receiver table (same sort), 2×2 anon-vs-domain breakdown matrix, and a window-level summary footer (total transfers, total amount routed, distinct senders, distinct receivers, anon-touching percentage). Flags anomalies: **`single_sender_dominant`** — any single sender > 30% of transfer count in the window (Sybil-submission signal worth review); **`single_receiver_dominant`** — any single receiver > 30% of transfer count (concentration / faucet-target signal worth review); **`anon_to_anon_ratio_high`** — anon-to-anon TRANSFER ratio > 80% of total anon activity (privacy-shielding pattern worth review for mixing-service detection); **`large_amount_spike`** — any single transfer in the top-bucket (≥1,000,000) exceeds 10× the previous top-bucket maximum (sudden whale-movement signal). `--anomalies-only` suppresses healthy-state rows; pair with `--json` for monitoring-system ingestion. Default human output is the amount-bucket histogram + top-N senders table + top-N receivers table + anon/domain breakdown + summary footer (window range, total transfers, total amount, distinct senders, distinct receivers, anon-touching percentage, anomaly count); `--json` emits `{window: {from,to}, amount_buckets: {le_1, ...}, top_senders: [...], top_receivers: [...], by_direction: {anon_to_anon, anon_to_domain, domain_to_anon, domain_to_domain}, summary: {total_transfers, total_amount, distinct_senders, distinct_receivers}, anomalies: [...]}`. **Exit codes**: 0 healthy distribution (or 0 when `--anomalies-only` AND no anomalies), 2 single_sender_dominant / single_receiver_dominant / anon_to_anon_ratio_high / large_amount_spike anomaly (operator alert gate), 1 RPC error / unreachable daemon / bad args. |
| `tools/operator_dust_audit.sh [--rpc-port N] [--dust-threshold N] [--json] [--anomalies-only]` | Dust-account classification audit. Enumerates every account in the live chain state via `determ chain-summary --json` + a follow-up `determ show-account <domain> --json` per account, then classifies each into one of four buckets: **Zero** (`balance == 0 AND next_nonce == 0` — auto-creation residue; not an anomaly but worth quantifying), **Dust-sender** (`balance > 0 AND balance <= dust_threshold AND next_nonce > 0` — has spent down to dust; default `--dust-threshold 100`), **Dust-receiver** (`balance > 0 AND balance <= dust_threshold AND next_nonce == 0` — received dust but never spent; the classic dust-spam victim pattern), **Active** (`balance > dust_threshold` — normal account). The window walk also tags recent inbound/outbound activity per account via the last 1000 blocks of TRANSFER traffic for context. Flags anomalies: **`mass_dust_spam`** — > 100 distinct Dust-receiver accounts appearing within the last 100 blocks (classic dust-spam attack pattern — adversary blasts small amounts to many anon addresses to bloat account state on disk), **`zero_account_growth_rate_high`** — count of Zero accounts (auto-creation residue) > 30% of total account count (suggests heavy credit-then-debit cycling, possibly indicative of test-fixture residue in production or a dust-then-sweep adversary), **`dust_receiver_concentration`** — > 50% of all Dust-receivers received their dust from a single sender (Sybil-victim pattern; the adversary is using one sender to dust many receivers). `--anomalies-only` suppresses healthy-state rows; pair with `--json` for monitoring-system ingestion. Default human output is a per-bucket count summary + top-20 Dust-receiver-by-recent-inbound table + summary footer (total accounts, per-bucket counts + percentages, dust threshold, anomaly count); `--json` emits `{dust_threshold, total_accounts, by_bucket: {zero, dust_sender, dust_receiver, active}, top_dust_receivers: [...], anomalies: [...]}`. **Exit codes**: 0 healthy distribution (or 0 when `--anomalies-only` AND no anomalies), 2 mass_dust_spam / zero_account_growth_rate_high / dust_receiver_concentration anomaly (operator alert gate — dust-spam-bloat pressure on the account state), 1 RPC error / unreachable daemon / bad args. |
| `tools/operator_stake_yield.sh [--rpc-port N] [--from H] [--to H] [--json] [--anomalies-only]` | Per-validator yield computation. Enumerates the active validator set via `determ stakes --json` (each entry: domain, `stake_locked`), then walks the block range (default: last 1000 blocks via `head - 999 .. head`; `--from H --to H` overrides) pulling per-block creator + fee + subsidy attribution via `determ block-info --json`, aggregates per-validator subsidy-earned + fees-earned across the window, and computes the apparent annualized yield = `(subsidy + fees) / stake_locked * (blocks_per_year / window_blocks)`. Reports per-validator: domain, current stake, subsidy earned in window, fees earned in window, total earned, yield % (annualized), participation rate (creator slot share). Sorts descending by yield by default. Computes top-3 by yield + bottom-3 by yield + concentration metrics. Flags anomalies: **`yield_concentration_high`** — top-1 validator's yield > 30% of the total committee yield in the window (Sybil-concentration / centralized-stake-pool signal worth review), **`yield_outlier_high`** — any single validator's yield exceeds 3× the median validator yield (potential signaling-irregularity worth audit against committee selection / Sybil pressure), **`yield_outlier_low`** — any single active validator's yield < 10% of the median (under-performing validator may be missing its committee-slot opportunities — worth review for participation gap). `--anomalies-only` suppresses healthy-state rows; pair with `--json` for monitoring-system ingestion. Default human output is a sorted-by-yield per-validator table + concentration summary + summary footer (window range, total validators, total subsidy distributed, total fees distributed, top-1 yield share, anomaly count); `--json` emits `{window: {from,to}, validators: [{domain, stake_locked, subsidy_in_window, fees_in_window, total_earned, yield_pct, participation_rate}, …], summary: {total_validators, total_subsidy, total_fees, top1_yield_share}, anomalies: [...]}`. **Exit codes**: 0 healthy distribution (or 0 when `--anomalies-only` AND no anomalies), 2 yield_concentration_high / yield_outlier_high / yield_outlier_low anomaly (operator alert gate — stake-yield concentration is the FA1 / FA8 cartelization signal that compounds across rounds), 1 RPC error / unreachable daemon / bad args. |
| `tools/operator_block_creator_fairness.sh [--rpc-port N] [--from H] [--to H] [--json] [--anomalies-only]` | Committee-selection fairness audit using a chi-squared statistical test against the expected uniform distribution. Walks the block range (default: last 1000 blocks via `head - 999 .. head`; `--from H --to H` overrides) pulling per-block `creators[]` arrays via `determ block-info --json`, counts each validator's appearance count across the window, and computes the chi-squared statistic: `expected_per_creator = (total_creator_appearances / committee_size)` (with degrees-of-freedom = `committee_size - 1`). Reports per-creator appearance counts (sorted descending), expected uniform count, per-creator chi-squared contribution, total chi-squared, degrees of freedom, and an interpretation band against standard chi-squared critical values at p=0.05 / p=0.01. Distinct from `operator_subsidy_lottery_audit.sh` (which tests LOTTERY-mode subsidy fairness — a function of the lottery winner selection inside `chain.cpp` distribute path); this script tests the committee-selection layer itself (the upstream FA8 selection over the active registrant set per `compute_creators_for_block`). Flags anomalies: **`chi_squared_p_lt_05`** — observed chi-squared exceeds the p=0.05 critical value (distribution is unlikely to be uniform under the null hypothesis; worth review for committee-selection bias — possible Sybil cluster or RNG-correctness issue), **`chi_squared_p_lt_01`** — observed chi-squared exceeds the p=0.01 critical value (strong evidence of non-uniform committee selection — operator alert gate for FA8 selection-soundness review), **`single_creator_dominant`** — any single creator appearance count > 30% of total appearances in the window (concentration signal worth review independent of chi-squared). `--anomalies-only` suppresses healthy-state rows; pair with `--json` for monitoring-system ingestion. Default human output is a per-creator appearance-count table + chi-squared statistics block + p-value interpretation + summary footer (window range, total appearances, committee size, observed chi-squared, p-value band, anomaly count); `--json` emits `{window: {from,to}, per_creator: [{domain, appearances, expected, chi_sq_contribution}, …], chi_squared: {total, dof, p_value_band}, summary: {total_appearances, committee_size}, anomalies: [...]}`. **Exit codes**: 0 fair distribution (or 0 when `--anomalies-only` AND no anomalies), 2 chi_squared_p_lt_05 / chi_squared_p_lt_01 / single_creator_dominant anomaly (operator alert gate — systematic non-uniformity in FA8 committee-selection distribution), 1 RPC error / unreachable daemon / bad args. |
| `tools/operator_storage_growth.sh [--data-dir <dir>] [--rpc-port N] [--json] [--anomalies-only]` | Chain.json + snapshot file size growth tracker. Inspects the on-disk footprint of the running daemon's data directory (default: `$HOME/.determ/`; `--data-dir <dir>` overrides) — measures `chain.json` size, every `snapshot-*.json` size, and (when present) backup-directory totals. Cross-references the live head height via `determ head --json` (or skips the cross-reference if RPC is unreachable — operator can still get a pure on-disk size report). Computes per-block bytes (`chain.json size / head_index`) plus snapshot age (newest snapshot file mtime vs wall clock) and snapshot-vs-chain delta (snapshot.head_index gap behind live head). Flags anomalies: **`chain_size_excessive`** — `chain.json > 1 GiB` AND per-block bytes > 4 KiB (sustained large-state pressure worth review — the typical p99 block is under 4 KiB even on busy chains; chronic excess signals either tx-payload bloat, snapshot-pruning regression, or a malformed serialization path), **`snapshot_stale`** — newest snapshot file is more than 24 hours old AND head_index has advanced > 1000 blocks since (operator snapshot cadence has stalled; future restore would require expensive full-replay), **`snapshot_lag_excessive`** — snapshot.head_index lags live head by > 10000 blocks (the same restore-cost-amplification signal from a different axis: even a "fresh" snapshot is operationally useless if it's far behind live state), **`per_block_growth_high`** — per-block bytes > 16 KiB (sustained block-bloat signal worth FA-Apply-3 / S-022 review). `--anomalies-only` suppresses healthy-state rows. Default human output is a per-file size table + a chain summary line (head_index, chain.json size, snapshot count, newest snapshot age) + summary footer (total bytes on disk, per-block bytes, anomaly count); `--json` emits `{data_dir, chain_size_bytes, snapshot_count, newest_snapshot_age_s, per_block_bytes, head_index, snapshot_lag_blocks, anomalies: [...]}`. **Exit codes**: 0 healthy growth (or 0 when `--anomalies-only` AND no anomalies), 2 chain_size_excessive / snapshot_stale / snapshot_lag_excessive / per_block_growth_high anomaly (operator alert gate — large-state pressure or stale-snapshot risk), 1 data-dir unreadable / RPC error (when cross-reference is required) / bad args. |
| `tools/operator_backup_health.sh [--data-dir <dir>] [--backup-dir <dir>] [--json] [--anomalies-only]` | Active vs backup directory comparison + truncation detection. Compares the live data directory (default `$HOME/.determ/`; `--data-dir <dir>` overrides) against a sibling backup directory (default `$HOME/.determ-backup/`; `--backup-dir <dir>` overrides) file-by-file (`chain.json` + every `snapshot-*.json`). For each file present in either directory, reports presence in both / active-only / backup-only, sizes (active vs backup), and the timestamp delta (when both present). Flags anomalies: **`backup_stale`** — backup `chain.json` mtime is older than 7 days (operator backup cadence has stalled; routine rotation has stopped), **`backup_truncated`** — backup `chain.json` size < 50% of active `chain.json` size (backup is suspiciously short — possible partial-write or rsync truncation; restoring from this would lose recent blocks silently), **`backup_size_mismatch`** — backup `chain.json` is larger than active (active chain may have been rolled back or rebuilt; the backup is now ahead of "live" — worth review before next backup overwrites), **`backup_missing`** — backup directory exists but contains no `chain.json` (rotation pipeline is failing silently), **`snapshot_count_mismatch`** — backup snapshot count differs from active by > 5 files (the backup pipeline is skipping snapshots — partial-coverage signal worth review). `--anomalies-only` suppresses healthy-state rows. Default human output is a per-file comparison table + summary footer (active total bytes, backup total bytes, ratio, anomaly count); `--json` emits `{data_dir, backup_dir, files: [{name, active_size, backup_size, mtime_delta_s, status}, …], summary: {active_total, backup_total, ratio, snapshot_count_active, snapshot_count_backup}, anomalies: [...]}`. Pure local computation — no daemon RPC required (file-system-only diagnostic). **Exit codes**: 0 healthy backup (or 0 when `--anomalies-only` AND no anomalies), 2 backup_stale / backup_truncated / backup_size_mismatch / backup_missing / snapshot_count_mismatch anomaly (operator alert gate — backup pipeline has regressed; do not rely on this backup for recovery without remediation), 1 data-dir or backup-dir unreadable / bad args. |
| `tools/operator_chain_freshness.sh [--rpc-port N] [--last-n N] [--max-age-ms N] [--json] [--anomalies-only]` | Per-block age distribution over the last-N-blocks sliding window (default `--last-n 100`; range clamps to chain head). For each block in the window, computes age = `now_ms - block.timestamp_ms` and emits min / median / p95 / max plus the count of blocks exceeding the configurable `--max-age-ms` threshold (default: profile-aware — pulled from `determ summary --json` `profile` field; tactical/cluster ≤ 2× round_total_ms, regional ≤ 3× round_total_ms, global ≤ 4× round_total_ms; falls back to `--max-age-ms` override). Default human output emits a 1-line digest (`freshness OK p95=… max=… stale_count=…`); `--json` emits `{n_blocks, min_ms, median_ms, p95_ms, max_ms, stale_count, stale_threshold_ms, profile, rpc_port}`; `--anomalies-only` suppresses output when `stale_count == 0`. Diagnostic for slow producers, network partitions, profile/operator-config mismatch, NTP drift on validator clocks. **Exit codes**: 0 freshness OK (`stale_count == 0`), 2 stale-block anomaly detected (operator alert gate), 1 RPC error / malformed response. |
| `tools/operator_dapp_topic_audit.sh [--rpc-port N] [--json] [--anomalies-only] [--collision-threshold N]` | DApp registry topic-usage audit + collision-attack detector. Enumerates all registered DApps via `determ dapp-list --json`, fans out to `determ dapp-info --domain D --json` per DApp to recover the per-DApp `topics[]` field, then aggregates the per-topic DApp count across the registry. Flags topics claimed by ≥ N distinct domains (default `--collision-threshold 2`) — a single topic claimed by multiple DApps indicates either coordination ambiguity (legitimate cross-DApp protocol) or topic-collision squat (one DApp registering popular topic names to confuse `dapp_messages` queries against a real DApp). Per-topic and per-DApp counts are emitted with the offenders listed; `--anomalies-only` skips output when no topic exceeds the threshold. Diagnostic for DApp-substrate registry hygiene (v2.18+) and topic-collision attack surface assessment. **Exit codes**: 0 no collision above threshold, 2 collision detected (operator alert gate), 1 RPC error / malformed response. |
| `tools/operator_genesis_diff.sh --left <file> --right <file> [--json] [--anomalies-only]` | Semantic two-genesis diff with severity classification. Parses two `genesis.json` files (the operator/forensic compare-two-bootstraps use case — onboarding-mismatch debugging, accidental-config-drift detection, fork forensics) and classifies each differing field into one of four severity tiers: **CRITICAL** (changes that produce a different `genesis_hash` per `compute_genesis_hash` — `chain_id`, `protocol_version`, `genesis_timestamp`, `initial_allocations`), **HIGH** (consensus-affecting parameters not currently bound by `compute_genesis_hash` per S-039 — `m_creators`, `k_block_sigs`, `bft_enabled`, `bft_escalation_threshold`, `initial_shard_count`, `shard_address_salt`, `min_stake`, `epoch_blocks`), **MEDIUM** (economic parameters per S-039 — `block_subsidy`, `subsidy_pool_initial`, `subsidy_mode`, `nef_grant_amount`, `nef_pool_initial`), **LOW** (operator-facing metadata — `description`, `notes`, ordering of equivalent fields). Default human output groups by tier; `--json` emits `{critical_diffs:[…], high_diffs:[…], medium_diffs:[…], low_diffs:[…], left_path, right_path}`; `--anomalies-only` suppresses output when all tiers are empty (genuine no-diff). Diagnostic for operator onboarding, post-incident genesis-config drift forensics, and S-039 awareness (matching `chain_id` + `initial_allocations` produces identical `genesis_hash` even when consensus params differ — runs into the S-039 gap loudly). **Exit codes**: 0 no differences, 2 critical or high diff detected (operator alert gate), 3 medium-only diff (advisory), 1 file-parse error / file not found. |
| `tools/operator_validator_uptime.sh [--rpc-port N] [--from H] [--to H] [--json] [--anomalies-only] [--threshold-pct N]` | Per-validator block-sig participation rate audit. Walks the block range (default: last 1000 blocks via `head - 999 .. head`; `--from H --to H` overrides) pulling per-block `creators[]` + `block_sigs[]` arrays via `determ block-info --json`. For each domain that appeared in any block's creator set in the window, computes the participation rate = `signed_blocks / eligible_blocks` (`eligible_blocks` = count of blocks where the domain appeared in `creators[]`; `signed_blocks` = subset of those where the domain produced a `BlockSigMsg` that landed in `block_sigs[]`). Reports per-validator: domain, eligible appearances, signed appearances, participation %, classification (HIGH ≥ 95%, MEDIUM 80%-95%, LOW < 80%). Sorts by participation ascending by default (worst-performing first — surfaces silent validators). Flags anomalies: **`low_participation`** — participation < `--threshold-pct N` (default 80% — silent-validator signal worth review for committee-rotation pressure or operator-side mute), **`zero_signed_eligible_nonzero`** — eligible_blocks > 0 AND signed_blocks == 0 (completely silent committee member — possible network partition or operator-side stall), **`participation_outlier_low`** — any single validator's participation < 50% of the median participation in the window (severe-underperformance signal independent of absolute threshold). `--anomalies-only` suppresses healthy-state rows; pair with `--json` for monitoring-system ingestion. Default human output is a sorted-by-participation per-validator table + classification summary + summary footer (window range, total validators audited, HIGH/MEDIUM/LOW counts, median participation, anomaly count, threshold); `--json` emits `{window: {from,to}, validators: [{domain, eligible_blocks, signed_blocks, participation_pct, classification}, …], summary: {total_validators, high, medium, low, median_pct, threshold_pct}, anomalies: [...]}`. **Exit codes**: 0 healthy participation (or 0 when `--anomalies-only` AND no anomalies), 2 low_participation / zero_signed_eligible_nonzero / participation_outlier_low anomaly (operator alert gate — silent-validator signals compound across rounds and degrade K-of-K convergence), 1 RPC error / unreachable daemon / bad args. |
| `tools/operator_unique_address_audit.sh [--rpc-port N] [--from H] [--to H] [--json] [--anomalies-only]` | Distinct-address engagement metrics audit. Walks the block range (default: last 1000 blocks via `head - 999 .. head`; `--from H --to H` overrides) pulling TRANSFER + REGISTER + STAKE + DAPP_CALL transactions per block via `determ block-info --json`, enumerates each tx's `from` + `to` addresses (TRANSFER), `domain` (REGISTER / STAKE), and `caller` (DAPP_CALL), then aggregates: total distinct addresses touched in window, by-type breakdown (anon-only count via `is_anon_address` predicate per S-028 vs domain-only count vs mixed-history addresses), new-vs-returning split (addresses first-seen within window vs addresses present in pre-window state), top-20 most-active addresses by interaction count + amount routed. Reports a window-level engagement profile and per-block churn (distinct addresses touched per block, sparkline-style). Flags anomalies: **`distinct_address_growth_high`** — distinct-address count grew > 100% across the window (sustained bulk-address engagement signal — possible Sybil-onboarding pressure), **`single_address_dominant`** — any single address > 30% of in-window interactions (concentration signal worth review for whale-or-bot activity), **`new_address_rate_high`** — > 50% of in-window addresses are first-seen (high-churn pattern worth review for ephemeral-address bots versus organic onboarding). `--anomalies-only` suppresses healthy-state rows; pair with `--json` for monitoring-system ingestion. Default human output is a top-20 active-address table + new-vs-returning summary + by-type breakdown + summary footer (window range, total distinct addresses, anon count, domain count, new count, returning count, anomaly count); `--json` emits `{window: {from,to}, distinct_addresses, by_type: {anon, domain, mixed}, new_count, returning_count, top_addresses: [...], anomalies: [...]}`. **Exit codes**: 0 healthy engagement (or 0 when `--anomalies-only` AND no anomalies), 2 distinct_address_growth_high / single_address_dominant / new_address_rate_high anomaly (operator alert gate — distinct-address dynamics are an early Sybil-detection signal), 1 RPC error / unreachable daemon / bad args. |
| `tools/operator_anomaly_summary.sh [--rpc-port N] [--json] [--scripts <list>]` | Meta-aggregator operator script — composes 5+ underlying operator scripts into a single anomaly-summary digest. Default script set (overridable via `--scripts <comma-separated-list>`): `operator_chain_health.sh`, `operator_supply_check.sh`, `operator_validator_uptime.sh`, `operator_stake_audit.sh`, `operator_committee_audit.sh`, `operator_dapp_audit.sh`, `operator_merge_state_audit.sh`, `operator_orphan_check.sh`, `operator_block_lag_check.sh`, `operator_storage_growth.sh`, `operator_backup_health.sh`. Invokes each underlying script with `--json --anomalies-only` (when supported by the underlying script — falls back to `--json` otherwise) and aggregates each script's per-anomaly-list into a single envelope keyed by script name. Computes a meta-classification per script: **GREEN** (script exit 0, zero anomalies), **YELLOW** (script exit 0 but non-empty anomaly list — script's anomaly-detection layer found issues but classified them below the alert threshold), **RED** (script exit 2 — operator alert gate fired), **ERROR** (script exit 1 — RPC / args / dependency error worth investigation independent of the audit content). Reports per-script status + per-script anomaly count + per-script top-3 anomaly identifiers, plus a window-level summary (total RED count, total YELLOW count, total ERROR count, scripts-run count). Designed for monitoring-system ingestion: a single `operator_anomaly_summary.sh --json` invocation gives a dashboard-grade per-script status panel without operators manually composing each underlying script. `--scripts <list>` overrides the default set (useful for narrower audits — e.g., `--scripts operator_chain_health.sh,operator_supply_check.sh` for a quick liveness-only check). Default human output is a per-script status table + per-script top-3 anomaly identifiers + summary footer (RED count, YELLOW count, ERROR count, scripts run, total anomalies); `--json` emits `{scripts: [{name, status, exit_code, anomaly_count, top_anomalies: [...]}, …], summary: {red, yellow, green, error, scripts_run, total_anomalies}}`. **Exit codes**: 0 all-green (zero anomalies across all underlying scripts), 2 any underlying script returned RED status (operator alert gate — at least one underlying audit found an alert-worthy anomaly), 1 any underlying script returned ERROR status (operator should investigate the failed dependency before trusting the aggregate). |
| `tools/operator_merge_state_audit.sh [--rpc-port N] [--json] [--anomalies-only]` | R7 under-quorum-merge state audit. Pulls the live `merge_state_` field via `chain-summary --json` (the R7 MERGE_BEGIN / MERGE_END field set: `refugee_region`, `host_region`, `merge_begin_height`, `expected_merge_end_height`, `effective_height`, `status`) and reports current merge status. Classifies the merge state: **NONE** (no active merge — the healthy default), **PENDING** (MERGE_BEGIN applied but MERGE_END not yet emitted — refugee region's K-quorum is currently borrowed from the host region), **STALE** (PENDING state has persisted longer than the expected merge duration — the R7 grace window has elapsed but MERGE_END was never emitted), **ANOMALOUS** (merge_state fields contain internally-inconsistent values — e.g., refugee_region == host_region, effective_height > current_height, expected_merge_end_height < merge_begin_height). Flags anomalies: **`merge_long_running`** — PENDING state has persisted for > 1000 blocks since `merge_begin_height` (operator should investigate why the refugee region hasn't re-formed a quorum; either the refugee operators have permanently left or the K-quorum threshold is misconfigured), **`merge_state_inconsistent`** — any internal field-set violation per the ANOMALOUS classification (data-integrity worth immediate triage), **`merge_overdue`** — `expected_merge_end_height < current_height` AND status still PENDING (the R7-protocol-defined grace window has passed; MERGE_END should have been emitted but wasn't — possible producer-side regression in the MERGE_END emit path). `--anomalies-only` suppresses healthy-state rows; pair with `--json` for monitoring-system ingestion. Default human output is a status-line summary (`merge_status=NONE/PENDING/STALE/ANOMALOUS`) + (when active) a field-set detail block + summary footer (status, merge_begin_height, current_height, blocks_in_merge, anomaly count); `--json` emits `{status, refugee_region, host_region, merge_begin_height, expected_merge_end_height, effective_height, current_height, blocks_in_merge, anomalies: [...]}`. **Exit codes**: 0 healthy merge state (or 0 when `--anomalies-only` AND no anomalies; status NONE always returns 0), 2 merge_long_running / merge_state_inconsistent / merge_overdue anomaly (operator alert gate — under-quorum-merge has stalled or regressed), 1 RPC error / unreachable daemon / bad args. |
| `tools/operator_merge_audit.sh [--rpc-port N] [--window N] [--block-timeout S] [--json]` | R7 merge audit judged against the **protocol threshold constants** (R41 I4) — the threshold/revert-budget complement to `operator_merge_state_audit.sh` (which does block-window event forensics with fixed heuristics). This one leads with the three live constants (`merge_threshold_blocks` / `revert_threshold_blocks` / `merge_grace_blocks`, read via `snapshot create --headers 0` → `snapshot inspect`) and judges each active merge against its *own* protocol-defined revert budget: a merge whose tip is more than `revert_threshold_blocks` past its on-chain `effective_height` is **OVERDUE**. Reads only read-only RPCs (`status` for sharding_mode/shard_id, the snapshot for constants + `merge_state[]`, `head --field height`, and `block-info` for in-flight MERGE_EVENT (TxType 7) decode) — no mutating endpoints. Per-merge window status pending / active / OVERDUE / unknown. Single bounded pass (no `--watch`), per-call timeout via `--block-timeout`. `--json` for monitoring ingestion. Soundness context: `docs/proofs/MergeStateSoundness.md` (MS-1..MS-6, the `m:` namespace determinism the merge_state it reads is bound by). **Exit codes**: 0 healthy (or non-EXTENDED / single-shard skip), 2 an active merge OVERDUE past its revert window (operator alert gate), 1 RPC / args / decode error. Verified node-free (`--help` + arg-guards + stubbed-RPC branch exercise). |
| `tools/operator_dapp_registration_audit.sh [--rpc-port N] [--from H] [--to H] [--json] [--anomalies-only]` | v2.18 `DAPP_REGISTER` event audit over an `[from, to]` block window (default: last 1000 blocks via `head --json` → `[head-1000, head]`). Walks blocks in range and partitions every DAPP_REGISTER / DAPP_DEREGISTER tx into a three-bucket breakdown — **first-time** (FA-Apply-14 NEF-drain trigger; first appearance of `domain` in the registry — the only path that drains `nef_pool / 2` per E1), **update** (registry entry exists, owner field unchanged; `service_pubkey` / `endpoint_url` / `topics` / `metadata` may rotate — no NEF credit per T-N2), and **deactivate** (DAPP_DEREGISTER schedules `inactive_from = current_height + DAPP_GRACE_BLOCKS`; the registry entry remains queryable until activation per T-D4). Per-domain timeline reconstruction: for each domain seen in the window, emits `{domain, first_seen_height, last_event_height, event_count, nef_credit_total, status: {active, pending_deactivation, inactive}}`. Aggregate metrics: total first-time count (matches the NEF drain count over the window — operator can cross-check against `nef_pool` shrinkage), total update count, total deactivate count, distinct-domain count, churn ratio (`deactivate / first_time`). Flags anomalies: **`dapp_churn_burst`** (≥10 first-times in any 100-block sub-window — bulk registration spike), **`dapp_registry_thrash`** (same domain DAPP_REGISTER → DAPP_DEREGISTER → DAPP_REGISTER within the window — operator-UX signal), **`dapp_zero_nef_first_time`** (first-time REGISTER recorded but no `nef_pool` decrement observed in the same block — pool-exhaustion edge per T-N3 OR a chain-state corruption signal). Default mode emits a 1-line digest (`DApp registrations: first_time=N updates=N deactivates=N domains=N anomalies=N`); `--json` emits the full structured envelope (`{from, to, totals: {first_time, update, deactivate}, by_domain: [{domain, first_seen_height, last_event_height, event_count, nef_credit_total, status}], anomalies: [...]}`). **Exit codes**: 0 healthy, 2 anomalies present (operator alert gate — bulk-registration spike, registry thrash, or chain-state corruption signal), 1 RPC error / bad args. |
| `tools/operator_event_summary.sh [--rpc-port N] [--from H] [--to H] [--json] [--anomalies-only]` | Cross-event aggregator — produces a single operator digest covering the three protocol-level evidence streams (AbortEvent, EquivocationEvent, MergeEvent) that each individually have a dedicated operator script (`operator_equivocation_digest.sh`, `operator_merge_state_audit.sh`) but whose joint health view is the natural operator question ("is anything weird happening on-chain in the last N blocks?"). Walks block range `[from, to]` (default: last 1000 blocks via `head --json` → `[head-1000, head]`) and partitions every event field into three streams: **aborts** (FA-Apply-11 Round-1 + Round-2 AbortEvents with offender domain + Phase tag + slash amount aggregation), **equivocations** (FA-Apply-10 EquivocationEvents with offender domain + evidence-bundle hash + slash amount aggregation), **merge events** (R7 MERGE_BEGIN / MERGE_END pairs per under-quorum-merge state transition with refugee/host region routing). Joint metrics: total event count by type, distinct offenders count (anti-cartel signal — concentration of misbehavior in a small validator set per FA5/FA6/FA8 economic-irrationality threshold), per-block event density (peaks → operator alert), accumulated_slashed delta over window (cross-check against `chain-summary --json` `accumulated_slashed` field for arithmetic consistency). Flags anomalies: **`event_burst`** (≥5 events of any single type in a single block — concentrated cartel-attack signal), **`equivocation_offender_concentration`** (single offender accounts for ≥50% of equivocation events in the window — concentrated Byzantine actor), **`merge_event_unpaired`** (MERGE_BEGIN without matching MERGE_END within the expected window — composes with `operator_merge_state_audit.sh` STALE diagnostic), **`slash_delta_mismatch`** (sum of per-event slash amounts ≠ `accumulated_slashed` delta over the window — apply-layer accounting drift signal per FA-Apply-10 T-E5 + FA-Apply-11 T-A4 A1 invariance). Default mode: 1-line digest (`Events [H1, H2]: aborts=N equivocations=N merges=N offenders=N anomalies=N`); `--json` emits `{from, to, totals: {aborts, equivocations, merges}, by_offender: [{domain, abort_count, equivocation_count, slash_total}], merge_pairs: [{begin_height, end_height, refugee_region, host_region}], anomalies: [...]}`. **Exit codes**: 0 healthy, 2 anomalies present (operator alert gate — event burst / offender concentration / unpaired merge / slash accounting drift), 1 RPC error / bad args. |
| `tools/operator_balance_distribution.sh [--rpc-port N] [--json] [--anomalies-only] [--gini-threshold F]` | Account-balance distribution audit + Gini coefficient computation. Enumerates every account in the live chain state via `determ chain-summary --json` followed by a per-account `determ show-account <domain> --json` fan-out, extracts the `balance` field per account, then computes the Gini coefficient `G = (sum_{i,j} \|b_i - b_j\|) / (2 N sum_i b_i)` over the balance vector (0.0 = perfect equality, 1.0 = perfect inequality — one account holds the entire supply). Also reports per-decile distribution (top 1% / top 10% / median / bottom 10% balance shares), absolute balance percentiles (p50 / p90 / p95 / p99), total-supply cross-check against `chain-summary.total_supply` (mismatch flags `supply_accounting_drift`), and top-20 by-balance table. Flags anomalies: **`gini_concentration_high`** — `G > --gini-threshold` (default 0.7 — high-concentration signal worth review for whale-pool dominance or initial-allocation Sybil pattern), **`top1pct_dominant`** — top 1% of accounts hold > 50% of total supply (oligarch concentration signal), **`supply_accounting_drift`** — `Σ balances ≠ total_supply` per `chain-summary` (data-integrity worth immediate triage — possible auto-creation accounting gap, dropped-account snapshot bug, or A1-counter divergence). `--anomalies-only` suppresses healthy-state rows; pair with `--json` for monitoring-system ingestion. Default human output is a top-20 by-balance table + per-decile breakdown + Gini + summary footer (total accounts, total supply, Gini, top1% share, top10% share, anomaly count); `--json` emits `{total_accounts, total_supply, gini, gini_threshold, by_decile: {p10..p100}, by_percentile: {p50, p90, p95, p99}, top_accounts: [...], anomalies: [...]}`. Pure read-only RPC enumeration — no on-chain side effects. Diagnostic for governance / token-traded deployments (Gini + decile distribution is the canonical wealth-concentration metric in economics; Determ exposes it for operator-visible distributional health). **Exit codes**: 0 healthy distribution (or 0 when `--anomalies-only` AND no anomalies), 2 gini_concentration_high / top1pct_dominant / supply_accounting_drift anomaly (operator alert gate — distributional concentration may foreshadow centralization or accounting regression), 1 RPC error / unreachable daemon / bad args. |
| `tools/operator_fee_distribution_audit.sh [--rpc-port N] [--from H] [--to H] [--json] [--anomalies-only] [--concentration-threshold F]` | Per-block fee-to-creator distribution audit. Walks the block range (default: last 1000 blocks via `head - 999 .. head`; `--from H --to H` overrides) pulling per-block `creators[]` + per-tx `fee` field via `determ block-info --json`, aggregates the total fee paid into each block and the creator-set that received it (under the E1/E3/E4 subsidy + fee distribution model — fees are distributed to the block's K-of-K committee per the apply rule), then attributes the per-block fee total back to each creator domain. Reports per-creator: domain, blocks-as-creator count, total fees earned in window, average fee per block, share-of-total-fees percentage. Sorts descending by fee earned. Cross-checks `Σ per-creator-fees == Σ per-block-fees` (mismatch flags `fee_accounting_drift` — possible apply-layer regression in `Chain::apply_block`). Flags anomalies: **`fee_concentration_high`** — top-1 creator's fee share > `--concentration-threshold F` (default 0.30 — Sybil-concentration / single-validator-dominance signal worth review against committee selection), **`fee_outlier_high`** — any single creator's fee share exceeds 3× the median creator share (potential bias in committee-selection RNG or per-validator stake concentration), **`fee_accounting_drift`** — per-creator-fee sum doesn't equal per-block-fee sum (data-integrity worth immediate triage). `--anomalies-only` suppresses healthy-state rows; pair with `--json` for monitoring-system ingestion. | `tools/operator_rate_limiter_audit.sh [--rpc-port N] [--config <file>] [--json] [--anomalies-only]` | S-014 token-bucket rate-limiter configuration audit + posture diagnostic. Pulls the live daemon's runtime config via `determ summary --json` (covering the four S-014 rate-limit knobs that landed in `include/determ/net/rate_limiter.hpp` — per-peer-IP `rate_limit_rpc_qps`, `rate_limit_rpc_burst`, `rate_limit_gossip_qps`, `rate_limit_gossip_burst`; HELLO exempt per SECURITY.md §S-014); when `--config <file>` is supplied, additionally parses the on-disk config and reports the two-way diff between runtime + on-disk values (`runtime_only`, `config_only`, `mismatch` categories — surfaces operator-side config drift where the daemon was started before a config edit landed on disk). Reports per-surface: configured QPS, configured burst capacity, enabled/disabled status (per the `rate_limit_enabled` field), profile-recommended floor (cluster/web/regional/global/tactical — see PROTOCOL.md §12.3 for per-profile guidance; each profile's recommended RPC + gossip floors are encoded in the script's constants table per Determ's deployment-profile defaults). Flags anomalies: **`rate_limiter_disabled_in_hostile_deployment`** — `rate_limit_enabled == false` AND deployment-profile suggests hostile-network exposure (global / regional / web profiles; cluster/tactical permissively allowed) — S-014 closure documented operator-policy gate per SECURITY.md §S-014, **`rate_limit_below_profile_floor`** — runtime QPS or burst is below the profile-recommended minimum floor for the active profile (operator may have under-configured the limiter against the deployment's threat model), **`rate_limit_above_profile_ceiling`** — runtime QPS or burst exceeds the profile-recommended ceiling (over-provisioned bucket effectively disables the limiter — flag for review), **`config_runtime_drift`** — `--config` was supplied AND values differ between runtime + on-disk (operator restarted before a config edit landed, or a runtime override is silently overriding the on-disk policy). `--anomalies-only` suppresses healthy-state rows; pair with `--json` for monitoring-system ingestion. Default human output is a per-surface table (RPC + gossip rows; each with configured QPS / burst / status / profile-floor / profile-ceiling columns) + summary footer (profile, enabled, anomaly count); `--json` emits `{rpc: {qps, burst, enabled, profile_floor, profile_ceiling}, gossip: {qps, burst, enabled, profile_floor, profile_ceiling}, profile, config_path?, drift?: [{surface, field, runtime, config}, …], anomalies: [...]}`. Pure read-only diagnostic — no side effects, no traffic shaping changes. Cross-references SECURITY.md §S-014 + PROTOCOL.md §12.3 for posture interpretation. **Exit codes**: 0 healthy rate-limit posture (or 0 when `--anomalies-only` AND no anomalies), 2 rate_limiter_disabled_in_hostile_deployment / rate_limit_below_profile_floor / rate_limit_above_profile_ceiling / config_runtime_drift anomaly (operator alert gate — rate-limit posture has regressed; S-014 closure assumes an enabled bucket on hostile-network deployments), 1 RPC error / unreachable daemon / config-file unreadable / bad args. |
| `tools/operator_tx_throughput.sh [--rpc-port N] [--from H] [--to H] [--last N] [--profile {cluster\|web\|regional\|global\|tactical}] [--expected-tps N] [--json] [--anomalies-only]` | TPS (transactions-per-second) measurement over a block window. Walks block range `[from, to]` (default: last 1000 blocks via `head --json` → `[head-1000, head]`; `--last N` shorthand for `[head-N, head]`) and computes throughput across the window: total tx count, total elapsed wall-time (max `block.timestamp` − min `block.timestamp`), tx-rate (`tx_count / elapsed_seconds`), per-block average tx count, per-block peak / median / p95 tx count. Per-tx-type breakdown: TRANSFER, STAKE, UNSTAKE, DEREGISTER, REGISTER, PARAM_CHANGE, DAPP_REGISTER, DAPP_CALL, DAPP_DEREGISTER — each emitting its own count + percentage-of-total. Per-profile expected-TPS comparison: each timing profile (`cluster` 50/50/25, `web` 100/100/50, `regional` 300/300/150, `global` 600/600/300, `tactical` 20/20/10 — see PROTOCOL.md §12.3) implies a different theoretical TPS ceiling under maximum block utilization (`MAX_BLOCK_TXS / round_time_ms × 1000`); the script reports observed-vs-expected as a percentage utilization. Optional `--expected-tps N` override pins the comparison floor for custom-tuned deployments. Flags anomalies: **`tps_underperformance`** (observed TPS < 50% of profile-expected — capacity gap signal, may indicate network congestion / mempool starvation / committee-selection bottleneck), **`tps_burst_overload`** (≥1 block with tx-count == MAX_BLOCK_TXS — block-size cap hit, mempool overflow risk per S-008), **`block_timestamp_skew`** (negative or zero elapsed time across the window — Block.timestamp monotonicity violation per Preliminaries V14), **`empty_block_run`** (≥10 consecutive empty blocks in the window — censorship-resistance signal per FA2 OR genuine no-tx-activity). Default mode: 1-line digest (`TPS [H1, H2]: tx_count=N elapsed=Xs rate=Y/s peak_block=Z utilization=W% anomalies=N`); `--json` emits the full structured envelope (`{from, to, tx_count, elapsed_seconds, tps_observed, tps_expected, utilization_pct, by_type: {...}, per_block: {avg, peak, median, p95}, anomalies: [...]}`). **Exit codes**: 0 healthy throughput (or 0 when `--anomalies-only` AND no anomalies), 2 anomalies present (operator alert gate — capacity gap / cap-hit / timestamp skew / empty-block run), 1 RPC error / bad args. |
| `tools/operator_consensus_lag.sh --rpc-ports P1,P2,... [--threshold N] [--json]` | Multi-node consensus-lag detector. Polls every supplied node's `status.height` via `determ status --rpc-port P --field height` and computes the max height across peers, then the per-peer lag (`max − peer_height`). Marks peers lagging more than `--threshold N` blocks (default 3) as STRAGGLERS. Unreachable peers (RPC connection refused, daemon down) are treated as max-lag stragglers (lag = max_height) and flagged as unreachable in both human and JSON output. Default human output is a per-peer table (port / height / lag / status columns) + `[OK]` / `[ALERT]` summary line; `--json` emits `{max_height, peers: [{port, height, lag, straggler, reachable}, …], stragglers: [P,…], ok, threshold}`. **Exit codes**: 0 no stragglers, 1 ≥1 straggler OR bad args. Operator monitoring tool — detects silent partitions, slow validators, or daemon hangs before they trigger BFT escalation gates downstream. Pair with `operator_chain_health.sh` for per-node health + multi-node lag in one operator pass. |
| `tools/operator_dapp_inventory.sh --rpc-port N [--message-window N] [--json]` | DApp registry enumeration + recent-activity summary. Enumerates all registered DApps via `determ dapp-list --json`, then for each fetches `dapp-info` (service_pubkey, endpoint_url, registered_at) and `dapp-messages` over a windowed range `[height - --message-window + 1, height + 1)` (default window 100 blocks) to count recent messages per DApp. Reports per-DApp: domain, service_pubkey hex (32B), endpoint URL, registered_block, recent_messages count, status (active/inactive). Sorted ascending by `(registered_block, domain)` for stable ordering. The `dapp_messages` RPC is page-capped at 256 events server-side; the operator script surfaces a `recent_truncated` flag in both modes when a DApp's recent count hits the cap (operator should narrow `--message-window` or use `operator_dapp_message_audit.sh` for deeper analysis). Default human output: `DApp inventory at chain height N` header + per-DApp section + summary count; `--json` emits `{chain_height: N, message_window: W, dapps: [{domain, service_pubkey, endpoint_url, registered_block, recent_message_count, recent_truncated}, …]}`. **Exit codes**: 0 success (incl. zero DApps), 1 RPC error / unreachable daemon / bad args. Operator inventory tool — pre-flight check before governance-batch DAPP_DEREGISTER, or routine ops auditing of the registered-DApp surface. |
| `tools/operator_dapp_census.sh --rpc-port N [--json] [--anomalies-only]` | DApp registry **ownership-audit** inventory (D4 R40) — the ownership-integrity complement to `operator_dapp_inventory.sh` (which summarizes registration + recent-activity). Enumerates all registered DApps via `determ dapp-list --json`, fetches each DApp's `dapp-info` (owner / service_pubkey / endpoint_url / registered_at / active), and cross-references each DApp's owning domain against the live validator / active-stake set (`determ validators --json` + `determ stakes --json`) to flag **orphaned ownership** — a DApp whose owner domain is no longer a registered/active validator (the owner deregistered or was slashed while the DApp entry persists). Reports per-DApp: domain, owner, owner_is_live (yes/no), service_pubkey, registered_block, status. Anomalies: `orphaned_ownership` (DApp owner absent from the live validator set — governance-attention signal: the DApp has no accountable on-chain owner), and the inventory summary (total DApps, orphaned count, active/inactive split). `--anomalies-only` suppresses healthy-state output; pair with `--json` for monitoring-system ingestion. Distinct from `operator_dapp_inventory.sh` (activity-focused) — `operator_dapp_census.sh` is governance-focused: which DApps still have a live, accountable owner. **Exit codes**: 0 healthy census (or 0 when `--anomalies-only` AND no orphans), 2 orphaned ownership detected (operator alert gate), 1 RPC error / unreachable daemon / bad args. Exercised by `tools/test_operator_dapp_census.sh` (cluster-bound). |
| `tools/operator_receipt_flow.sh --rpc-port N [--peer-ports P1,P2,…] [--imbalance-tolerance N] [--json]` | Cross-shard **receipt-flow audit** (E4 R40) — the operational view of the FA7 cross-shard-atomicity invariant + the `CrossShardSupplyConservation.md` (FA-Apply-17) K-shard supply identity. Unlike the three single-port block-walk siblings (`operator_receipt_audit.sh` per-shard volume + dedup, `operator_inbound_outbound_balance.sh` net-flow trend, `operator_cross_shard_health.sh` pending-pool + apply-lag), this is the only **counter-driven, multi-daemon** flow audit: it reads the A1 supply counters directly (two light RPC calls per shard — `determ status --json` for `shard_id` / `pending_inbound_receipts` / `sharding_mode`, and `determ supply --json` / `chain_summary` for `accumulated_inbound` / `accumulated_outbound`) instead of walking thousands of blocks. Single-port mode reports this shard's outbound-emitted + inbound-applied totals + in-flight estimate; `--peer-ports` builds the per-shard-pair flow matrix and runs the K-shard supply-identity gate `Σ_outbound == Σ_inbound + in-flight`, flagging `Σ_in > Σ_out` (potential double-credit — FA7 should make this impossible) and pure imbalance. `--imbalance-tolerance` suppresses sub-threshold noise; `--json` for monitoring ingestion. All fan-out + aggregation runs in one Python pass with an 8s per-RPC subprocess timeout, so it cannot block regardless of `--peer-ports` count or a hung daemon. **Exit codes**: 0 balanced (or within tolerance) / 2 imbalance detected (operator alert gate) / 1 RPC error / unreachable daemon / duplicate shard_id / bad args. Exercised by `tools/test_operator_receipt_flow.sh` (node-free arg-surface smoke). |
| `tools/operator_receipt_proof_audit.sh [--rpc-port N] [--json] [--from H] [--to H] [--max-receipts N] [--anomalies-only]` | Read-only **inbound-receipt proof audit** — the composite-key proof-AUDIT companion to `operator_receipt_audit.sh` (volume/flow) and `operator_receipt_flow.sh` (A1 counters). Walks a window of finalized blocks (default last 500; `--from/--to` overrides) via `determ block-info --json`, reads each block's `inbound_receipts[]` (src_shard, tx_hash), and for every applied receipt issues a `determ state-proof --ns i --key <hex>` against the composite-key `i:` (applied_inbound_receipts) namespace — building the hex body `u64_be(src_shard) ‖ tx_hash[32]` exactly as `node.cpp::rpc_state_proof` expects (caller hex-encodes the binary key body). Each receipt is classed PROVABLE only when the proof is present AND (a) `key_bytes == "i:" ‖ src_be8 ‖ tx_hash` (binds the proof to THIS leaf), (b) `value_hash == SHA256(0x01)` (the presence marker, `4bf5122f…459a`), (c) `target_index` in `[0, leaf_count)`, and (d) the proof's `state_root` matches the audit-anchor root; otherwise NOT_PROVABLE (state_proof not_found for a receipt the body claims was applied — applied-set vs state-tree divergence), MISBOUND (proof binds a different leaf), or STALE_ROOT (proof root drift). `--max-receipts` (default 2000; 0 = no cap) bounds the RPC fan-out. Issues only `status` / `head` / `block-info` / `state_proof` (never a mutating RPC). Single-shard daemons (`sharding_mode == none`) and empty chains exit 0 with an INFO line. Mirrors the three bindings `determ-light verify-receipt-inclusion` checks before rolling the Merkle path (see `docs/proofs/ReceiptInclusionProofSoundness.md`), so a PROVABLE verdict is a strong precondition for a downstream INCLUDED verdict. `--json` emits a `{receipts_seen, receipts_checked, provable, not_provable, misbound, stale_root, failures:[…]}` envelope for monitoring ingestion. **Exit codes**: 0 success / informational (or single-shard deployment), 2 `--anomalies-only` AND ≥1 of `receipt_not_provable` / `receipt_misbound` / `stale_proof_root` fired (operator alert gate), 1 RPC error / unreachable daemon / malformed response / bad args. |
| `tools/operator_receipt_settlement_latency.sh --rpc-port N [--peer-ports P1,P2,…] [--from H] [--to H] [--last N] [--settle-budget-slack N] [--peer-scan-cap N] [--block-timeout S] [--json] [--anomalies-only]` | Cross-shard receipt **settlement-latency profiler** — the only operator tool that JOINS the local (source) shard's emitted `cross_shard_receipts[]` to the destination shards' `inbound_receipts[]` on the `(src_shard, src_block_index, tx_hash)` apply-dedup key (`src/chain/block.cpp::CrossShardReceipt`), so it measures the per-receipt round-trip **settlement latency** = `apply_block_index − src_block_index` rather than the count-aggregate views of its siblings (`operator_cross_shard_health.sh` pending-pool + emit/apply counts, `operator_receipt_flow.sh` fleet A1-counter balance, `operator_receipt_audit.sh` per-shard dedup forensics). `--rpc-port` is the LOCAL source daemon; `--peer-ports` enumerates the DESTINATION shards' RPC ports (each walked genesis-to-tip, capped by `--peer-scan-cap` default 2000). Reports the settled-latency distribution (min / p50 / p95 / max / mean blocks), a per-destination-shard breakdown, and the roster of emitted-but-unsettled receipts. Settlement budget = `CROSS_SHARD_RECEIPT_LATENCY (3, src/node/node.cpp) + --settle-budget-slack` (default 20). Anomalies: **`receipts_unsettled_overdue`** (emitted receipt still UNSETTLED past budget on the most-advanced queried destination tip — stalled/aborting destination producer or lost gossip bundle), **`settlement_latency_high`** (settled receipt's round-trip latency exceeds budget — slow settlement), **`settled_before_emit`** (NEGATIVE latency, apply before emit — mismatched-chain / index-corruption; catastrophic). Issues only read-only RPCs (`status`, `head --field height`, `block-info`) — never a mutating endpoint; single bounded pass with per-`block-info` `--block-timeout`, no node spawning / no `--watch`. Short-circuits to an INFO line + exit 0 on `sharding_mode == "none"` or an empty chain. `--json` for monitoring ingestion. **Exit codes**: 0 healthy (or single-shard / informational mode), 2 `--anomalies-only` AND ≥1 anomaly fired (operator alert gate), 1 RPC error / unreachable daemon / malformed response / bad args. Verified node-free (`--help` + arg-guards + empty-chain / single-shard branches). |
| `tools/operator_pending_param_proof_audit.sh [--rpc-port N] [--json] [--at-height H] [--max-entries N] [--anomalies-only]` | Read-only **pending-param proof audit** — the `p:`-namespace member of the composite-key proof-audit trilogy alongside `operator_receipt_proof_audit.sh` (`i:` applied_inbound_receipts) and `operator_merge_audit.sh` (`m:` merge_state). Answers the governance light-client question: for each PARAM_CHANGE the chain claims it has STAGED (it will mutate a named constant at a future `effective_height`), can the daemon produce a Merkle inclusion proof binding `(effective_height, idx)` AND the scheduled `(name, value)` to the committee-signed `state_root`? Pulls the staged list via `determ pending-params --json` (ordered by `effective_height` ascending; `pending_param_changes_` is a `std::map`), assigns each entry its 0-based position `idx` WITHIN its `effective_height` bucket (insertion = apply order, matching `build_state_leaves`), and issues `determ state-proof --ns p --key <hex>` with hex body `u64_be(effective_height) ‖ u32_be(idx)` (12B; daemon prepends `p:`). Each entry is PROVABLE only when (a) `key_bytes == "p:" ‖ eff_be8 ‖ idx_be4` (binds THIS leaf), (b) `value_hash == SHA256(u64_be(len(name)) ‖ name ‖ u64_be(len(value)) ‖ value)` recomputed from the RPC-reported `(name, value_hex)` — a deeper bind than the `i:` presence marker since the `p:` leaf carries a real payload, so the proof commits to the EXACT scheduled mutation — (c) `target_index` in `[0, leaf_count)`, and (d) the proof `state_root` matches the audit-anchor root; otherwise NOT_PROVABLE (pending_params claims it staged but state_proof returns not_found — governance-projection vs state-tree divergence), MISBOUND (proof binds a different leaf or a different scheduled value), or STALE_ROOT. Also cross-checks `status`'s `pending_param_changes` count against the `pending_params` list length (`count_mismatch`). `--at-height H` proof-checks only entries with `effective_height <= H` (idx still computed over the full bucket); `--max-entries` (default 2000; 0 = no cap) bounds the RPC fan-out. Issues only `status` / `head` / `pending-params` / `state-proof` (never a mutating RPC); nothing-staged exits 0 with an INFO line. `--json` emits a `{total_staged, status_count, entries_seen, entries_checked, provable, not_provable, misbound, stale_root, failures:[…]}` envelope. **Exit codes**: 0 success / informational (or nothing staged), 2 `--anomalies-only` AND ≥1 of `pending_not_provable` / `pending_misbound` / `stale_proof_root` / `count_mismatch` fired (operator alert gate), 1 RPC error / unreachable daemon / malformed response / bad args. |
| `tools/operator_effective_param_audit.sh [--rpc-port N] [--expect NAME=VALUE ...] [--json] [--anomalies-only]` | Trustlessly audits the CURRENT EFFECTIVE value of each governance-activatable consensus scalar against the committee-signed `k:` namespace state_root — the activated-value end of the PARAM_CHANGE lifecycle, distinct from `operator_pending_param_proof_audit.sh` (which proves the PENDING `p:` staged changes) and from the RPC-posture / historical-log siblings (`operator_governance_audit.sh`, `operator_governance_history.sh`, `operator_param_history.sh`, `operator_param_change_history.sh`). Read-only: issues only `state-root`, `state-proof --ns k`, and `pending-params` (never a mutating RPC). Splits the validator whitelist (`src/node/validator.cpp::kWhitelist`) into PROVABLE (`MIN_STAKE`/`SUSPENSION_SLASH`/`UNSTAKE_DELAY` — per-Chain scalars `min_stake_`/`suspension_slash_`/`unstake_delay_` set by `activate_pending_params` and committed as `k:` `const_leaf`s `min_stake`/`suspension_slash`/`unstake_delay`) vs HOOK_ONLY (`bft_escalation_threshold`/`tx_commit_ms`/`block_sig_ms`/`abort_claim_ms`/`param_keyholders`/`param_threshold` — forwarded to the Node hook / `params.hpp` constants, no `k:` leaf, not state-root-provable). Per PROVABLE scalar: fetches `state-proof --ns k --key <leaf>`, recomputes the `const_leaf` value_hash `SHA256(be8(expected))` (big-endian per `SHA256Builder::append(uint64_t)`) from `--expect NAME=VALUE`, and asserts `key_bytes == "k:"+leaf` AND `value_hash == SHA256(be8(expected))` AND `target_index in [0,leaf_count)` AND proof state_root == the anchor captured at start (stale-snapshot guard). Verdicts: VERIFIED / MISMATCH / NOT_PROVABLE / UNCHECKED (no `--expect`; SHA-256 is one-way so the proof binds SOME value but the audit can't assert WHICH); HOOK_ONLY scalars report NOT_APPLICABLE. Each scalar's staged future change is surfaced inline from `pending-params` (`pending_change` with effective_height + decoded value). `--anomalies-only` suppresses the per-scalar table; `--json` emits `{rpc_port, height, state_root, scalars:[...], anomalies:[...], summary:{provable,verified,mismatch,not_provable,unchecked,hook_only,pending_total,anomaly_count}}`. **Exit codes**: 0 audit completed; every checked scalar VERIFIED (or informational), 2 >=1 MISMATCH / NOT_PROVABLE / stale-proof-root anomaly (operator alert gate), 1 RPC error / unreachable daemon / malformed response / bad args. Verified node-free (`--help` + arg-rejection smoke). |
| `tools/operator_dapp_registry_proof_audit.sh [--rpc-port N] [--json] [--prefix P] [--topic T] [--max-dapps N] [--anomalies-only]` | Read-only **DApp-registry proof audit** — the simple-key `d:`-namespace member of the trustless proof-audit family, completing it across the application registry alongside the composite-key proof-audit trilogy (`operator_receipt_proof_audit.sh` `i:` applied_inbound_receipts, `operator_merge_audit.sh` `m:` merge_state, `operator_pending_param_proof_audit.sh` `p:` pending_param_changes). Answers the v2.18 DApp light-client question: for each DApp the chain claims it has REGISTERED (the `d:`-namespace registry leaf the V2-DAPP-DESIGN.md light-client read path resolves), can the daemon produce a Merkle inclusion proof binding the owning domain (`d:` key) AND the entry's canonical fields to the committee-signed `state_root`? Enumerates the registry via `determ dapp-list --json` (server-side `--prefix` / `--topic` filters), then for each domain fetches the FULL entry via `determ dapp-info --domain <D>` (the compact dapp-list row omits `service_pubkey` / `retention` / `metadata` / `registered_at`), recomputes the canonical `d:` value_hash `SHA256(service_pubkey[32] ‖ u64_be(registered_at) ‖ u64_be(active_from) ‖ u64_be(inactive_from) ‖ u64_be(len(endpoint_url)) ‖ endpoint_url ‖ u64_be(len(topics)) ‖ per-topic(u64_be(len(t)) ‖ t) ‖ u64_be(retention) ‖ u64_be(len(metadata)) ‖ metadata)` exactly as `src/chain/chain.cpp::build_state_leaves` emits it (`SHA256Builder::append(uint64_t)` big-endian; retention u8 promoted to u64), and issues `determ state-proof --ns d --key <domain>` (simple-key raw domain — the daemon prepends `d:`, unlike the i:/m:/p: hex bodies). Each DApp is PROVABLE only when (a) `key_bytes == "d:" ‖ domain` (binds THIS domain), (b) `value_hash` equals the recomputed canonical hash (a deeper bind than the `i:` presence marker since the `d:` leaf carries a real multi-field payload — the proof commits to the EXACT registry entry), (c) `target_index` in `[0, leaf_count)`, and (d) the proof `state_root` matches the audit-anchor root; otherwise NOT_PROVABLE (dapp_list claims it registered but state_proof returns not_found, or dapp_info itself no longer resolves it — registry-projection vs state-tree divergence), MISBOUND (proof binds a different leaf or a different entry), or STALE_ROOT. Also cross-checks `dapp-list`'s `count` against its `dapps` array length (`count_mismatch`). `--max-dapps` (default 2000; 0 = no cap) bounds the RPC fan-out. Issues only `head` / `dapp-list` / `dapp-info` / `state-proof` (never a mutating RPC); no registered DApps in scope exits 0 with an INFO line. `--json` emits a `{filter, total_registered, list_count, dapps_seen, dapps_checked, provable, not_provable, misbound, stale_root, state_root, height, failures:[…], anomalies:[…]}` envelope. **Exit codes**: 0 success / informational (or no registered DApps), 2 `--anomalies-only` AND ≥1 of `dapp_not_provable` / `dapp_misbound` / `stale_proof_root` / `count_mismatch` fired (operator alert gate), 1 RPC error / unreachable daemon / malformed response / bad args. Verified node-free (`--help` + arg-guards + value-hash/key encoding). |
| `tools/operator_committee_audit.sh --rpc-port N [--from H] [--to H] [--last N] [--bias-threshold F] [--json] [--anomalies-only]` | Per-validator committee selection fairness audit over a block window. Walks block range (default last 1000 blocks; `--from H --to H` overrides; `--last N` shorthand) via `determ block-info N --json` to extract `creators[]` per block; cross-references `determ validators --json` for per-validator stake. Computes per-validator: blocks-selected count, observed-share = count / (window_blocks × K), expected-share = stake_i / total_stake, deviation = (observed - expected) / expected. Modal K over the window is used as the per-block committee-size baseline (matches `operator_block_creator_fairness.sh` convention; BFT-degraded blocks don't distort). Per-validator `position_distribution[]` (length K) tallies which slot indices each validator occupied — exposes proposer-slot vs trailing-slot bias for forensic drill-down. Anomalies: `committee_bias_high` (any \|deviation\| > `--bias-threshold` default 0.30), `validator_excluded` (registered validator with non-zero stake never selected — potential exclusion bug or stake-weight underflow), `validator_dominant` (single validator selected in > 50% of blocks — centralization signal). Special handling for zero-stake validators: deviation = +inf (JSON string `"+inf"` since vanilla JSON has no IEEE inf); never flagged as biased if also zero-observed. Default human output is ranked-by-deviation table (worst first) + summary footer; `--json` emits `{window: {from, to, block_count, K}, validators: [{domain, stake, blocks_selected, observed_share, expected_share, deviation, position_distribution, biased}], summary: {max_deviation, n_biased, n_total}, anomalies: [...]}`. **Exit codes**: 0 healthy (or 0 when `--anomalies-only` AND no anomalies), 2 anomalies present (operator alert gate — committee-selection drift can mask Sybil concentration or stake-weighting bugs), 1 RPC error / bad args. |
