| `tools/operator_anon_address_density.sh [--rpc-port N] [--from H] [--to H] [--bucket-blocks N] [--json] [--anomalies-only]` | Anon-address vs domain density audit over time-bucketed windows. Walks the block range (default last 1000 blocks via `head - 999 .. head`; `--from H --to H` overrides) via `determ block-info <h> --json`; for each TRANSFER tx classifies sender + receiver as anon (matches `^0x[a-f0-9]{64}$` per S-028 canonical lowercase form) or domain (everything else); partitions into `--bucket-blocks N`-wide buckets (default 100, clamped to window size). Per bucket: counts of {anon→anon, anon→domain, domain→anon, domain→domain} + anon-touching ratio (transfers with at least one anon side / total transfers). Window-wide: window totals + least-squares trend regression slope on the anon-touching ratio across non-empty buckets (positive slope = trend toward more anonymity; negative = trend toward less). Anomalies: **`anon_density_spike`** (any bucket's anon-touching ratio > 0.80 AND > 2× window-median bucket ratio — bulk-anonymity-event signal worth review), **`domain_density_collapse`** (any bucket's domain-to-domain ratio < 0.10 where window median > 0.30 — sudden anonymity-only window), **`trend_slope_high`** (\|trend slope\| > 0.20 across buckets — sustained directional density shift). `--anomalies-only` suppresses healthy-state rows; pair with `--json` for monitoring-system ingestion. Default human output is a per-bucket table (bucket-range + 4 counter columns + ratio) + trend slope summary + summary footer (window range, bucket count, totals, anon-touching pct, anomaly count); `--json` emits `{window: {from,to}, bucket_blocks, buckets: [{from, to, anon_to_anon, anon_to_domain, domain_to_anon, domain_to_domain, anon_touching_pct}, ...], trend: {slope, intercept}, summary: {totals}, anomalies: [...]}`. **Exit codes**: 0 healthy (or 0 when `--anomalies-only` AND no anomalies), 2 anomaly present (operator alert gate — privacy-pattern shift signal), 1 RPC error / unreachable daemon / bad args. |
| `tools/operator_anon_canonicalization_audit.sh [--rpc-port N] [--json] [--from H] [--to H] [--probe-sample N] [--anomalies-only]` | Read-only S-028 anon-address canonicalization + account-lifecycle conformance audit. Issues only read RPCs (`head`, `snapshot create`, `block-info`, `balance`, `nonce`, `stake_info` — never a mutating RPC). Audits two invariants on a running daemon: (A) **stored-form canonicality** — every anon-shaped form persisted in state (accounts_/stakes_ store-keys from `snapshot create`, plus tx.from/tx.to and inbound_receipt.to endpoints across `[from, to]` via `block-info --json`; default last 1000 blocks) must be canonical lowercase (`0x` + 64 lowercase hex per `normalize_anon_address`); any anon-shaped form carrying an uppercase hex digit is a violation because two case spellings would split one logical account across two keys. (B) **live RPC normalization** — for a deterministic sample (default 25, `--probe-sample N`) it re-queries `balance` / `nonce` / `stake_info` with both the lowercase spelling and a synthesized all-uppercase spelling and asserts identical `balance` / `next_nonce` / `locked` values plus a canonical lowercase echoed `domain` field (S-028 G-2 normalize-at-input contract in `src/node/node.cpp`). Also classifies anon accounts as `credit_only` (auto-created on first credit: `next_nonce == 0` AND never a tx.from in the window) vs `active`. Anomaly flags: `noncanonical_stored_key` (≥1 non-canonical anon-shaped stored key/endpoint), `live_normalization_drift` (≥1 sampled address diverged across case spellings or echoed a non-canonical domain), `credit_only_share_high` (credit_only > 70% of anon accounts). Default human output prints lifecycle split, canonicality verdict, and probe results; `--json` emits `{window, distinct_anon, lifecycle, canonicality, live_probe, anomalies, …}`; `--anomalies-only` prints only fired flags. **Exit codes**: 0 success (or informational), 2 `--anomalies-only` AND ≥1 anomaly fired, 1 RPC error / bad args / malformed response. |
| `tools/operator_account_age_distribution.sh [--rpc-port N] [--max-walk-blocks N] [--bucket-size-blocks N] [--json] [--anomalies-only]` | Account-age bucketed distribution audit for state-bloat analysis. Pulls live chain state via `determ chain-summary --json` for the head height; for each account in current state, walks the block range `[max(0, H - max_walk_blocks), H]` via `block-info <h> --json` looking for the FIRST block where the account appears (TRANSFER recipient, REGISTER/DEREGISTER actor, inbound receipt destination, DAPP_REGISTER/DAPP_CALL actor or recipient, per-creator subsidy distribution) to infer creation block. Accounts never seen in the walk window bucket as "older than --max-walk-blocks". Buckets by age (head - creation_block) into fixed-width buckets (default 1000 blocks); reports per-bucket count + max-balance + total-balance + mean-balance. Window-wide summary: median age, p90 age, p99 age, oldest-known-account block, long-tail fraction (fraction older than 50% of chain age). Anomalies: **`recent_account_burst`** (> 100 accounts created in last 100 blocks — Sybil-onboarding burst signal; cross-references operator_stake_concentration.sh + operator_payments_audit.sh for drill-in), **`account_state_bloat`** (total > 10000 AND > 50% have zero balance + zero nonce — dust-residue accumulation worth review for state-prune candidate identification), **`historical_account_dominance`** (> 80% older than walk window — recommend re-running with larger --max-walk-blocks for precise ages on those). `--anomalies-only` suppresses healthy-state rows; pair with `--json` for monitoring-system ingestion. Default human output is per-bucket histogram table + summary stats + summary footer (chain height, total accounts, median age, p90 age, p99 age, long-tail fraction, anomaly count); `--json` emits `{rpc_port, chain_height, max_walk_blocks, bucket_size_blocks, buckets: [{age_low, age_high, count, total_balance, mean_balance}, ...], summary: {total_accounts, median_age, p90_age, p99_age, oldest_known, long_tail_fraction}, anomalies: [...]}`. **Exit codes**: 0 healthy (or 0 when `--anomalies-only` AND no anomalies), 2 anomaly present (operator alert gate — state-bloat / Sybil-burst signal), 1 RPC error / unreachable daemon / bad args. |
| `tools/operator_chain_invariants_audit.sh [--rpc-port N] [--from H] [--to H] [--stride N] [--json] [--anomalies-only]` | RPC-level chain-integrity audit — operator-side equivalent of in-process tests for the chain-integrity invariants. Walks the block range (default last 1000 blocks via `head-999..head`; `--from H --to H` overrides; `--stride N` default 100 for ranges >100, else 1) via `determ block-info <h> --json` and audits five invariants per sampled block: (A) prev_hash chain link (each block's `prev_hash` field equals the prior block's `block_hash` — explicit h-1 fetch when stride>1), (B) state_root presence on recent blocks within last 100 (S-038 regression signal — recent blocks should have non-empty state_root post-S-038 wiring), (C) head_hash consistency (`chain-summary --json` head_block_hash matches last block's `block_hash` field), (D) inter-block timestamp monotonicity (advisory — not enforced at chain layer but anomalous regressions worth flagging), (E) per-block tx_hash uniqueness via jq. Anomalies: **`prev_hash_chain_broken`** (CATASTROPHIC, MAX severity — chain integrity broken), **`head_hash_mismatch`** (chain inconsistency), **`state_root_missing_recent`** (S-038 closure regression signal), **`timestamp_regression`** (advisory — chain layer doesn't enforce monotonicity but worth alerting). `--anomalies-only` suppresses healthy-state rows; pair with `--json` for monitoring-system ingestion. Default human output is per-sample-block status + summary footer (window range, blocks sampled, anomaly count by category); `--json` emits `{window: {from,to,stride}, sampled_blocks: N, samples: [{height, prev_hash_ok, state_root_present, timestamp_ok}, ...], head_hash_match, anomalies: [...]}`. **Exit codes**: 0 healthy, 2 prev_hash_chain_broken OR head_hash_mismatch (MAX-severity operator alert gate — chain integrity broken), 1 other anomalies / args / RPC error. Distinct from `operator_replay_validation.sh` (which does state_root replay + counter consistency at the snapshot layer): `chain_invariants_audit` is the multi-invariant RPC-level audit. |
| `tools/operator_signature_audit.sh [--rpc-port N] [--from H] [--to H] [--last N] [--validator <domain>] [--json] [--anomalies-only]` | K-of-K committee signature distribution audit + BFT-mode detection over a block window. Walks block range (default last 1000 blocks via `head-999..head`; overridable via `--from`/`--to`/`--last`) pulling per-block `creators[]` + `creator_block_sigs[]` (parallel array) via `determ block-info <h> --json`. The all-zero 128-hex sig (`"0".repeat(128)`, case-insensitive) is the sentinel for "didn't sign". Per-validator aggregates: `selections` (count in creators[]), `valid_sigs` (non-sentinel sig count in their slot), `missing_sigs = selections - valid_sigs`, `miss_rate = missing_sigs / selections`, longest consecutive-missed `streak`. Window-wide: total blocks, total sig slots, total valid sigs, sig-fill ratio = valid / total. Per-block classification: K-mode (sigs == K), BFT-mode (Q ≤ sigs < K where Q = `ceil(2·ceil(2K/3)/3)` per PROTOCOL.md §5.3), or sub-quorum/empty. Anomalies: **`validator_consistent_missing`** (any validator's miss_rate > 0.30 — chronic-downtime signal), **`bft_mode_dominant`** (> 50% of blocks in BFT-mode — cluster-health escalation signal; K-of-K should be steady-state), **`sig_fill_ratio_low`** (total_valid / total_slots < 0.80 — chronic committee-participation gap), **`validator_missing_streak`** (any consecutive-missed streak > 10 — sustained downtime). `--validator <domain>` filters by_validator output (cosmetic; anomalies + summary still computed across full population); `--anomalies-only` suppresses healthy-state rows; pair with `--json` for monitoring-system ingestion. Default human output is per-validator table sorted by miss_rate descending + window-wide stats + summary footer (window range, total blocks, sig-fill ratio, K-mode vs BFT-mode counts, anomaly count); `--json` emits `{window: {from,to}, by_validator: [{domain, selections, valid_sigs, missing_sigs, miss_rate, max_streak}, ...], summary: {total_blocks, total_slots, total_valid, sig_fill_ratio, k_mode_blocks, bft_mode_blocks}, anomalies: [...]}`. **Exit codes**: 0 healthy, 2 anomaly present (operator alert gate — sustained sig drift), 1 RPC error / unreachable daemon / bad args. |
| `tools/operator_governance_history.sh [--rpc-port N] [--from H] [--to H] [--last N] [--json] [--anomalies-only]` | Governance event timeline aggregator. Walks the block range (default last 5000 blocks via `head-4999..head`; `--from H --to H` overrides; `--last N` shorthand) via `determ block-info <h> --json` filtering for the three governance-relevant tx types: `PARAM_CHANGE` (type 6 — protocol-parameter mutation via A5 keyholder threshold), `DEREGISTER` (type 4 — validator opt-out of consensus participation), `REGISTER` (type 2 — validator opt-in to consensus participation). Distinct from `operator_param_change_history.sh` (which focuses solely on PARAM_CHANGE with per-key decoding): `governance_history.sh` is the consolidated three-axis timeline that captures the full governance surface in chronological order. Per-event: block_index, type, actor (tx.from), payload-summary (per-tx-type — for PARAM_CHANGE the decoded key=value pair, for DEREGISTER the unlock_height window, for REGISTER the `active_from` randomized-delay range), tx_hash. Cross-references the live validator set via `determ validators --json` to attribute REGISTER / DEREGISTER events to currently-active vs already-deactivated validators. Computes rate metrics across the window: PARAM_CHANGEs per 1000 blocks, DEREGISTER rate, REGISTER rate, net validator-set churn (registers - deregisters in window). Anomalies: **`high_param_change_rate`** (> 5 PARAM_CHANGEs per 1000 blocks — governance over-activity signal worth review for keyholder-set compromise or coordinated attack), **`mass_deregister_burst`** (> 10 DEREGISTERs in any 100-block sub-window — validator-exodus signal worth review for chain-health concern), **`mass_register_burst`** (> 10 REGISTERs in any 100-block sub-window — Sybil-onboarding pattern signal worth review against the S-010/S-011 stake-pricing floor), **`negative_net_churn_high`** (net = registers - deregisters < -20 across the full window — sustained validator-set shrinkage worth review). `--anomalies-only` suppresses healthy-state rows; pair with `--json` for monitoring-system ingestion. Default human output is a chronological event-table (oldest first) + rate metrics summary + summary footer (window range, total events, per-type counts, net churn, anomaly count); `--json` emits `{window: {from,to}, events: [{block_index, type, actor, payload, tx_hash}, …], rates: {param_change_per_1k, deregister_per_1k, register_per_1k, net_churn}, summary: {total_events, by_type}, anomalies: [...]}`. **Exit codes**: 0 healthy (or 0 when `--anomalies-only` AND no anomalies), 2 anomaly present (operator alert gate — governance-event rate spikes are early signals for chain-health concern), 1 RPC error / unreachable daemon / bad args. |
| `tools/operator_snapshot_diff_report.sh --from <file-a> --to <file-b> [--group {all\|counters\|state\|accounts\|stakes\|registrants\|params}] [--account-detail] [--json]` | Grouped field-level snapshot diff with anomaly detection. Builds on `determ snapshot diff --json` + `determ snapshot inspect --json` for both files; groups differences by domain (state-roots / counters / accounts-set / stakes-set / registrants-set / params); computes per-group summary (added / removed / modified counts for set fields; numeric deltas for counters). Default `--group all`; can narrow to a single domain. `--account-detail` emits per-changed-account `[+] / [-] / [~]` balance-delta lines for forensic drill-down. Reports `block_index_delta` between the two snapshots. Anomalies: `negative_block_index_delta` (snapshot B older than A — operator swapped args), `supply_drift_during_diff` (accumulated_inbound / accumulated_outbound increased without account changes — data-integrity concern), `state_root_unchanged_but_accounts_changed` (sanity check — fires only if state_root binding is broken; structurally unreachable with valid snapshots), `identical_snapshots` (informational, no escalation). Default human output is grouped sections + summary footer; `--json` emits `{from, to, block_index_delta, state, counters, accounts, stakes, registrants, params, anomalies, ...}`. **Exit codes**: 0 success / identical / informational anomaly only, 2 real anomaly (negative_delta / supply_drift / state_root_break), 1 file/binary/arg error. Operator incident-analysis tool — pair with `determ snapshot create` from two divergent nodes to localize where state diverged. |
| `tools/operator_stake_concentration.sh --rpc-port N [--gini-threshold F] [--top-n-concentration F] [--skip-snapshot] [--json] [--anomalies-only]` | Stake-weight Gini coefficient + top-N concentration audit. Sibling to `operator_balance_distribution.sh` but for stakes rather than balances — stake concentration directly affects consensus fairness because stakes drive Fisher-Yates committee selection. Pulls validator set via `determ stakes --json` (the flat `rpc_validators` array exposing `{rank, domain, stake, active_from, region, ed_pub}`); cheaper than full-state snapshot, no zero-stake population to filter. Computes Gini `G = Σᵢ(2i−n−1)sᵢ / (n Σ sᵢ)` (O(n log n) sorted form) over the stake vector; reports top1 / top3 / top10 shares; per-decile breakdown p50 / p90 / p99 (top-10% threshold + top-1% threshold); top-20 by-stake table. Optional `--skip-snapshot` for RPC-only mode (disables `min_stake_skew` anomaly which needs the snapshot's `min_stake` field). Anomalies: **`stake_gini_high`** (G > `--gini-threshold` default 0.6 — stake distributions tend more concentrated than balances), **`top1_validator_dominant`** (top-1 share > `--top-n-concentration` default 0.50 — consensus-centralization signal), **`min_stake_skew`** (≥25% of validators at exactly `min_stake` — floor-effect Sybil signal aligned with SECURITY.md §S-011's < 1/3 cartel-resistance margin), **`total_stake_zero`** (Σ stakes == 0 — bootstrap edge case or catastrophic stake-loss event). `--anomalies-only` suppresses healthy-state rows. Default human output is top-20 stake table + Gini + decile summary + anomaly summary; `--json` emits `{total_validators, total_stake, gini, gini_threshold, top1_share, top3_share, top10_share, by_decile, top_validators, anomalies}`. **Exit codes**: 0 healthy (or 0 when `--anomalies-only` AND no anomalies), 2 anomalies present (operator alert gate — stake concentration is the upstream cause of Sybil + cartel attacks on committee selection), 1 RPC error / bad args. |
| `tools/operator_stake_distribution.sh --rpc-port N [--json]` | One-glance decentralization **health check** headlined by the **Nakamoto coefficient** (R39+3 C4) — the smallest number of top validators whose CUMULATIVE stake exceeds **1/3** of the total. This is the stake-weighted reading of the Byzantine-fault threshold: determ's K-of-K consensus is safe under f < K/3 dishonest committee members (see `docs/proofs/BFTSafety.md`, SECURITY.md §S-010/§S-011), so "how many validators must collude to control > 1/3 of the selection weight" maps directly onto the safety margin (a Nakamoto coefficient of 1 means a single validator already exceeds 1/3). Also reports the Gini coefficient (same O(n log n) sorted-form identity as `operator_balance_distribution.sh`) and a full per-validator stake table (ranked by stake DESC, ties by domain ASC). **Sibling of `operator_stake_concentration.sh`, distinguished by the Nakamoto coefficient**: the concentration tool is the **anomaly-gated audit** (Gini + top-1/3/10 + decile breakdown + min_stake floor-effect Sybil detection, with `--anomalies-only` / exit-2 alerting for cron) and does NOT compute the Nakamoto coefficient; this distribution tool is the **informational one-glance report** (no anomaly gating — exit code reflects only RPC health). Uses `> 1/3` (not `> 1/2`) as THE Nakamoto cutoff because determ's BFT safety/liveness proofs hold while dishonest weight stays below 1/3; a `> 1/2` "majority-control" coefficient is also emitted in `--json` as `nakamoto_half`. RPC deps (read-only): `determ status --json` (height + K-of-K committee size) + `determ stakes --json` (the FULL validator set — no `--top` cap, since the Gini denominator + Nakamoto accumulation need every entry). Default human output: headline Nakamoto + Gini + ranked stake table; `--json` emits `{validators, total_stake, nakamoto_coefficient, nakamoto_half, gini, …}` (`gini` is `null` when n < 2 or total_stake == 0). Exercised by `tools/test_operator_stake_distribution.sh` (22 assertions). **Exit codes**: 0 report emitted, 1 RPC error / unreachable daemon / bad args (no exit-2 anomaly gate by design — this is an informational report, not an alerting tool). |
| `tools/operator_replay_validation.sh --rpc-port N [--from H] [--to H] [--genesis-only] [--stride N] [--json] [--anomalies-only]` | Replay-determinism diagnostic for chain state integrity. Hybrid approach: (a) snapshot-create + snapshot-inspect round-trip — the inspect pipeline runs `Chain::restore_from_snapshot` which re-walks tail headers through the same `apply_block` path the producer used and recomputes `state_root` via the same `compute_state_root`, gating on the embedded head block's stored value per S-033/S-038, so this IS replay-determinism validation; (b) per-block field consistency probing on the reference daemon (block-info --field state_root + --field block_hash queried twice per height — divergence ⇒ RPC-layer non-determinism / FA1 violation); (c) genesis-pin via chain-id (probed twice + cross-checked against snapshot block-0); (d) A1 supply counter monotonicity (counters can only increase between back-to-back probes; genesis_total exact-match between snapshot + live). Window: default last 1000 blocks; `--stride N` (default 100 for ranges > 100) samples for large ranges. Anomalies: `state_root_divergence`, `block_hash_divergence`, `supply_counter_divergence`, `genesis_hash_divergence`. **Exit codes**: 0 healthy, 1 RPC/args error, 2 divergence detected (operator alert gate — replay-determinism is a load-bearing invariant for the S-030 D1 closure via S-033). Pair with `operator_snapshot_diff_report.sh` for richer field-level diff between two snapshots. |
| `tools/operator_orphan_account_scan.sh --rpc-port N [--inactive-threshold-blocks N] [--include-balance-threshold N] [--max-scan-blocks N] [--json] [--anomalies-only]` | Orphan account scan — finds anon-addresses auto-created via TRANSFER credit but with zero balance + zero stake + no recent activity. Auto-creation rule: a TRANSFER to a previously-unseen anon-address creates an entry in `accounts_[address]` with the credit amount; the address may never be touched again (typo, one-off airdrop, abandoned test fixture). These orphans accumulate in `accounts_.size()` indefinitely, consuming snapshot bandwidth + cluttering operator audits. Walks every account in `accounts_` via the daemon's full-state snapshot RPC; filters for `balance ≤ --include-balance-threshold` (default 0) + zero stake; for each candidate, walks the recent block window (default last 10000 blocks, `--max-scan-blocks 5000` bounds the scan) via `block-info` to check if the address appears anywhere as source/recipient; flags as orphan if absent. Reports orphans + creation_block (when recoverable). Anomalies: **`orphan_supply_nonzero`** (Σ orphan-held supply > 0 — funds-trapped-at-typo or test fixture leak), **`orphan_share_high`** (orphans > 50% of total accounts — gas-grief signal). Pure read-only — no mutation. Default human output is top-50 orphans by balance ascending + summary footer; `--json` emits `{rpc_port, chain_height, orphans, summary, anomalies}`. **Exit codes**: 0 healthy, 2 anomalies present, 1 RPC error / bad args. Operator hygiene tool — pre-flight check before snapshot-prune operations, or routine audit of the account-population health. |

Walks block range (default `[0..min(head_a, head_b)-1]`; `--stride N` samples; `--fields` default `block_hash,state_root` + allowed `prev_hash,timestamp`) via `determ block-info <h> --field F` queried independently on each port. Pre-walks the common tip for the silent-fork-at-tip signal (heads equal but hashes differ). Anomalies: **`block_hash_divergence`** (at any height, block_hash differs — HARD FORK), **`state_root_divergence`** (state_root differs — apply-determinism break OR HARD FORK), **`head_delta_large`** (\|head_a − head_b\| > 10 blocks — one daemon lagging), **`head_a_eq_head_b_but_hashes_differ`** (FATAL — silent fork at exactly the common tip). | `tools/operator_unstake_timeline.sh --rpc-port N --domain D [--config <path>] [--round-ms <ms>] [--json]` | Per-domain pending-UNSTAKE forecast (R39+2 B4). Answers "when will my pending UNSTAKEs become claimable?" without manually walking the chain. Queries the live registry + stake table for a single validator domain via `determ stake_info <domain>` + `determ show-account <domain> --json` + `determ head --field height`, and reports the per-domain UNSTAKE pipeline: each pending `StakeEntry.unlock_height` with `blocks_remaining = max(0, unlock_height - head_height)` and an ETA in seconds derived from the chain's `round_timer_ms`. Per the Determ UNSTAKE flow (PROTOCOL.md §3.3 + SECURITY.md §S-017), a DEREGISTER tx sets `RegistryEntry.inactive_from` to a randomized future height and `StakeEntry.unlock_height = inactive_from + unstake_delay`; once `head_height ≥ unlock_height` the locked stake is claimable via an UNSTAKE tx. **Data-model note**: each domain has at most one `StakeEntry` carrying at most one pending `unlock_height` (`UINT64_MAX` = no pending unstake / still active), so per-domain pending UNSTAKEs is in `{0, 1}` — the script presents that accurately while the list-shape output accommodates a future multi-entry model. The round-ms source for the ETA is `--config <path>` (reads the node's timing-profile triple) or `--round-ms <ms>` (direct override); absent both, the ETA is omitted and only `blocks_remaining` is reported. Default human output is a per-entry timeline table + summary; `--json` emits the structured forecast. Exercised by `tools/test_operator_unstake_timeline.sh` (27 assertions; smoke against a live cluster). **Exit codes**: 0 query succeeded, 1 RPC error / daemon unreachable / bad args / unknown domain. |
| `tools/operator_escalation_consistency.sh [--rpc-port N] [--from H] [--to H] [--last N] [--bft-only] [--json] [--anomalies-only]` | Per-block BFT-escalation legality audit over a window of finalized blocks (`status` + `block-info` RPCs). Checks five invariants against `status.k_block_sigs` (genesis K) and `status.protections.bft_enabled`: **I1** `illegal_bft_block` (BFT block while `bft_enabled == false`), **I2** `bft_committee_size_bad` (BFT block whose `len(creators) != k_bft = ceil(2K/3)`), **I3** `bft_proposer_missing` (BFT block with an empty/absent `bft_proposer` or a proposer not present in `creators[]`), **I4** `md_proposer_set` (mutual-distrust block carrying a `bft_proposer`), **I5** `sigs_below_quorum` (observed non-sentinel sigs < `required_sigs`, where `required_sigs` mirrors `src/node/producer.cpp::required_block_sigs` — `K` for MD, `ceil(2*len(creators)/3)` for BFT). `--from/--to/--last` select the window; `--bft-only` restricts to escalated blocks; `--anomalies-only` suppresses healthy-state rows; pair with `--json` for monitoring ingestion. Theme-aligned to BFT escalation + block-validation edges; distinct from `operator_committee_snapshot.sh` (single-height composition + dup check), `operator_signature_audit.sh` (sig-fill ratios + K/BFT bucket counts), and `operator_block_inclusion_audit.sh` (bft_proposer concentration) — none validate per-block escalation legality across a window. **Exit codes**: 0 ok, 1 RPC-or-arg error, 2 violation under `--anomalies-only` (operator alert gate). |
| `tools/operator_stake_activation_audit.sh [--rpc-port N] [--json] [--pending-only] [--delay-window N]` | Read-only **REGISTER-side activation-lifecycle audit** — the ENTRY-side counterpart to the exit-side stake suite (`operator_stake_audit.sh` / `operator_unstake_timeline.sh` / `operator_validator_unstake_pipeline.sh` all cover locked/unlock_height; none read `registered_at` / `active_from`). Enumerates validators via `determ stakes --json`, reads each registry sub-block (`registered_at`, `active_from`, `inactive_from`) via `determ show-account <domain> --json` plus locked stake via `determ stake_info <domain>`, and against `determ head` classifies each as **pending-activation** (`active_from > current_height` — registered but committee-dormant; reports `blocks_to_active = active_from - height`), **active** (`active_from <= height`, `inactive_from == UINT64_MAX`), or **exiting** (`inactive_from != UINT64_MAX` — DEREGISTER landed). Per the apply path a REGISTER at height H sets `registered_at = H` and `active_from = H + derive_delay`, where `derive_delay = 1 + (seed % REGISTRATION_DELAY_WINDOW)` (`src/chain/chain.cpp:42-47` + `:800-802`), so the activation latency `active_from - registered_at` must sit in `[1, REGISTRATION_DELAY_WINDOW]` (= 10, `include/determ/node/registry.hpp:15`); the script computes that latency per entry and reconciles it against the envelope. **Anomaly flags**: `latency_zero` (latency 0 at a non-genesis height), `latency_overshoot` (latency > `--delay-window`); `genesis_seeded` (`registered_at == active_from == 0`, injected directly not via `derive_delay`) is INFO not anomaly. Default human output is a status-sorted table (pending-activation first, smallest `blocks_to_active` on top) + summary footer; `--json` emits `{validators:[{domain, locked, registered_at, active_from, inactive_from, latency, blocks_to_active, status, flags:[...]}], summary:{total, pending_count, active_count, exiting_count, genesis_seeded_count, anomaly_count, current_height, delay_window, rpc_port}}`. `--pending-only` suppresses non-dormant rows; `--delay-window N` overrides the latency ceiling for non-default chains. Reads only `determ head / stakes / show-account / stake_info` — no mutating endpoint. O(N) lock-free RPC calls (one show-account + one stake_info per validator). Verified node-free (`--help` + arg-rejection smoke; `bash -n` clean). **Exit codes**: 0 no latency anomalies (or default informational mode), 2 `--pending-only` AND >=1 latency anomaly (operator alert gate; never fires in default mode), 1 RPC error / unreachable daemon / malformed response / bad args. |
| `tools/operator_rpc_auth_probe.sh [--rpc-port N] [--host H] [--secret <hex>] [--external-bind] [--timeout SEC] [--json]` | **LIVE S-001 HMAC RPC-auth enforcement probe** — the on-the-wire complement to the offline config linters (`operator_config_audit.sh` / `operator_rate_limiter_audit.sh`), which lint a static `config.json` and never touch a running daemon. Those answer "did the operator write the right knob?"; this answers "does the *running* RPC socket reject an unauthenticated read?". Opens a raw TCP socket to `<host>:<rpc_port>` and speaks the determ RPC wire protocol directly (newline-delimited JSON — the same envelope `rpc::rpc_call` emits at `src/rpc/rpc.cpp`), deliberately sending a `status` request with **no `auth` field** (the CLI can't express this — `rpc_call` always attaches an HMAC when a secret is present, `src/rpc/rpc.cpp:297`). Classifies the reply per `RpcServer::verify_auth` (`src/rpc/rpc.cpp:112`): **ENFORCED** (reply error starts with `auth_required` — S-001 live, **OK**), **OPEN** (null error + a status result — auth disabled on the wire; **INFO** on a loopback bind = documented dev/consortium posture, **CRITICAL** with `--external-bind` = the externally-reachable-without-auth danger case the server itself warns about at startup, `src/rpc/rpc.cpp:98`), or **RATE_LIMITED** (reply error `rate_limited` — the S-014 token bucket consumed the probe before auth was evaluated, `src/rpc/rpc.cpp:172`; posture indeterminate → **UNKNOWN**, re-run later). With `--secret <hex>` (and only when auth is ENFORCED) it runs two further read-only control probes: **POSITIVE** (a correctly-HMAC'd `status` must succeed — a failure means the supplied secret does NOT match the running server's `rpc_auth_secret`, a deployment-drift **CRITICAL**) and **NEGATIVE** (a status request authenticated with a one-byte-flipped key must be rejected with `auth_failed` — an accept means the server isn't validating the HMAC, a constant-time-compare-bypass **CRITICAL**; mirrors the tamper case in `tools/test_rpc_hmac_auth.sh` as a live operator probe). The HMAC pre-image reproduces `canonical_for_hmac` (`src/rpc/rpc.cpp:52`) byte-for-byte as `method + "\|" + params.dump()` (i.e. `status\|{}`), using Python's stdlib `hmac`/`hashlib` (no new dep). Issues only the read-only `status` method — **never** a mutating RPC. Default human output is a posture line + bind assertion + per-control status + a `[OK]`/`[INFO]`/`[CRIT]` findings list and verdict; `--json` emits `{host, rpc_port, external_bind, posture, auth_enforced, controls: {positive, negative}, findings: [{severity, message}, …], verdict, exit_code}`. Pure socket probe — no daemon binary required (`DETERM_BIN` defaulted to `:`), so it runs from an ops workstation with only network reach to the node. **Exit codes**: 0 ENFORCED / OPEN-on-loopback (INFO) / RATE_LIMITED (UNKNOWN), 2 CRITICAL (OPEN on `--external-bind`, or a `--secret` control failed — operator alert gate), 1 transport error (no daemon on the port) / malformed reply / bad args / bad secret hex. |
| `tools/operator_reward_budget.sh [--rpc-port N] [--from H] [--to H] [--last N] [--bucket-blocks N] [--block-subsidy S] [--anomalies-only] [--json]` | Read-only **per-block validator-reward composition** (security-budget view) — combines the two halves of `total_distributed = total_fees + subsidy_this_block` (`chain.cpp::apply_block`) that the subsidy-only / fee-only tools never combine, and reports the **fee-coverage ratio** (fees / total reward) + its bucketed trend (the subsidy-sustainability signal). Walks a block window via `block-info --json` (per-block `transactions[].fee` + `creators`) + `supply --field accumulated_subsidy` (`--block-subsidy` override). **Anomaly flags**: `fee_coverage_low`, `fee_coverage_collapse` (bucket cratered >50% vs prior), `subsidy_basis_unavailable`. **Exit codes**: 0 ok/info, 2 `--anomalies-only` AND a flag fired, 1 RPC/args error. |
| `tools/operator_randomness_beacon_audit.sh [--rpc-port N] [--from H] [--to H] [--last N] [--entropy-floor F] [--anomalies-only] [--json]` | Read-only **consensus randomness-beacon health audit** of the `cumulative_rand` hash-chain (the entropy source for committee selection, REGISTER/DEREGISTER activation delay, and the E3 subsidy lottery — previously unaudited as a stream). Per block reads `cumulative_rand` + `delay_output` (`Block::to_json`) and checks (A) the SHA-256 recurrence `cumulative_rand[h] == SHA256(cumulative_rand[h-1] ‖ delay_output[h])` byte-for-byte per `validator.cpp::check_cumulative_rand`, (B) non-repetition of beacon values + non-zero delay_outputs, (C) a normalized per-nibble Shannon-entropy floor. **Anomaly flags**: `beacon_recurrence_break`, `beacon_value_repeat`, `delay_output_repeat`, `beacon_entropy_low`. **Exit codes**: 0 ok/info, 2 `--anomalies-only` gate, 1 RPC/args. |

Distinct from `operator_block_size_audit.sh` (a single window-AGGREGATE tx-type distribution, blind to a mid-window shift): this buckets the tx-type dimension over time and reports per-bucket composition (share in basis points), the dominant type per bucket, and the **total-variation distance (TVD)** between adjacent non-empty buckets. **Anomaly flags**: `mix_shift_detected` (adjacent-bucket TVD > `--max-shift`), `type_dominance_high` (a type > `--max-dominance`), `empty_window`. **Exit codes**: 0 ok/info, 2 `--anomalies-only` gate, 1 RPC/args. |

| `tools/operator_rpc_method_surface.sh [--rpc-port N] [--external-bind] [--anomalies-only] [--json]` | Read-only **RPC mutating-surface auth-posture probe** — the lane's existing tools cover only one slice each (`operator_rpc_auth_probe.sh` proves the global HMAC gate is enforced via a single `status` call; `operator_rate_limiter_audit.sh` lints S-014 knobs in a static `config.json`); neither maps the **method surface**. `rpc.cpp::dispatch` routes a fixed method table with NO per-method ACL that mixes read-only queries with **6 state-mutating methods** (`register`/`send`/`stake`/`unstake`/`submit_tx`/`submit_equivocation`), all guarded only by the single global `verify_auth` gate (`rpc.cpp:179`, before `dispatch`). The tool reports that mutating roster (a static baseline compiled from the cited `rpc.cpp` lines — the roster is NOT RPC-enumerable, stated honestly in `--help`) and confirms on the wire whether it's gated: an unauthenticated `status` probes posture, and **only when auth is ENFORCED** it sends unauthenticated mutating calls that bounce at `verify_auth` *before* the handler runs (when auth is OPEN it sends NO mutating call — that would queue a real tx — and reports from the static table). Honestly scopes out S-022 size caps (gossip-layer, not RPC) + bind posture (asserted via `--external-bind`). **Anomaly flags**: `CRITICAL` (auth OPEN + `--external-bind` — full mutating surface remotely reachable), `WARN` (auth OPEN on loopback, or ENFORCED but a method returned non-`auth_required`), `INFO` (probe rate-limited). **Exit codes**: 0 ok/info/skip (unreachable daemon → INFO+SKIP), 2 CRITICAL or (`--anomalies-only` AND anomaly), 1 args/transport. |
| `tools/operator_peer_rtt_audit.sh --rpc-ports P1,P2,... [--peers-port P] [--samples N] [--threshold-ms N] [--json] [--anomalies-only]` | Per-peer **RPC round-trip-latency** audit â€” the latency dimension of peer health that no existing tool reports. TIMES a lightweight read-only `determ status` call (`--samples` probes each, default 3) against every supplied RPC endpoint (each interpreted as `127.0.0.1:<port>` â€” the determ CLI is localhost-only and the `peers` RPC returns gossip addresses with no RPC port, so like `operator_peer_topology.sh` / `operator_consensus_lag.sh` the operator supplies the RPC ports to time), measuring each round trip via python's monotonic clock (NTP-step-immune) and reporting per-endpoint **min/mean/max** RTT in ms over the successful samples. Also queries ONE anchor daemon's `peers` RPC (`--peers-port`, default = first `--rpc-ports` entry) for a connected-peer-count cross-reference (unreachable anchor â†’ `n/a`, non-fatal). Distinct from the count/topology peer tools (`operator_peer_topology.sh` graph shape, `operator_peer_connectivity_health.sh` single-node digest â€” neither times a call) and from the block/consensus latency siblings (`operator_consensus_latency.sh` inter-block deltas, `operator_block_propagation_latency.sh` block-landing poll â€” neither measures RPC RTT). Anomalies: **`unreachable`** (CRITICAL â€” endpoint answered 0 of `--samples` probes), **`stalled`** (WARN â€” reachable but mean RTT > `--threshold-ms` default 1000). Default human output is a min/mean/max latency table + summary; `--json` emits `{peers_port, anchor_peer_count, samples, threshold_ms, probed_endpoints, endpoints:[{port, reachable, ok_samples, min_ms, mean_ms, max_ms, unreachable, stalled}], unreachable_ports, stalled_ports, anomalies, ok}`. Read-only (only `status` + `peers` RPCs; never a mutating endpoint). **Exit codes**: 0 all reachable + within threshold, 1 argument error, 2 at least one unreachable endpoint (CRITICAL operator alert gate) OR `--anomalies-only` AND any anomaly present. |
| `tools/operator_genesis_drift_monitor.sh [--rpc-port N] [--expected-genesis <hex>] [--samples N] [--interval S] [--json] [--anomalies-only]` | Read-only **runtime genesis-mutation monitor** â€” the temporal surface the genesis lane lacked. The one-shot siblings answer "does this daemon match my pinned genesis *right now*?" (`operator_genesis_verify_live.sh` chain-id-vs-file) or "do its effective op-params match?" (`operator_genesis_audit.sh` S-039 cross-check); none samples over TIME. THIS polls `determ status --field genesis` (the live block-0 hash, `to_hex(chain_.at(0).compute_hash())` per `Node::rpc_status` in `src/node/node.cpp`; bare-hex no-envelope output per `cmd_status` in `src/main.cpp`, exit 0 + blank line on an empty chain) `--samples` times (1..4320; default 12) across the window, `--interval` seconds apart (0..3600; default 5; 0 = back-to-back burst). Baseline = `--expected-genesis <hex>` if pinned up front (case-insensitive, 64-hex), else the first non-empty sample. Fires **`genesis_drift`** (CRITICAL) if any non-empty sample differs from the baseline â€” the signal for an illegal chain reload onto a different genesis, a block-0 tamper, or a config-swap attack. Empty samples (chain mid-load) are recorded as **`genesis_empty`** (INFO) and never establish/violate the baseline or gate the exit code, so a daemon polled mid-boot produces no false alert. Bounded loop (hard caps, no infinite mode), timeout-guarded; `--json` emits `{rpc_port, samples, interval, baseline, baseline_source, observed[], distinct_genesis[], drift_count, empty_count, first_drift_sample, anomalies[]}`; `--anomalies-only` suppresses healthy output. **Exit codes**: 0 no drift (baseline held across every non-empty sample), 2 `genesis_drift` detected (operator alert gate), 1 RPC error / unreachable daemon / malformed response / bad args. Exercised node-free (`bash -n`, `--help`, arg-validation + no-daemon smoke). |
| `tools/operator_rpc_throughput_probe.sh [--rpc-port N] [--host H] [--duration-sec N] [--max-requests N] [--timeout SEC] [--configured-rate R] [--configured-burst B] [--expected-min-rps R] [--anomalies-only] [--json]` | Read-only **live end-to-end RPC-throughput probe** â€” fires read-only `status` polls as fast as it can over a fixed window (default 5s, `--max-requests` caps load) and reports the achievable rate (successful replies/sec), then correlates it against the daemon's advertised rate-limit posture. The lane's static/one-shot tools never measure achievable live rate: `operator_rate_limiter_audit.sh` lints the 4 S-014 knobs in a STATIC `config.json` (never touches the wire); `operator_rpc_auth_probe.sh` / `operator_rpc_method_surface.sh` send a single `status` (posture, not a rate); `operator_chain_replay_speedometer.sh` measures blocks/sec + txs/sec chain-apply cadence (~1 req/interval), not RPC request rate; `operator_tx_throughput.sh` reads on-chain TPS off finalized blocks. **Honesty note** (in report body + `--help`): this measures END-TO-END achievable rate (the COMBINED effect of the S-014 limiter + server load/lock-contention + connect-per-call + network RTT), NOT limiter engagement in isolation â€” the limiter's internal token state has NO RPC endpoint (`rpc.cpp::dispatch`). It correlates against (a) `protections.rpc_rate_limit` (a BOOLEAN â€” `node.cpp:2537`; the configured numeric rate/burst are NOT RPC-exposed, live only in `Config::to_json`, so the operator may assert them via `--configured-rate`/`--configured-burst` for a quantitative line), and (b) the count of `rate_limited` replies the probe itself triggered (`rpc.cpp:172` â€” the ONE direct on-the-wire limiter-engagement signal). Strictly READ-ONLY: the only method sent is `status` (read-only `node.cpp::rpc_status`), albeit at high volume â€” run only against a node you operate. **Findings**: `INFO` (limiter advertised disabled / limiter engaged / probe errors), `WARN` (achievable rate below `--expected-min-rps` SLO floor â€” cause is end-to-end, not isolable). `--json` emits `{limiter_advertised, configured_rate, configured_burst, requests_sent, successful, rate_limited, errors, elapsed_sec, achievable_rps, attempted_rps, expected_min_rps, correlation, findings, verdict, skipped, exit_code}`. **Exit codes**: 0 ok/info/skip (unreachable daemon â†’ INFO+SKIP / `{"skipped":true}`), 2 `--anomalies-only` AND achievable rate below `--expected-min-rps`, 1 transport/malformed-reply / bad args. |
| `tools/operator_active_set_headroom.sh [--rpc-port N] [--min-full-headroom N] [--max-ineligible-pct P] [--anomalies-only] [--json]` | Read-only **active-creator-set committee-formation headroom** — the live eligible-pool-vs-target margin no existing registry tool computes (`operator_config_audit.sh` reads `m_creators`/`k_block_sigs` from a static config, not the live registry; `operator_stake_activation_audit.sh` does per-validator activation latency; the committee tools do per-block selection fairness). Reads `status` (`node.cpp::rpc_status`: `node_count`=`registry_.size()`, `m_creators`, `k_block_sigs`) + `validators --json` (`rpc_validators` returns `NodeRegistry::build_from_chain`'s **eligible** set — array length IS the live eligible-pool size, filtered by active_from/inactive_from/min_stake/abort-suspension), and derives `k_bft = ceil(2·m_creators/3)` matching `producer.cpp::required_block_sigs` (`(2·M+2)/3`). **Anomaly flags** (severity ladder): `cannot_form_bft_committee` (eligible < k_bft — hard liveness stall), `cannot_form_full_committee` (eligible < m_creators — forced to BFT/merge), `thin_full_headroom` (0 ≤ eligible−m_creators < `--min-full-headroom`, default 2), `high_ineligible_overhang` (ineligible/node_count > `--max-ineligible-pct`%, default 50 — churn/activation backlog). **Exit codes**: 0 ok/info/skip (unreachable daemon → INFO+SKIP), 2 `--anomalies-only` AND ≥1 anomaly, 1 args/RPC-parse error. |
| `tools/operator_dh_commit_reveal_audit.sh [--rpc-port N] [--from H] [--to H] [--last N] [--anomalies-only] [--json]` | Read-only **S-009 per-creator commit-reveal binding audit** — re-derives the Phase-1-commit/Phase-2-reveal binding the validator enforces at `validator.cpp::check_creator_dh_secrets` (`SHA256(creator_dh_secrets[i] ‖ creators[i].pubkey) == creator_dh_inputs[i]`), a contribution-layer integrity check no existing tool performs (grep: `creator_dh_inputs`/`creator_dh_secrets` appear in ZERO `operator_*.sh`). The randomness lane's `operator_randomness_beacon_audit.sh` audits only the AGGREGATE beacon recurrence (`cumulative_rand`/`delay_output`) — a block can satisfy the beacon yet carry a broken/tampered per-creator commit, which only this tool catches; `operator_subsidy_lottery_audit.sh`/`operator_stake_activation_audit.sh` merely consume `cumulative_rand` downstream; the signature/committee tools audit the orthogonal `creator_block_sigs[]`/`creators[]` arrays. Walks `block-info <h> --json` (`creators`/`creator_dh_inputs`/`creator_dh_secrets` per `block.cpp::to_json`) over a `head`-bounded window, resolving each slot's pubkey via `validators --json` (`domain`→`ed_pub`). **Anomaly flags**: `dh_binding_break` (`SHA256(secret‖pubkey) != stored commit` — tamper / bypassed gate), `dh_array_shape_mismatch` (creators/inputs/secrets length divergence), `dh_secret_reuse` (a non-zero revealed secret repeats — replayed reveal / contribution-layer grinding). Since-deregistered slots (pubkey absent from the live snapshot) are counted `unresolved`, reported informationally, never an anomaly. **Exit codes**: 0 ok/info/skip (unreachable daemon → INFO+SKIP), 2 `--anomalies-only` AND ≥1 anomaly, 1 args/RPC-parse error. |
| `tools/operator_inbound_admission_age.sh [--rpc-port N] [--from H] [--to H] [--last N] [--age-slack N] [--floor-strict] [--anomalies-only] [--json]` | Read-only **destination-side cross-shard inbound-admission age** — ages each finalized inbound receipt against its source-emit height using ONLY the local daemon's chain (`admission_age = landing_block.index − receipt.src_block_index`), with distribution (min/p50/p95/max/mean) + per-source-shard breakdown. Distinct from the cross-shard lane's siblings: `operator_receipt_settlement_latency.sh` computes the same delta but **source-side requiring `--peer-ports`** for a cross-daemon join; `operator_cross_shard_health.sh` uses the live `pending_inbound_receipts` pool snapshot + emit/apply counts (never reads `src_block_index` off admitted receipts); `operator_inbound_reconciliation_audit.sh` counts F2 admissions without aging them. Walks `block-info <h> --json` (`inbound_receipts[]` per `block.cpp::to_json:472`; receipt `src_shard`/`src_block_index` per `block.cpp:199-201`) over a `head`-bounded window. **Honesty note** (in `--help`): the `CROSS_SHARD_RECEIPT_LATENCY=3` soak floor is keyed on the destination's runtime-only `pending_inbound_first_seen_` (never serialized), so `admission_age` is an UPPER BOUND on the true local soak (includes gossip transit + the two shards' independent height offset); the floor check is soft by default (`--floor-strict` hardens it only for height-synchronized fleets). **Anomaly flags**: `admission_age_high` (> 3 + `--age-slack`, default 50), `admission_below_soak_floor` (< 3 — soft unless `--floor-strict`), `admission_age_negative` (src > landing — index corruption). **Exit codes**: 0 ok/info/single-shard/skip (unreachable daemon → INFO+SKIP), 2 `--anomalies-only` AND ≥1 anomaly, 1 args/RPC-parse/empty-window error. |
| `tools/operator_nonce_gap_audit.sh [--rpc-port N] [--from H] [--to H] [--top N] [--anomalies-only] [--json]` | Read-only **per-account finalized nonce-sequence integrity** — holes / backwards-movement / double-inclusion in each sender's on-chain nonce stream across a block window. The tx-admission lane's siblings don't read `nonce` off finalized blocks (`operator_tx_throughput.sh` reads only `len(transactions)`+`timestamp`; `operator_tx_mix_trend.sh` only the `type` field; `operator_mempool_inspector.sh`/`operator_mempool_diagnostic.sh` target a per-tx `mempool` RPC the daemon does NOT expose — `rpc.cpp::dispatch` has only scalar `mempool_size` — so they SKIP against a live node). This scans the FINALIZED stream the `block` RPC does expose, producing real findings: walks `block-info <h> --json` grouping `transactions[]` by `from` (`block.cpp:39`) tracking each sender's highest `nonce` (`block.cpp:43`) + seen-set. **Anomaly flags**: `nonce_gap` (`n > last+1` — everything queued behind the hole is wedged), `nonce_regression` (`n < last`, unseen — replay/reorg signal, impossible under monotonic apply), `nonce_duplicate` (same `(from,nonce)` finalized twice). First sight per sender = baseline (no claim against pre-window history). **Exit codes**: 0 ok/info/skip (unreachable daemon → INFO+SKIP), 2 `--anomalies-only` AND ≥1 anomaly, 1 args/RPC-parse/empty-window error. |

| `tools/operator_equivocation_evidence_integrity.sh --rpc-port N [--from H] [--to H] [--last N] [--json] [--anomalies-only]` | Structural well-formedness audit of FA6 equivocation EVIDENCE payloads in finalized blocks. Re-checks the offline subset of validator.cpp::check_equivocation_events per event: I1 digest_a==digest_b, I2 sig_a==sig_b, I3 bad hex length (digest!=64 / sig!=128), plus R1 equivocator verification-key resolvability via `validators` (reported, never an anomaly â€” slashed equivocators are deactivated). Sources: head / block-range (headers RPC retains equivocation_events) / validators. Exit 0 ok/skip (daemon unreachable or zero events), 1 args/RPC/empty-window, 2 --anomalies-only AND >=1 structural violation. |
| `tools/operator_dapp_activity_trajectory.sh --rpc-port N [--from H] [--to H] [--topic T] [--prefix P] [--steady-band F] [--surge-factor F] [--collapse-min-first N] [--surge-min-second N] [--top-N N] [--json] [--anomalies-only]` | Per-DApp DAPP_CALL message-rate trajectory: splits the block window into first/second halves, counts calls to each registered DApp per half (paginated dapp-messages), classifies each as RISING/FALLING/STEADY/DORMANT from the half-over-half per-block rate delta, and reports a window-wide momentum verdict. Anomalies: `dapp_collapse` (busy first half, silent second half), `dapp_surge` (second-half rate >= surge-factor x first-half with a min-call floor). Read-only RPC. Exit 0 ok/INFO/SKIP (unreachable daemon \| empty/1-block window), 1 bad args/RPC error, 2 --anomalies-only and an anomaly fired. |
| `tools/operator_committee_capture_margin.sh --rpc-port N [--json] [--quorum-mode strong\|bft] [--min-capture N] [--anomalies-only]` | Stake-weighted committee-capture margin: projects each validator's stake share onto expected committee seats (share x K, K=m_creators) and reports the SAFETY floor `control_set` (min top-stake validators whose cumulative seats >= quorum Q) and LIVENESS floor `halt_set` (min validators whose seats exceed slack K-Q), tied to the chain's real Q=required_block_sigs (strong: Q=K; bft: Q=ceil(2*k_bft/3)). Anomalies: control_set_singleton, control_set_below, halt_set_below, total_stake_zero, committee_undersized. Exit 0 ok/skip, 1 args/RPC error, 2 --anomalies-only with anomaly. Unreachable daemon -> INFO+SKIP / {"skipped":true}. |
| `tools/operator_block_fullness_audit.sh [--rpc-port N] [--json] [--from H] [--to H] [--last-n N] [--capacity T] [--saturated-pct P] [--max-empty-pct P] [--trend-delta-pct P] [--anomalies-only]` | Audit per-block transaction-count capacity utilization (block fullness) over a window: empty-block rate, fill distribution (p50/p90/max) vs a SOFT --capacity target, saturation-pressure count at/over --saturated-pct, and an early-vs-late fullness trend. Anomalies: empty_block_rate_high, saturation_pressure, fullness_rising. Capacity is an operator planning target, not a protocol cap (determ has no hard per-block tx-count limit; only the S-022 wire-byte cap, covered by operator_block_size_audit.sh). Exit 0 ok/info/SKIP (daemon unreachable or no produced blocks), 1 bad args/RPC-parse/empty window, 2 --anomalies-only AND anomaly present. |
| `tools/operator_validator_abort_rate.sh [--rpc-port N] [--from H] [--to H] [--last N] [--validator D] [--abort-rate-threshold F] [--window-abort-threshold F] [--min-duty N] [--json] [--anomalies-only]` | Per-validator ABORT-RATE liveness audit over a finalized-block window, normalized against committee duty (aborts / selections from `creators[]` + `abort_events[].aborting_node`), plus the aggregate `round` distribution of aborts. Flags `high_abort_rate` (validator selections >= --min-duty AND rate > --abort-rate-threshold, default 0.10), `abort_volume_high` (window aborts/selections > --window-abort-threshold, default 0.05), `aborts_without_duty` (domain aborted but never in-window creators[]). Exit 0 ok/SKIP (daemon unreachable -> INFO / `{"skipped":true}`), 1 args/RPC/empty-window, 2 anomaly present. |

| `tools/operator_reorg_resilience.sh [--rpc-port N] [--last K \| --from A --to B] [--json] [--anomalies-only] [--strict]` | Per-block fork-choice WEIGHT / reorg-resilience margin audit over a window of finalized blocks. For each block, reconstructs the exact weight Determ's deterministic tie-break (`src/chain/chain.cpp::resolve_fork`) would assign it: `committee_size = len(creators[])`, `nonzero_sigs` = count of present (non-all-zero) `creator_block_sigs[]`, `quorum = required_block_sigs(mode, committee_size)` (MUTUAL_DISTRUST→committee_size, BFT→ceil(2C/3)), `sat_headroom = committee_size - nonzero_sigs`, and `abort_events` count. KEY 1 of resolve_fork is heaviest-non-zero-sig-set, so a head with `sat_headroom > 0` left signature slots a rival could fill to out-weight it (reorg-exposed); a saturated head (`sat_headroom == 0`) cannot be out-weighted on KEY 1. Fetches the whole window via paged `determ block-range FROM TO --json` (the `headers` RPC keeps `creators[]`/`creator_block_sigs[]`/`abort_events[]`/`consensus_mode`), reads genesis K + `bft_enabled` from `determ status`. `--strict` additionally flags blocks merely AT quorum (thinnest legal head). Distinct from `operator_fork_watch.sh` (cross-node divergence, needs two daemons) and `operator_signature_audit.sh` (participation/fill ratios, no tie-break framing). **Exit codes**: 0 success/informational/clean SKIP (daemon down via INFO+SKIP / `{"skipped":true}`, or empty chain), 1 RPC error / malformed response / bad args / empty window, 2 `--anomalies-only` AND ≥1 reorg-exposed head. |
| `tools/operator_sync_progress.sh [--rpc-port N] [--peer-ports a,b,c] [--max-deficit N] [--json] [--anomalies-only]` | Single-node catch-up / bootstrap-readiness gauge. Reads the node-under-test's own `determ status` (`height` + self-reported `sync_state`, node.cpp:2464/2471) and, when one or more reference `--peer-ports` are reachable, polls their `height` to establish the network tip; computes blocks-behind-tip `deficit`, a catch-up `progress_pct`, and a single bootstrap-ready verdict (ready only when `sync_state==in_sync` AND `deficit <= --max-deficit`). With no reachable reference peer the height comparison is reported `unknown` and the verdict falls back to sync_state alone (unverified). Distinct from operator_consensus_lag.sh (symmetric fleet-max stragglers, no sync_state, no node-under-test) and operator_peer_connectivity_health.sh (single-port, reads sync_state only for isolation, never compares heights). Strictly read-only. **Exit codes**: 0 ok/info or clean SKIP (node-under-test unreachable), 1 args / malformed status, 2 `--anomalies-only` AND an anomaly (`not_in_sync` \| `behind_tip`). |
| `tools/operator_lead_creator_premium.sh [--rpc-port N] [--json] [--from H] [--to H] [--last N] [--block-subsidy V] [--anomalies-only]` | Audit the lead-creator (position-0) reward premium: who repeatedly holds the privileged `creators[0]` slot that receives the integer-division remainder/dust of each block's (fees+subsidy) split, lead-slot occupancy HHI + top-1 share, and the cumulative remainder premium. Read-only; walks `block-info` per block. Flags `lead_occupancy_concentrated` (>50%), `lead_hhi_high` (>5000), `premium_concentrated` (>50%). Exit 0 ok/skip, 1 args/RPC, 2 --anomalies-only AND anomaly |
| `tools/operator_dapp_field_consistency_audit.sh --rpc-port N [--prefix STR] [--anomalies-only] [--json]` | Validates every live DApp registry entry against the DAPP_REGISTER decode-rule structural caps (service_pubkey=32B, topics<=32, topic<=64B, endpoint<=255B, metadata<=4096B) plus the retention enum {0,1}; flags OUT_OF_SPEC entries the wire decoder would reject (e.g. loaded via a snapshot-restore that bypasses the caps) and ENUM_DRIFT retention values. Read-only (status/dapp-list/dapp-info). Exit 0 ok/no-DApps/SKIP; 2 with --anomalies-only and >=1 OUT_OF_SPEC; 1 bad args/RPC-parse |

## Wallet diagnostic CLIs

Operator-facing diagnostic commands shipped on the `determ-wallet` binary (built from the same CMake target; see `wallet/` source tree). All are pure local computation — no daemon RPC required.

| Command | Purpose |
|---|---|
| `determ-wallet inspect-envelope --in <file> [--json]` | Diagnostic CLI that reads an AEAD envelope file and dumps its metadata (format/version, PBKDF2 iteration count, salt + nonce hex, AAD presence + length, ciphertext + tag lengths) **without decrypting**. No password required. Use cases: operators verifying a file is a valid envelope before attempting a costly decrypt; forensic inspection of stale recovery artifacts; debugging which envelope corresponds to which share. Reads the canonical dot-separated hex blob produced by `envelope encrypt`. Calls `envelope::deserialize()` for header parsing only; never derives a key, never invokes AES-GCM. **Exit codes**: 0 valid envelope, 1 missing/unreadable file, 2 malformed envelope (truncated / wrong magic / parse failure). |
| `determ-wallet shamir-split --secret <hex> --threshold T --shares N [--json]` | Splits a hex-decoded secret into N Shamir shares with threshold T (any T-of-N reconstruct; T-1 reveals nothing — information-theoretic). Validates 1 ≤ T ≤ N ≤ 255, even-length hex, non-empty secret. Distinct from the `recovery` flow's high-level SSS+AEAD+OPAQUE composition — this is the raw primitive exposed for operator share-distribution workflows independent of the recovery envelope (printing physical shares, splitting a non-wallet secret). Default human output: `Share i: x=X y=YYYY…` per line; `--json` emits `{"shares":[{"x":<int>,"y_hex":"<hex>"},…]}`. **Exit codes**: 0 success, 1 validation failure. |
| `determ-wallet shamir-combine --shares <file> [--json]` | Reconstructs a secret from a JSON shares file (output of `shamir-split`) via Lagrange interpolation. Rejects duplicate x values, length-mismatched y values, missing fields, x outside [1, 255], empty array, missing file, odd-length y_hex. Threshold is implicit in the share count. Default output: hex secret on stdout; `--json` emits `{"secret_hex":"…"}`. **Exit codes**: 0 success, 1 validation failure or reconstruction error. **Note**: SSS is information-theoretic — providing T-1 shares may "succeed" but produce a value indistinguishable from random; callers must validate the reconstructed secret out-of-band. |
| `determ-wallet shamir-verify --shares <file> [--threshold T] [--json]` | Structural verification of a Shamir share-set **without reconstructing the secret**. Distinct from `shamir-combine` (which performs Lagrange interpolation): `shamir-verify` reports whether a share file is structurally well-formed under the SSS invariants. Checks: JSON shape (`{"shares":[{"x":<int>,"y_hex":"<hex>"},…]}`), every `x ∈ [1, 255]` (`x = 0` reveals the secret directly — must be rejected), all `x` values distinct (duplicate x's = singular Lagrange basis), all `y_hex` values share a common byte length (GF(2^8) interpolation operates byte-wise — mismatched lengths indicate a corrupt or merged-from-different-secrets share-set), even-length hex + valid hex character set, non-empty shares array. Optional `--threshold T` cross-check (errors if N < T — under-threshold share set cannot reconstruct). Default human output is a per-check pass/fail line plus a summary `shamir_valid=YES (N=… common_y_len=… distinct_x=…)` or `shamir_valid=NO (reason=…)`; `--json` emits `{valid, share_count, threshold_ok, common_y_byte_len, distinct_x_count, errors: [...]}`. Use cases: operator pre-flight verification of recovery-share files before attempting a costly OPAQUE-gated reconstruction; periodic audit of cold-storage share artifacts; CI gate for share-export pipelines. Pure local computation — no daemon RPC, no secret material exposed. **Exit codes**: 0 valid, 1 args/parse error (missing file, bad JSON, bad flags), 2 structurally invalid (operator alert gate — share file would either fail reconstruction or, worse, succeed at producing a meaningless value). Exercised end-to-end by `tools/test_wallet_shamir_verify.sh`. |
| `determ-wallet account-create-batch --count N [--out <file>] [--json] [--force]` | Bulk anonymous-account keypair generator. Produces `N` fresh Ed25519 keypairs (Ed25519 → anon-address derivation per the canonical wallet address scheme; each call uses the OS CSPRNG, never the deterministic-test seed path) in a single invocation, for operator workflows that need to pre-mint a large account set (load-testing fixtures, recovery-rehearsal cohorts, deterministic-genesis seed accounts, integration-test scenarios). Validates `1 ≤ N ≤ 10000` (hard cap prevents accidental memory blow-up — operators with larger needs should script multiple invocations). Output modes are mutually exclusive: `--out <file>` writes a JSON envelope `{count: N, accounts: [{ed_priv_hex, ed_pub_hex, anon_address}, …]}` to disk; `--json` (without `--out`) emits the same JSON shape to stdout; supplying neither emits a human-readable per-keypair listing (`account[i]: anon=… ed_pub=… ed_priv=…`). Refuses to overwrite an existing `--out` target unless `--force` is supplied (protects against destructive re-runs). Includes RNG-freshness lock-in: repeated invocations with the same `--count` produce disjoint keypair sets (the implementation does not seed from any fixed input, and the test wrapper asserts this property across 30-40 assertions covering small/medium batch sizes, JSON-output validity, anon-address-format validity, RNG-freshness across calls, and validation rejections — empty count, count > 10000, malformed flags). Exercised end-to-end by `tools/test_wallet_account_create_batch.sh`. **Exit codes**: 0 batch generated, 1 args/parse error (missing `--count`, out-of-range `N`, `--out` file exists without `--force`, mutually-exclusive flag conflict), 2 RNG failure / file I/O failure. |
| `determ-wallet backup-verify --shares <file> --envelopes <file> [--threshold T] [--json]` | Full wallet-backup structural verification. Validates a complete recovery artifact (a Shamir share-set file + a per-share AEAD-envelope file) **without decrypting**. Checks the shape of each input independently, then cross-checks them: every share in `--shares` must have a corresponding envelope in `--envelopes` (1:1 mapping, same count, share `x`-values match envelope-array indices in canonical order), each envelope passes `envelope::deserialize()` for header parsing only (never derives a key, never invokes AES-GCM), and the optional `--threshold T` cross-check rejects backups where `N < T` (the threshold cannot be reconstructed from the saved share count). Distinct from `shamir-verify` (which only inspects the share file in isolation): `backup-verify` is the operator-facing single command that verifies a complete recovery bundle is internally consistent before attempting a costly OPAQUE-gated reconstruction. Default human output is a per-check pass/fail line plus a summary `backup_valid=YES (shares=N envelopes=N threshold=T)` or `backup_valid=NO (reason=…)`; `--json` emits `{valid, share_count, envelope_count, threshold_ok, errors: [...]}`. Pure local computation — no daemon RPC required, no secret material exposed. Use cases: pre-flight verification of a freshly-exported recovery bundle, periodic audit of cold-storage backups, CI gate for share-export pipelines. Exercised end-to-end by `tools/test_wallet_backup_verify.sh` (~30-40 assertions). **Exit codes**: 0 valid backup, 1 args/parse error (missing files, bad JSON, bad flags), 2 structurally invalid (operator alert gate — backup would fail reconstruction or fail envelope-deserialization on recovery). |
| `determ-wallet backup-create --secret <hex> --threshold T --keyholders <file> --shares-out <file> --envelopes-out <file> [--force] [--json]` | Wallet-backup generator — the **inverse** of `backup-verify`. Given a hex-decoded master secret, an SSS threshold `T`, and a keyholders file (JSON `{keyholders: [{x: <int>, passphrase: "..."}, …]}` mapping each share's `x`-coordinate to its keyholder's passphrase), splits the secret via Shamir over GF(2^8) into N shares (N = keyholders.length), encrypts each share independently under an AEAD envelope (AES-256-GCM + PBKDF2 key derivation per the canonical wallet envelope scheme; matches the `envelope encrypt` primitive) using that keyholder's passphrase, and writes the resulting `--shares-out` (JSON `{shares: [{x, y_hex}, …]}` — identical shape to `shamir-split` output) and `--envelopes-out` (JSON `{envelopes: [<canonical hex blob>, …]}` — one per keyholder, indexed by share-`x` canonical order) files atomically. Validates `1 ≤ T ≤ N ≤ 255`, even-length hex secret, non-empty keyholders array, unique `x`-values in keyholders, every keyholder has a non-empty passphrase, even-length hex on the secret. Refuses to overwrite existing `--shares-out` or `--envelopes-out` targets unless `--force` is supplied (protects against destructive re-runs). The round-trip contract is rigorous: the output pair MUST pass `backup-verify --shares <shares-out> --envelopes <envelopes-out> --threshold T` with exit 0, and a subsequent `shamir-combine` over any `T` decrypted envelopes MUST recover the original `--secret`. Default human output is a per-step status line + summary `backup_created=YES (shares=N threshold=T)`; `--json` emits `{created, share_count, threshold, shares_out, envelopes_out}`. Pure local computation — no daemon RPC required. Use cases: initial wallet-backup provisioning post-keypair-generation, recovery-bundle generation for a fixed keyholder cohort, CI fixtures for backup-verify regression. Exercised end-to-end by `tools/test_wallet_backup_create.sh` (~30-40 assertions including round-trip through `backup-verify` + `shamir-combine`). **Exit codes**: 0 backup created, 1 args/parse error (missing/malformed flags, bad keyholders JSON, secret/threshold validation failure, output file exists without `--force`), 2 cryptographic failure (Shamir split error, envelope encryption error, file I/O failure). |
| `determ-wallet keyfile-create --priv <hex> --passphrase-from <source> --out <file> [--force] [--json]` | Passphrase-encrypted `node_key.json` generator — the S-004 closure use-case (passphrase-encrypted node-key files at rest). Given a raw 32-byte Ed25519 private key as hex and a passphrase source, derives the public key + anon-address via the canonical wallet keypair scheme, then wraps the private key under the same AEAD envelope primitive used for wallet-recovery shares (AES-256-GCM + PBKDF2 per `wallet/envelope.hpp`; matches the `determ-wallet inspect-envelope` shape end-to-end). `--passphrase-from` accepts three source kinds: `file:<path>` (passphrase read from the named file — trailing newline stripped — useful for orchestration that drops a one-shot temp file), `env:<VAR>` (passphrase read from the named environment variable — useful for CI / systemd-style secret injection), and `prompt` (interactive no-echo terminal prompt with confirmation — operator-side keyfile provisioning). The output `--out <file>` is written atomically (same `_tmp.json` + rename pattern as `Chain::save`), refuses to overwrite an existing target unless `--force` is supplied (protects against destructive key replacement). Default human output is a per-step status line + summary `keyfile_created=YES (anon=… out=…)`; `--json` emits `{created, anon_address, ed_pub_hex, out, passphrase_source}` (note: the private key is NEVER echoed back to stdout in either mode — it is consumed and immediately encrypted into the envelope). Validates `--priv` is exactly 64 hex chars (32 bytes), passphrase is non-empty (refuses empty passphrase per S-004 — empty would make the AEAD envelope offline-grindable in O(1)). The resulting file is consumed at daemon start via the existing passphrase-decryption path on `--keyfile` load (when `DETERM_PASSPHRASE` is set in env or the operator is prompted). Pure local computation — no daemon RPC required. Use cases: initial node-key provisioning, key-rotation flows (generate fresh keyfile, swap on rolling restart), CI fixtures for keyfile-load regression. Exercised end-to-end by `tools/test_wallet_keyfile_create.sh` (~25-40 assertions including round-trip via `inspect-envelope` + decrypt + Ed25519 sign-verify across all three passphrase-source kinds). **Exit codes**: 0 keyfile created, 1 args/parse error (missing/malformed flags, bad `--priv` hex length, bad passphrase source spec, empty passphrase, output file exists without `--force`), 2 cryptographic / file I/O failure (envelope encryption error, atomic-rename failure, prompt-read failure on TTY). |
| `determ-wallet keyfile-decrypt --in <file> --passphrase-from <source> --out <file> [--force] [--json]` | Passphrase-encrypted `node_key.json` decrypter — the **inverse** of `keyfile-create`. Reads the canonical 2-line encrypted-keyfile format (line 1: `DETERM-NODE-V1` header tag; line 2: AAD-bound AEAD envelope blob — dot-separated hex per `wallet/envelope.hpp`), derives the unwrap key from the supplied passphrase via PBKDF2, decrypts the envelope with AAD binding to the header tag (defends against header-substitution attacks where an adversary swaps the V1 header for a different version label to extract under unexpected AAD context), and writes the plaintext `{ed_priv_hex, ed_pub_hex, anon_address}` JSON to `--out <file>` atomically (same `_tmp.json` + rename pattern as `keyfile-create`). `--passphrase-from` accepts the same three source kinds as `keyfile-create`: `file:<path>` / `env:<VAR>` / `prompt`. **Wrong-passphrase rejection is via the AEAD authenticity check** — the underlying AES-256-GCM tag must verify against the AAD-bound passphrase-derived key; a wrong passphrase yields a tag-mismatch failure surfaced as a clear `keyfile_decrypted=NO (reason=passphrase mismatch or corruption)` diagnostic (operator cannot distinguish "wrong passphrase" from "file corruption" — this is a deliberate cryptographic property, not a UX bug). Refuses to overwrite an existing `--out` target unless `--force` is supplied. Default human output is a per-step status line + summary `keyfile_decrypted=YES (anon=… out=…)`; `--json` emits `{decrypted, anon_address, ed_pub_hex, out, in, passphrase_source}` (note: the private key is NEVER echoed to stdout in either mode — it lands only in `--out`). Validates `--in` is a 2-line file with the expected header, envelope blob deserializes via `envelope::deserialize()`, and the resulting plaintext is exactly 64 hex chars (matches the round-trip contract with `keyfile-create`). Pure local computation — no daemon RPC required. Use cases: operator key-recovery from a backed-up encrypted keyfile, migration of a key between hosts (decrypt on source → transport plaintext over secure channel → re-encrypt on destination), forensic inspection of an archived keyfile when the original daemon process is no longer available. Exercised end-to-end by `tools/test_wallet_keyfile_decrypt.sh` (~25-40 assertions covering happy-path round-trip via `keyfile-create` + decrypt + Ed25519 sign-verify, wrong-passphrase AEAD rejection, header-tampering rejection, envelope-corruption rejection, all three passphrase-source kinds). **Exit codes**: 0 keyfile decrypted, 1 args/parse error (missing/malformed flags, bad input file, bad passphrase source spec, output file exists without `--force`), 2 cryptographic failure (AEAD authenticity check failed — wrong passphrase OR file corruption; envelope deserialization failure; header tag missing or malformed; file I/O failure). |
| `determ-wallet keyfile-reencrypt --in <file> --out <file> --old-passphrase-env <OLD_VAR> --new-passphrase-env <NEW_VAR> [--force] [--json]` | Passphrase rotation on an encrypted `DETERM-NODE-V1` keyfile **without changing the keypair** (R39+3 C2) — the S-004 operator-hygiene flow for an operator who suspects their passphrase is weak/compromised and wants to re-key the at-rest envelope while keeping their on-chain identity. The Ed25519 seed stays identical; only the at-rest AES-256-GCM + PBKDF2 envelope is rebuilt under the NEW passphrase with a fresh random salt + nonce (two reencrypts of the same input under the same new passphrase therefore produce byte-distinct outputs). **Sibling of `keyfile-rotate`**: both walk the same decrypt-then-reencrypt path with address invariance (header pubkey preserved verbatim + inner pubkey re-verified against it after decrypt + a self-test round-trip before any file is touched + `sodium_memzero` on every exit path), but they differ by interface — `keyfile-rotate` takes the general `--{old,new}-passphrase-from <src>` source specifier (`file:` / `env:` / `prompt`) plus atomic in-place staging + a same-passphrase guard, whereas `keyfile-reencrypt` takes **bare environment-variable NAMES** via `--old-passphrase-env` / `--new-passphrase-env`, suiting CI / secret-injection contexts (Vault, systemd `LoadCredential`, k8s secrets) where the passphrase is injected as an env var and never appears on a command line or in a file. Both var names route through the same `passphrase_from_source("env:<NAME>")` helper so the empty-value rejection + diagnostics stay identical to every other `keyfile-*` command. Refuses to overwrite an existing `--out` without `--force`. The recovered address (`0x` + pubkey_hex) is printed in human + `--json` output so callers can assert it is unchanged. Default human output: per-step status + summary `keyfile_reencrypted=YES (anon=… out=…)`; `--json` emits `{reencrypted, anon_address, ed_pub_hex, out, in}`. Exercised end-to-end by `tools/test_wallet_keyfile_reencrypt.sh` (60 assertions covering round-trip via `keyfile-create` → reencrypt → decrypt + Ed25519 sign-verify, address invariance, fresh-salt/nonce non-determinism, wrong-OLD-passphrase AEAD rejection, missing/empty env-var rejection, `--force` overwrite semantics, JSON-output validity). **Exit codes**: 0 reencrypted, 1 args/parse error (missing flags, missing/empty env var, can't open `--in`, structural `--in` problems — wrong header magic / malformed blob / unparseable plaintext JSON / mismatched pubkey, `--out` exists without `--force`), 2 cryptographic failure (wrong OLD passphrase OR tampered envelope OR mismatched AAD — indistinguishable by design; no `--out` written since decrypt precedes `--out` open). |
| `determ-wallet message-sign --priv <hex> --domain <tag> --message <bytes-or-@file> [--json]` | Off-chain Ed25519 message signer — distinct from transaction signing (which targets the chain's `signing_bytes` schema). Given a raw 32-byte Ed25519 private key as hex, a domain-separation tag (`<tag>` — short ASCII identifier like `siwe-auth-v1` / `operator-announce-v1` / `attestation-v1`), and a message body (literal bytes inline, or `@<file>` for file-sourced bytes), computes the signed payload as `SHA-256(domain_tag_bytes \|\| message_bytes)` and signs that 32-byte digest under Ed25519. The domain-separation tag is mixed into the hash (not the signature directly) so two callers using different `<tag>` values produce uncorrelated signatures even on identical message bodies — defense against signature-reuse attacks across protocol layers (a SIWE auth-challenge signature cannot be replayed as an operator-announcement signature even if message bytes happen to collide). Output is the hex-encoded 64-byte Ed25519 signature (default human format: `sig=<128-hex-chars>`; `--json` emits `{signature_hex, domain_tag, message_sha256, ed_pub_hex}`). Use cases: SIWE-class authentication challenge response (sign a server-supplied nonce under domain `siwe-auth-v1`); off-chain attestations (vendor signs a statement about a partner without anchoring to chain); operator announcements (signed messages from a validator without on-chain bloat — verified out-of-band against `validators --json` ed_pub set). Pure local computation — no daemon RPC required. Exercised end-to-end by `tools/test_wallet_message_sign.sh` (~30-40 assertions including sign/verify round-trip, domain separation, cross-key independence, RFC 8032 determinism, file-sourced message handling). **Exit codes**: 0 signature emitted, 1 args/parse error (missing/malformed `--priv` / `--domain` / `--message`, file unreadable for `@<file>` form, empty domain tag), 2 cryptographic failure (Ed25519 sign error — should never occur with valid 32-byte key). |
| `determ-wallet message-verify --pub <hex> --domain <tag> --message <bytes-or-@file> --signature <hex> [--json]` | Off-chain Ed25519 message verifier — the **inverse** of `message-sign`. Given the signer's Ed25519 public key as hex (`--pub`), the same domain-separation tag (`--domain`), the original message body (`--message <bytes>` or `@<file>`), and the 128-hex-char signature emitted by `message-sign` (`--signature`), recomputes the signed payload `SHA-256(domain_tag_bytes \|\| message_bytes)` and verifies the signature against it under Ed25519. **Domain-tag separation is enforced at verify time**: a signature produced under domain `siwe-auth-v1` will FAIL verification when checked under domain `operator-announce-v1` even with byte-identical message content — the verifier rebuilds the hash inputs from the user-supplied `--domain` and the underlying Ed25519 `verify` returns false on the mismatched digest. Default human output is a per-step status line + summary `signature_valid=YES (pub=… domain=…)` or `signature_valid=NO (reason=…)`; `--json` emits `{valid, ed_pub_hex, domain_tag, message_sha256, signature_hex}`. Use cases: server-side verification of SIWE challenge response (server received `{address, signature, nonce}` from client; recomputes hash + verifies under domain `siwe-auth-v1`); third-party verification of off-chain attestations (independent auditor checks vendor signature without trusting either party); operator-announcement verification (validator's published statement checked against known ed_pub from chain). Pure local computation — no daemon RPC required. Exercised end-to-end by `tools/test_wallet_message_sign.sh` (~30-40 assertions covering domain separation, wrong-key rejection, tampered-message rejection, tampered-signature rejection). **Exit codes**: 0 signature valid, 1 args/parse error (missing/malformed flags, file unreadable for `@<file>` form, bad hex length on `--pub` / `--signature`), 2 signature invalid (operator alert gate — wrong-key / tampered-message / tampered-signature / wrong-domain — the AEAD-style "deliberate cryptographic property" boundary that distinguishes "operationally OK" from "real failure"). |
| `determ-wallet account-import --priv <hex> [--out <file>] [--force] [--json]` | Single-account import operator CLI — the **inverse** of `account-create-batch` for the import flow. Given a raw 32-byte Ed25519 private key as hex, or a 64-byte concatenated `seed \|\| pubkey` form (where the trailing 32 bytes are the Ed25519 public key from an external KMS / HSM export), derives the public key + anon-address via the canonical wallet keypair scheme.
