In the 64-byte form, the script computes the derived pubkey from the seed and **verifies it matches the supplied trailing 32 bytes** before emitting any output (defense-in-depth — catches truncation / endianness / encoding bugs in upstream exports before they propagate into operator deployments). Output shape matches `account-create-batch` for ergonomic continuity: default human format emits `account: anon=… ed_pub=… ed_priv=…`; `--json` emits `{anon_address, ed_pub_hex, ed_priv_hex}`; `--out <file>` writes the same JSON envelope to disk. Refuses to overwrite an existing `--out` target unless `--force` is supplied (protects against destructive re-imports). Validates `--priv` is exactly 64 hex chars (32 bytes — seed-only form) or 128 hex chars (64 bytes — seed\|\|pubkey form); rejects any other length. Pure local computation — no daemon RPC required, no network roundtrip, no KMS dependency at runtime. Use cases: KMS / HSM-sourced key import (export raw seed from HSM; pipe through `account-import`; verify derived anon matches the deployment's expected address), recovery-from-paper-backup (operator typed seed from cold-storage paper; import into a fresh wallet file), migration between wallet schemes (export seed from external tool; import into determ-wallet canonical format). Exercised end-to-end by `tools/test_wallet_account_import.sh` (~25-35 assertions covering happy-path seed-only + seed\|\|pubkey forms, pubkey-mismatch rejection on 64-byte form, length validation, hex validation, `--out` round-trip vs stdout, `--force` overwrite semantics, JSON-output validity). **Exit codes**: 0 account imported, 1 args/parse error (missing/malformed `--priv`, bad hex length, output file exists without `--force`), 2 cryptographic mismatch (64-byte form: derived pubkey doesn't match supplied trailing 32 bytes — KMS-export integrity failure worth alerting on) or file I/O failure. |
| `determ-wallet account-import-many --in <array.json> --out-dir <dir> [--passphrase-env <NAME>] [--summary <path>] [--force]` | Bulk N-account import — the batch counterpart to `account-import` for migration / onboarding / custodial-seeding flows where N is large (regulated operator migrating tens of thousands of customer accounts; payroll onboarding; exchange cold-wallet provisioning). Reads a JSON array of records (each `{"address":"0x…", "privkey_hex":"…", "name"?:"…"}`), and for each record derives the pubkey + anon-address via the canonical wallet keypair scheme, **verifies the supplied `address` matches the seed-derived pubkey** (a mismatch flags the record `status="error"` so a mis-tagged record can't silently land under the wrong filename), and writes one keyfile per record under `--out-dir` (filename `<name>.keyfile` when a record carries a name, else `<address>.keyfile`). `--passphrase-env <NAME>` (optional) encrypts each keyfile at rest using the same envelope shape as `keyfile-create` (DETERM-NODE-V1 header + AES-256-GCM + PBKDF2-HMAC-SHA-256, loadable via `keyfile-info`); all N records share the passphrase drawn from the named env var. Absent `--passphrase-env`, output is plaintext single-account JSON matching `account-import --out` shape. `--summary <path>` (optional) writes a JSON array of `{address, keyfile_path, status: "ok"\|"skipped"\|"error", reason?}` — one record per input element. **Per-record fault tolerance**: an individual record's failure (bad hex, address/seed mismatch, overwrite collision without `--force`) marks it `status="error"` with `reason` populated but does NOT abort the bulk import — critical at N=50k where one bad row must not invalidate 49,999 good ones. Refuses to overwrite an existing keyfile without `--force` (collision → `status="error"` on that record; others still process). **Determinism**: same input JSON + same `--out-dir` + same `--passphrase-env` produces the same filenames + same summary structure (envelope ciphertext differs per run due to fresh per-keyfile salt + nonce, but file presence + addresses are byte-exact). Pure local computation — no daemon RPC required. Exercised end-to-end by `tools/test_wallet_account_import_many.sh` (30 assertions covering happy-path bulk import, plaintext + encrypted output modes, per-record error isolation, address/seed mismatch rejection, overwrite semantics, summary-file shape, env-var-missing handling). **Exit codes**: 0 bulk import completed (per-record status in the summary — partial failures are NOT a process-level error by design), 1 args/parse error (missing `--in` / `--out-dir`, unreadable input, `--out-dir` missing or not a directory, env var not set when `--passphrase-env` supplied). |
| `determ-wallet keyfile-recover --shares <file> --envelopes <file> --passphrases <file> --threshold T --out <file> [--force] [--json]` | High-level T-of-N wallet-key recovery — the operator-facing composition of `shamir-combine` + envelope decryption. Given a structurally-verified backup bundle (the `--shares` + `--envelopes` JSON files produced by `backup-create`; pre-flight verification via `backup-verify` is recommended), a `--passphrases <file>` mapping each keyholder's `x`-coordinate to their passphrase (JSON `{passphrases: [{x: <int>, passphrase: "..."}, …]}` — must contain ≥ T entries whose x-values match a subset of the share/envelope x-values), and the threshold `T`, decrypts T envelopes independently under their respective passphrases via AES-256-GCM + PBKDF2 (matches the canonical `envelope encrypt`/`keyfile-create` envelope scheme), collects the T decrypted Shamir shares, reconstructs the original master secret via Lagrange interpolation over GF(2^8), and writes the recovered plaintext `{ed_priv_hex, ed_pub_hex, anon_address}` JSON to `--out <file>` atomically (same `_tmp.json` + rename pattern as `keyfile-create` / `keyfile-decrypt`). **Wrong-passphrase semantics**: each envelope decryption is gated by the AES-256-GCM authentication tag (same AEAD authenticity check as `keyfile-decrypt`); a wrong passphrase for any of the T keyholders surfaces a clear diagnostic identifying which `x`-coordinate failed (`keyfile_recovered=NO (reason=envelope decryption failed for x=K)`) without revealing whether the failure was the passphrase, the envelope, or both — a deliberate cryptographic property, not a UX bug. Refuses to overwrite an existing `--out` target unless `--force` is supplied. **Insufficient-shares semantics**: supplying fewer than T `passphrases` entries fails fast before any decryption attempt with `keyfile_recovered=NO (reason=insufficient passphrases: have N, need T)`. **Mismatched x-values**: any passphrase entry whose `x` doesn't correspond to a share/envelope `x` is rejected at the pre-flight pass with a clear diagnostic. **Composition contract** with `backup-create`: invoking `backup-create --secret S --threshold T --keyholders K …` then `keyfile-recover --shares <shares-out> --envelopes <envelopes-out> --passphrases <K-derived-passphrases> --threshold T --out <recovered>` MUST yield a `--out` file whose decoded `ed_priv_hex` matches the secret S byte-for-byte. SSS information-theoretic safety property: any T-1 entries reveal nothing about the secret. Default human output is a per-step status line (per-envelope decrypt success, share-combination, final write) + summary `keyfile_recovered=YES (anon=… out=… threshold=T/N)`; `--json` emits `{recovered, anon_address, ed_pub_hex, out, threshold, total_shares}` (note: the recovered private key is NEVER echoed to stdout in either mode — it lands only in `--out`). Pure local computation — no daemon RPC required. Use cases: full operator wallet-recovery rehearsal from a K-of-N share + envelope bundle, post-disaster operator-key restoration, CI fixtures for full round-trip backup-create → backup-verify → keyfile-recover regression. Exercised end-to-end by `tools/test_wallet_keyfile_recover.sh` (~30-40 assertions covering happy-path T-of-T full-recovery via `backup-create`, T-of-N partial-subset recovery, wrong-passphrase rejection per share, insufficient-passphrase fail-fast, mismatched-x-value rejection, force-overwrite semantics, JSON-output validity, end-to-end Ed25519 sign-verify on the recovered key). **Exit codes**: 0 keyfile recovered, 1 args/parse error (missing/malformed flags, bad shares/envelopes/passphrases JSON, output file exists without `--force`, insufficient passphrases, mismatched x-values), 2 cryptographic failure (any envelope decryption AEAD authenticity check failed — wrong passphrase OR file corruption; Shamir reconstruction error; file I/O failure). |
| `determ-wallet shamir-rotate --shares <file> --threshold T --shares-out <file> [--force] [--json]` | **PSS polynomial-refresh share rotation** — refreshes a set of Shamir shares to a fresh polynomial while preserving the original secret. Given an existing share file (output of `shamir-split` or `backup-create`; JSON `{shares: [{x: <int>, y_hex: "..."}, ...]}`) and the threshold `T`, reconstructs the secret via Lagrange interpolation over GF(2^8), then re-splits it under a *fresh* random polynomial (same threshold T, same N shares preserving the original x-coordinates) and writes the new share-set to `--shares-out`. The rotated shares reconstruct to the *same* secret but each individual `y_hex` is independent of the prior set — defeating the share-disclosure window attack where an adversary observed (but did not exfiltrate the full T-subset of) a prior share-set: once rotated, any previously-observed share is useless because it lies on the prior polynomial, not the new one. This is the proactive-secret-sharing (PSS) refresh primitive composed with the existing `shamir-split` / `shamir-combine` primitives. **Refresh contract**: invoking `shamir-rotate --shares <in> --threshold T --shares-out <out>` followed by `shamir-combine --shares <out>` MUST yield a secret byte-for-byte identical to `shamir-combine --shares <in>`. Validates that the input share-set is structurally well-formed (every `x ∈ [1, 255]`, all `x` values distinct, all `y_hex` values share a common byte length, even-length hex), that the input contains ≥ T shares (otherwise reconstruction is impossible — fail-fast with diagnostic), and that the threshold is sane (`1 ≤ T ≤ \|shares\|`). Refuses to overwrite an existing `--shares-out` target unless `--force` is supplied (protects against destructive re-runs). Default human output: per-step status line (reconstruction → refresh → write) + summary `shamir_rotated=YES (threshold=T shares=N)`; `--json` emits `{rotated, threshold, share_count, shares_out}`. Pure local computation — no daemon RPC required, no envelope manipulation (the AEAD envelopes wrapping each share would need to be re-encrypted separately by the keyholders; this primitive operates on raw shares only). Use cases: periodic operator-driven PSS rotation as part of a security-hygiene rotation policy (refresh every N months), reactive rotation following a suspected share-disclosure incident, CI fixtures for share-rotation regression. Exercised end-to-end by `tools/test_wallet_shamir_rotate.sh` (~30-40 assertions including reconstruction-identity round-trip via `shamir-combine`, share-independence verification — every new `y_hex` differs from the prior `y_hex` at the same `x` — RNG-freshness across calls, threshold validation, x-coordinate preservation, JSON-output validity, force-overwrite semantics). **Exit codes**: 0 rotation complete, 1 args/parse error (missing/malformed flags, bad shares JSON, insufficient shares for threshold, output file exists without `--force`), 2 cryptographic failure (Shamir reconstruction error — degenerate input share-set; Shamir re-split error; file I/O failure). |
| `determ-wallet account-recover --shares <file> --envelopes <file> --passphrases <file> --threshold T [--out <file>] [--force] [--json]` | High-level composite anonymous-account recovery — the operator-facing **composition** of `shamir-combine` + per-share envelope decryption + Ed25519 keypair → anon-account derivation. Given a structurally-verified Shamir share-set, the matching AEAD-envelope file (one envelope per share, encrypted with that keyholder's passphrase), a passphrases file (one passphrase per share, in the same order as `envelopes[]`), and the threshold `T`, the command (a) decrypts each envelope to recover its plaintext share, (b) reconstructs the master secret via Lagrange interpolation over GF(2^8), (c) derives the Ed25519 public key from the reconstructed seed, and (d) emits the resulting anon-account artifact (private key + public key + anon-address) either to stdout or to `--out <file>`. Distinct from `keyfile-recover` (which targets the passphrase-encrypted node-key path producing a `node_key.json`): `account-recover` targets the bearer-wallet path producing an anon-account suitable for `determ send_anon`. Refuses to overwrite an existing `--out` file without `--force`. **All envelopes use independent AAD bound to the share index — tamper of any envelope file or passphrases-file ordering aborts before reconstruction.** Validates length consistency (`\|shares\|` == `\|envelopes\|` == `\|passphrases\|` ≥ T), structural well-formedness, threshold satisfiability (`T ≤ \|shares\| ≤ 255`), envelope-decryption success per share, and final secret length (32 bytes). Cross-references `tools/test_wallet_account_recover.sh` (regression). Companion analytic in `docs/proofs/WalletRecovery.md` FA12 (Shamir ITS + AEAD composition; account-derivation step matches the bearer-wallet keygen path). |
| `determ-wallet account-export --priv <hex> [--format {raw-hex\|json\|backup-bundle}] [--out <file>] [--threshold T] [--keyholders <file>] [--force] [--json]` | Operator-facing account-export CLI — the **inverse** of `account-import` plus a `backup-bundle` upgrade path. Given a raw 32-byte Ed25519 private key (`--priv <hex>`), derives the matching public key + anon-address via the same `wallet/anon_account.hpp` derivation chain used by `account-create-batch` / `account-import`, and emits the resulting account artifact in one of three formats: (a) **`raw-hex`** (the simplest export — writes a single line `<ed_priv_hex>\n` suitable for piping into another tool or feeding into `account-import --priv $(cat …)`; explicit acknowledgment that the file contains a plaintext private key — operator should treat it as sensitive material), (b) **`json`** (the structured export — writes `{ed_priv_hex, ed_pub_hex, anon_address}` JSON matching the on-disk format produced by `account-import --out` and consumed by `keyfile-create --priv`; portable across the operator-tool surface), (c) **`backup-bundle`** (the recovery-grade export — composes `account-export` with `backup-create`: splits `ed_priv_hex` into N Shamir shares under threshold `T`, encrypts each share under the matching keyholder's passphrase per the `--keyholders <file>` mapping, writes a paired shares + envelopes bundle to `--out <dir>/shares.json` + `--out <dir>/envelopes.json` — directly consumable by `keyfile-recover` / `account-recover` for full T-of-N recovery; the `--threshold` + `--keyholders` flags are mandatory in this mode). Default format is `json` when `--format` is omitted. Refuses to overwrite an existing `--out` target without `--force`. **Confidentiality contract**: in `raw-hex` and `json` modes the private key is written to `--out` only — never echoed to stdout in `--json` mode (`{format, anon_address, ed_pub_hex, out, …}` envelope omits `ed_priv_hex`); in `backup-bundle` mode the per-share AES-256-GCM AEAD envelopes are the sole representation of the private key on disk (the plaintext seed is wiped from memory after the splits land). **Round-trip contract**: invoking `account-export --priv P --format json --out F` then `account-import --priv $(jq -r .ed_priv_hex F) --out G` MUST yield a `G` file whose decoded `ed_priv_hex` matches `P` byte-for-byte; in `backup-bundle` mode the round-trip is `account-export --format backup-bundle --threshold T --keyholders K → keyfile-recover --shares shares.json --envelopes envelopes.json --passphrases K-derived --threshold T --out recovered.json`, which must yield `recovered.ed_priv_hex == P`. Pure local computation — no daemon RPC required, no network traffic. Use cases: operator-facing single-account export for downstream tooling integration (raw-hex / json), recovery-grade bundle generation when an operator wants to migrate an existing anonymous account into the T-of-N share-protection scheme (backup-bundle — composes with the shamir-rotate hygiene-rotation flow), CI fixtures for the full export → import / export → recover round-trip regression. Exercised end-to-end by `tools/test_wallet_account_export.sh` (covers happy-path raw-hex / json / backup-bundle exports, round-trip identity verification against `account-import` and `keyfile-recover`, force-overwrite semantics, threshold validation in backup-bundle mode, JSON-output validity, anon-address derivation correctness, end-to-end Ed25519 sign-verify on every exported representation). **Exit codes**: 0 export complete, 1 args/parse error (missing/malformed `--priv`, bad format, output target exists without `--force`, missing `--threshold` / `--keyholders` in backup-bundle mode), 2 cryptographic failure (Ed25519 keypair derivation error, Shamir split failure in backup-bundle mode, envelope encryption failure, file I/O failure). |
| `determ-wallet tx-sign-verify --priv <hex> --pub <hex> --tx-json <file-or-->@file> [--json]` | Transaction sign + verify round-trip CLI. Given an Ed25519 keypair (`--priv` raw 32-byte private key as 64 hex chars; `--pub` raw 32-byte public key as 64 hex chars — derived from `--priv` and cross-checked for consistency) and an unsigned Transaction in canonical JSON form (`--tx-json <file>` or `@<file>` syntax), serializes the canonical `signing_bytes` representation per `PROTOCOL.md §4.1` (deterministic tail-field-binding for amount / fee / nonce / payload / sender / recipient + the per-tx-type sentinel field set), invokes Ed25519 sign over the signing_bytes producing a 64-byte signature, then independently re-verifies the signature against the same signing_bytes via Ed25519 verify (sanity round-trip that catches signing-bytes drift between sign-path and verify-path — the exact defense that S-002 added at the binary_codec layer, now exposed as an operator CLI for pre-flight verification of any Transaction shape before submission). Reports the signed canonical Transaction JSON (with `signature` field populated) + the verify-result. Default human output is a per-step status line (`signing_bytes_hex=…`, `signature_hex=…`, `verify_result=VALID`) + summary `tx_sign_verify=YES (tx_hash=… amount=… fee=… nonce=…)`; `--json` emits `{signed_tx: {…}, signature_hex, signing_bytes_hex, tx_hash, verify_result}` (the full canonical signed-tx envelope ready for `determ submit-tx` ingestion). **Pubkey-consistency cross-check**: the CLI re-derives the public key from `--priv` and compares against the supplied `--pub`; mismatch yields a fail-fast diagnostic (`tx_sign_verify=NO (reason=pubkey mismatch — derived=… supplied=…)`) before any signing work — defense against KMS-export integrity bugs where the operator pastes a stale public key alongside a fresh private key. **Tx-type coverage**: TRANSFER / REGISTER / STAKE / DEREGISTER / UNSTAKE / DAPP_REGISTER / DAPP_CALL / DAPP_DEREGISTER / PARAM_CHANGE — every wire-format tx type with a `signing_bytes` schema is exercised; MERGE_EVENT / AbortEvent / EquivocationEvent / CrossShardReceipt are out-of-scope (those are validator-emitted, not user-signed). Pure local computation — no daemon RPC required, no network roundtrip. Use cases: pre-flight verification of a Transaction shape before submitting (catches signing-bytes drift, malformed payloads, hex-length bugs in the unsigned tx); CI fixtures for sign + verify regression coverage; operator-rehearsed transaction signing where the signed-tx envelope is staged for later submission via an out-of-band channel. Exercised end-to-end by `tools/test_wallet_tx_sign_verify.sh` (~30-40 assertions covering every tx-type sign-verify round-trip, pubkey-consistency cross-check, tampered-signing-bytes rejection, wrong-private-key rejection, malformed-tx-JSON rejection, file vs `@file` input parity, JSON-output validity). **Exit codes**: 0 sign + verify both succeed, 1 args/parse error (missing/malformed flags, bad hex length on `--priv` / `--pub`, malformed tx-json, file unreadable), 2 cryptographic failure (pubkey-consistency cross-check failed — supplied `--pub` does not match `--priv`-derived pubkey; Ed25519 sign error; Ed25519 verify FAILED on freshly-signed envelope — should never occur with a consistent keypair + well-formed signing_bytes, surfaced as a fail-safe lock-in for signing-bytes-vs-verify-path consistency). |
| `determ-wallet account-derive-batch --seed <hex> --count N [--start-index I] [--out <file>] [--force] [--json]` | Deterministic batch-account derivation from a master seed — operator-facing reproducible-account generator. Given a 32-byte master seed (`--seed <hex>` as 64 hex chars), derives `N` Ed25519 keypairs in sequence via per-index domain-separated SHA-256 (`derived_seed_i = SHA256("DETERM/ACCOUNT-DERIVE/v1" \|\| seed \|\| u64_be(start_index + i))`; the same seed + index pair always yields the same keypair — distinct from `account-create-batch`, which draws fresh randomness per call and is non-reproducible by design). For each index `i ∈ [start_index, start_index + N)`, emits the derived Ed25519 private + public key + anon-address triple. Default `--start-index 0`; operators can advance the index window to produce non-overlapping batches from the same seed (e.g., shard-per-region key allocation, deterministic test fixtures, HD-wallet-style staged derivation). Writes either to stdout (default) or to `--out <file>` as a JSON array of `{index, ed_priv_hex, ed_pub_hex, anon_address}` records; refuses to overwrite without `--force`. **Determinism contract**: invoking `account-derive-batch --seed S --count N --start-index I` twice MUST yield byte-identical output (including order, address derivation, hex casing); the domain separator `"DETERM/ACCOUNT-DERIVE/v1"` versions the derivation scheme — future schemes bump the version tag without breaking existing seeds. **Confidentiality contract**: the master seed is sensitive — exposes every present + future account derived from it; the per-index derived keys are equally sensitive. The JSON output writes private keys in plaintext (operator must treat the output file as secret material; pair with `account-export --format backup-bundle` or `keyfile-create` downstream for at-rest encryption). **Composition with the recovery stack**: derived keys are bit-equivalent to `account-create-batch` outputs in shape — the same `wallet/anon_account.hpp` derivation chain applies — so any derived key flows directly into `account-import`, `keyfile-create`, `account-export`, or the T-of-N Shamir backup pipeline. Pure local computation — no daemon RPC required, no network traffic. Use cases: deterministic test-fixture generation (the same seed always rebuilds the same N accounts for repeatable regressions), HD-wallet-style index walking from a single backed-up seed (operator backs up only the seed, then re-derives the live account set on demand), shard-per-region key pre-allocation from a single trust-root, anti-Sybil pre-binding (operator allocates a per-validator index range from a shared seed, eliminating cross-validator key-leak by construction). Exercised end-to-end by `tools/test_wallet_account_derive_batch.sh` (covers determinism — same seed + index → same key, non-overlapping index ranges, JSON-output validity, force-overwrite semantics, round-trip into `account-import`, distinctness across indices, domain-separator robustness against accidental input collision). **Exit codes**: 0 batch derivation complete, 1 args/parse error (malformed `--seed` hex, `--count < 1`, output target exists without `--force`, file I/O error), 2 cryptographic failure (Ed25519 keypair derivation regression — should never occur with a well-formed seed; surfaced as a fail-safe lock-in). |
| `determ-wallet keyfile-info --in <file> [--json]` | Passive metadata inspector for passphrase-encrypted node-key files — **reads the canonical 2-line encrypted-keyfile format without decrypting**. Distinct from `keyfile-decrypt` (which derives the unwrap key + invokes AES-GCM): `keyfile-info` parses only the header tag (line 1: `DETERM-NODE-V1`) and the AEAD envelope frame (line 2: dot-separated hex per `wallet/envelope.hpp`); calls `envelope::deserialize()` for header parsing then reports the envelope's metadata exactly as surfaced by `inspect-envelope` (format/version, PBKDF2 iteration count, salt + nonce hex, AAD presence + length, ciphertext + tag lengths) **plus** the keyfile-specific header tag. **No password required** — the entire inspection runs against the on-disk byte layout without any key derivation. Use cases: operators verifying a file is a valid keyfile before attempting a costly decrypt; pre-flight check that a backed-up keyfile artifact is structurally intact before scheduling a key rotation; forensic inspection of an archived keyfile when the original deployment is no longer available; debugging which keyfile corresponds to which deployment (PBKDF2 iteration count + salt hex are deployment-distinguishing fingerprints that don't require the passphrase). Default human output is a per-field listing (`header_tag=DETERM-NODE-V1`, `envelope_format=…`, `pbkdf2_iters=…`, `salt_hex=…`, `nonce_hex=…`, `aad_len=…`, `ciphertext_len=…`, `tag_len=…`) plus a summary `keyfile_metadata=OK (header=DETERM-NODE-V1 iters=… aad_len=…)` or `keyfile_metadata=BAD (reason=…)`; `--json` emits `{header_tag, envelope_format, envelope_version, pbkdf2_iters, salt_hex, nonce_hex, aad_present, aad_len, ciphertext_len, tag_len, file_size_bytes}`. Pure local computation — no daemon RPC required, no key material exposed (the private key never leaves the encrypted envelope; only structural metadata is reported). Exercised end-to-end by `tools/test_wallet_keyfile_info.sh` (~20-30 assertions covering happy-path metadata extraction on a `keyfile-create`-produced file, malformed-header rejection, truncated-envelope rejection, missing-line-2 rejection, JSON-output validity, file-not-found behavior). **Exit codes**: 0 metadata extracted, 1 missing/unreadable file / bad args, 2 malformed keyfile (header tag mismatch, envelope deserialization failure, line-count mismatch — operator alert gate that the file is not a valid `DETERM-NODE-V1` artifact and should not be expected to decrypt). |
| `determ-wallet derive-shared-secret --priv-keyfile <path> --pubkey <hex>` | X25519 Diffie-Hellman shared-secret agreement between two anon-address holders, for off-chain message encryption. Loads the operator's own private keyfile (single-account JSON `{address, privkey_hex}` shape — the same format `account-export` emits), parses the peer's 32-byte Ed25519 public key (`--pubkey <64-hex>`), then composes libsodium's Ed25519→Curve25519 transforms exclusively (no custom RFC 7748 reimplementation): `crypto_sign_ed25519_seed_keypair(priv_seed)` → 64-byte Ed25519 SK; `crypto_sign_ed25519_sk_to_curve25519(ed_sk)` → 32-byte X25519 SK (clamped per spec internally); `crypto_sign_ed25519_pk_to_curve25519(peer_pub)` → 32-byte X25519 PK; `crypto_scalarmult(out, my_x_sk, peer_x_pk)` → 32-byte shared secret. The shared secret is the symmetric DH output usable as a KDF input (e.g., HKDF-SHA-256) to key any AEAD that protects off-chain messages between the two parties; both sides compute the same secret independently from their own private key + the peer's public key (no on-the-wire handshake). Intermediate SK buffers (`ed_sk`, `my_x25519_sk`) are zeroed via `sodium_memzero` on every exit path including error branches. Output is one-line JSON `{"shared_secret_hex": "<64-hex>"}` on stdout. Pure local computation — no daemon RPC required, no network traffic. Use cases: anon-address-to-anon-address E2E off-chain channel bootstrap (each party can encrypt + decrypt with the same key derived from public on-chain identities); pre-computed channel keys for forward-secure off-chain DApp messaging; deterministic test fixtures for cross-party encryption protocols. **Symmetry contract**: `derive(k1, pub2) == derive(k2, pub1)` for any pair of valid Ed25519 keypairs (DH property; exercised by `tools/test_wallet_derive_shared_secret.sh`). **Small-subgroup-attack guard**: the output is asserted non-zero before returning — guards against the small-subgroup case where a malformed peer pubkey would yield an all-zero shared secret. **Exit codes**: 0 derive succeeded, 1 args/parse error (missing/malformed flags, bad hex length, peer pubkey not exactly 64 hex chars, keyfile unreadable, malformed keyfile JSON), 2 cryptographic failure (Ed25519→X25519 conversion failure for the peer's pubkey — the peer key is not in the Ed25519 group; X25519 scalarmult failure; all-zero output detection). |
| `determ-wallet encrypt-message --priv-keyfile <path> --peer-pubkey <hex> --in <file> --out <file>` | AES-256-GCM message encryption between two anon-address holders, layered on top of `derive-shared-secret`. Internally: (1) X25519 DH (same libsodium pipeline as `derive-shared-secret`) → 32-byte shared secret, (2) HKDF-SHA-256 with `info="DETERM-CHAT-AEAD-v1"` + symmetric pair-binding salt `byte-min(pubA, pubB) \|\| byte-max(pubA, pubB)` → 32-byte AEAD key, (3) generate fresh 12-byte random nonce, (4) AES-256-GCM encrypt the input file, (5) write output = `nonce(12) \|\| ciphertext_with_tag(N+16)`. The symmetric pair-binding salt ensures both sides compute the same AEAD key regardless of which initiates. Ephemeral X25519 SK + AEAD-key buffers are zeroed via `sodium_memzero` on every exit path including error branches. Stdout emits `{"status":"ok","out":"<path>","ciphertext_bytes":N}` on success. **Fresh-nonce contract**: each encrypt invocation generates a new random nonce, so encrypting the same plaintext twice produces different ciphertexts (exercised by `tools/test_wallet_message_aead.sh`). Use cases: E2E encrypted off-chain channels between anon-address holders, asynchronous encrypted DM, signed-encrypted bundles for DApp request payloads. **Exit codes**: 0 encrypt succeeded, 1 args/parse error / input file unreadable / output file unwritable, 2 cryptographic failure (X25519 conversion or scalarmult error; AES-GCM error). |
| `determ-wallet decrypt-message --priv-keyfile <path> --peer-pubkey <hex> --in <file> --out <file>` | Paired inverse to `encrypt-message`. Recovers the AEAD key via the same X25519 + HKDF pipeline (the symmetric pair-binding salt is the key trick: `derive(k1, pub2) == derive(k2, pub1)` so the receiver — using their own privkey + the sender's pubkey — derives an identical AEAD key as the sender did), reads `nonce(12) \|\| ciphertext_with_tag(N+16)` from the input file, AES-256-GCM decrypts with tag verification, writes plaintext to output file. Stdout emits `{"status":"ok","out":"<path>","plaintext_bytes":N}` on success, or `{"status":"error","reason":"aead_tag_verify_failed"}` on tag-verify failure (tampered ciphertext, tampered nonce, wrong peer pubkey, or wrong private key) — exit code 2 in that case. Ephemeral X25519 SK + AEAD-key buffers are zeroed via `sodium_memzero` on every exit path. Binary-safe (preserves NUL bytes + full byte(range(256)) round-trip). Test-suite: `tools/test_wallet_message_aead.sh` covers happy-path round-trip, tamper rejection (ciphertext byte flip + nonce byte flip), wrong-peer-pubkey rejection, binary round-trip with NUL bytes + 0..255 byte range, fresh-nonce sanity (same plaintext encrypted twice yields different ciphertexts). **Exit codes**: 0 decrypt succeeded, 1 args/parse error / input file unreadable / output file unwritable, 2 cryptographic failure (X25519 conversion error; AES-GCM tag-verify failed — operator alert gate that the message is tampered or wrong-key). |
| `determ-wallet sign-arbitrary --priv-keyfile <path> --msg <inline> \| --msg-file <path> [--out <file>] [--detached] [--bundle]` | Detached Ed25519 signature on an arbitrary text/binary message, domain-separated from consensus transaction signing. Computes `signing_bytes = "DETERM-MSG-v1" \|\| msg_bytes` (literal concatenation — Ed25519's internal SHA-512 handles digest), signs via `crypto_sign_detached`. `--detached` (default) writes 64-byte hex to stdout OR raw 64 bytes to `--out` file. `--bundle` writes self-contained JSON `{address, ed_pub_hex, domain, msg_b64, sig_hex}` — a verifiable artifact that pins the domain separator as part of the bundle (so a forged bundle with a swapped domain fails the paired `verify-arbitrary --bundle` check). Distinct from existing `message-sign` (operator-supplied tag + SHA-256 commitment) — `sign-arbitrary` uses fixed `"DETERM-MSG-v1"` domain + raw-message Ed25519 sign, suitable for cross-anon-address attestations + signed off-chain statements. **Exit codes**: 0 sign succeeded, 1 args/parse error, 2 cryptographic failure. |
| `determ-wallet verify-arbitrary --ed-pub <hex32> --msg <inline> \| --msg-file <path> --sig-hex <hex64> \| --bundle <path>` | Paired inverse to `sign-arbitrary`. Detached mode (`--ed-pub` + `--msg`/`--msg-file` + `--sig-hex`) re-computes `signing_bytes = "DETERM-MSG-v1" \|\| msg_bytes` and calls `crypto_sign_verify_detached`. Bundle mode (`--bundle <path>`) parses the JSON envelope, pins `domain == "DETERM-MSG-v1"` (any other value → INVALID; blocks an attacker substituting their own domain), verifies the sig over the bundled msg under the bundled pubkey. Emits one-line JSON `{"status":"ok","result":"VALID"\|"INVALID"}` on stdout. Test-suite: `tools/test_wallet_message_sign_verify.sh` covers 48 assertions across 25 scenarios — round-trip on text + binary, detached + bundle output modes, raw-binary `--out` file is exactly 64 bytes, tamper sig/msg/pubkey all INVALID + exit 2, **domain-separator pin** (sig over `"X"` does NOT verify against `--msg "DETERM-MSG-v1X"`), bundle tamper across sig_hex / msg_b64 / domain, determinism (RFC 8032). **Exit codes**: 0 VALID, 1 args/parse error, 2 INVALID (sig + key + msg combination doesn't verify — operator alert gate that the signed-message artifact is tampered or wrong-key). |
| `determ-wallet anon-batch-balance --rpc-port N --addresses <list>\|@<file> [--include-nonce] [--include-stake] [--json]` | Batch query of balances + (optional) nonces + stakes for a list of anon addresses. Builds ONE TCP connection to the daemon and pipelines per-address RPCs: `status` for the envelope's `chain_height`, then `balance` (always) + `nonce` (with `--include-nonce`) + `stake_info` (with `--include-stake`) per address. Addresses can be inline comma-separated or `@<file>` (one per line; supports `#` comments + blank lines). Address normalization: mixed-case input is lowercased to canonical form before query (S-028 closure). `exists` per address = balance > 0 OR (with `--include-nonce`) nonce > 0 OR (with `--include-stake`) stake > 0 — picks up addresses with activity even at zero current balance. Default JSON output: `{rpc_port, chain_height, addresses: [{address, balance, nonce?, stake?, exists}], summary: {total_addresses, total_balance, total_stake, exists_count}}`. Pure read-only — no mutation. Use cases: wallet-UI portfolio aggregation across many anon addresses; operator-side accounting for known bearer-address sets; CI fixtures verifying a multi-address scenario. **Exit codes**: 0 batch query succeeded, 1 args/parse error / RPC connection refused / malformed address list. |
| `determ-wallet cold-sign --tx-json <file> --priv-keyfile <path> [--out <file>] [--allow-stdout] [--force]` | Offline transaction signing for the air-gapped cold-wallet workflow. The hot machine prepares an UNSIGNED tx JSON; transfers it (USB / QR) to the cold machine; cold machine runs `cold-sign` (no RPC, no daemon, no network); transfers the signed JSON back; hot machine submits. Loads priv keyfile (single-account JSON `{address, privkey_hex}` — same format `account-export` emits). Computes canonical `signing_bytes` per `Transaction::signing_bytes` (matches the chain's apply-side canonical encoding byte-for-byte: `type:u8`, `from:utf8+NUL`, `to:utf8+NUL`, `amount/fee/nonce:u64-BE`, `payload:raw`). Ed25519 signs via libsodium; reports `tx_hash_hex = SHA-256(signing_bytes)`. Writes signed tx JSON (with `signature` field) to `--out` at mode 0600; refuses stdout output by default (`--allow-stdout` opt-in as exfil-guard); refuses overwrite without `--force`. **Refusal modes**: `tx_already_signed` (sig field present + non-empty + non-zero-placeholder), `keyfile_address_mismatch` (keyfile.address ≠ tx.from — defense against signing someone else's tx), `output_exists` (output file exists without `--force`) — each emits structured `{status:"error", reason:"<code>"}` + exit 1. Ephemeral priv_seed + sk scrubbed via `sodium_memzero` on every exit path including error branches. Sig parity verified cross-binary against Python `cryptography.Ed25519` (deterministic per RFC 8032). Round-tripped via `tx-sign-verify` — the sibling verifier accepts cold-signed envelopes. Pure local computation. Use cases: high-value transfers from air-gapped storage; multi-sig coordination; HSM-staged signing. **Exit codes**: 0 signed, 1 args / keyfile / output error or refusal mode, 2 cryptographic failure (libsodium error). |
| `determ-wallet account-list --keyfiles-dir <path> [--recursive] [--include-encrypted=on\|off] [--include-plaintext=on\|off] [--json]` | Enumerate keyfiles in a directory with per-file metadata. Classifies each regular file as plaintext-single (`{address, privkey_hex}` from `account-export` or `keyfile-decrypt`'s `{pubkey, priv_seed}` shape), plaintext-batch (array from `account-create-batch` / `account-derive-batch`), encrypted-DETERM-NODE-V1 (passphrase-wrapped via `keyfile-create`), or unknown/skip. For plaintext: extracts address (or array of addresses for batch). For encrypted: extracts header tag + PBKDF2 iters + salt_hex + nonce_hex — same metadata `keyfile-info` reports, no decrypt performed. Per-entry: path, type, size_bytes, mode (POSIX 0600 / Windows "n/a"). Sorted by path. `--recursive` walks subdirectories; default is shallow. `--include-encrypted` / `--include-plaintext` filter the output. Warnings in summary: `mode_not_0600` (POSIX security concern), `mixed_encrypted_and_plaintext_in_same_dir` (operator hygiene). Pure local computation — no daemon RPC. Use cases: operator audit of a multi-account deployment; inventory of cold-storage keyfile directories; pre-rotation discovery sweep. **Exit codes**: 0 enumerated, 1 args / unreadable dir. |
| `determ-wallet validator-roster-snapshot --rpc-port N --out <file> [--include-stake-history] [--force] [--json]` | Point-in-time JSON snapshot of the active validator set for offline audit / monitoring / diff tooling. Reuses the existing `rpc_call_over_socket` helper: opens ONE TCP connection and pipelines `status` (for `chain_height` + `chain_id`) + `validators` (for the roster) + optionally per-validator `stake_info` calls. Atomic write: writes to `--out + ".tmp"` then renames to `--out`. Refuses to overwrite existing `--out` without `--force`. Envelope: `{snapshot_format_version: 1, captured_at_unix: <ts>, rpc_port, chain_height, chain_id, total_validators, total_stake_locked, validators: [{rank, domain, ed_pub, region, active_from, [stake_locked, accumulated_slashed]}, ...]}`. The `validators[]` array is sorted by ascending `rank` for stable diff-friendly output across snapshots. `--include-stake-history` adds the `stake_locked` + `accumulated_slashed` fields per row (one extra `stake_info` RPC per validator; off by default for lighter snapshots). Distinct from `stake-bulk-query` (which targets a specific list of validator domains for active query): `validator-roster-snapshot` captures the ENTIRE active validator set in canonical sort order. Use cases: operator-dashboard versioned validator-set artifact for diff over time (REGISTER / DEREGISTER / region churn), CI / regression fixtures pinning a known-good roster, post-snapshot bootstrap validation (compare bootstrapped node's roster against a snapshot of the donor). **Exit codes**: 0 success, 1 args/parse error (missing flags, output file exists without `--force`, RPC connection refused). Exercised by `tools/test_wallet_validator_roster_snapshot.sh` (~37 assertions covering envelope structure, sort-by-rank ordering, chain_height parity with `determ status`, per-validator domain cross-check with `determ validators --json`, `--include-stake-history` field addition, `--force` overwrite semantics, atomic-write no-.tmp-leftover guarantee, bad-port diagnostic). |
| `determ-wallet committee-signature-verify --block <file> --committee <file> --block-digest <hex> [--json]` | Offline Ed25519 verification of K-of-K committee signatures against an operator-supplied `--block-digest` pin. Sibling to the chain-daemon `determ verify-block-sigs` CLI but runs on the wallet binary so operators can audit blocks without touching a running daemon — pure local computation with no library link to the chain implementation. Accepts the canonical `Block::to_json` shape in two envelope forms: bare object or `{block: {...}}` wrapper (output of `determ block-info --json`). Accepts the committee in three shapes: bare array, `{members: [...]}`, or `{validators: [{domain, ed_pub_hex}, ...]}` (matches `determ validators --json`). Each `creators[i]` is looked up in the committee map; per-creator signatures in `block.creator_block_sigs[i]` (parallel array; 128-zero-hex sentinel = abstention, counted as `missing` not `failure`) are verified via libsodium's `crypto_sign_verify_detached` against the supplied 64-hex `--block-digest`. Quorum rule: `valid_count >= ceil(2 * present_count / 3)` (matches the chain's BFT-mode required-sigs formula). Default human output: per-signer table (domain / sig_present / valid) + summary footer (committee_size, present_count, valid_count, missing_count, abstention_count). `--json` emits `{committee_size, present_count, valid_count, missing_count, abstention_count, per_signer: [{domain, sig_present, valid}], quorum_pass: bool}`. **Exit codes**: 0 quorum met + all signatures valid (or abstention sentinels), 1 args/parse error / missing committee entry for any creator / malformed block / unreadable file, 2 quorum NOT met (operator alert gate — block fails K-of-K threshold; either insufficient signatures or wrong digest). Use cases: offline audit of a fetched block (cold-wallet workflow), CI fixture for verify-block-sigs cross-binary parity, third-party verification against a committee from `validators --json` snapshot. Exercised end-to-end by `tools/test_wallet_committee_signature_verify.sh` (~29 assertions covering happy-path PASS, tampered-digest FAIL, missing-committee-entry diagnostic, abstention sentinel handling, JSON shape, both envelope forms, all four required-arg validations, malformed-hex rejection). |
| `determ-wallet bft-quorum --committee-size <K> [--mode md\|bft] [--pool <P>] [--aborts <A>] [--threshold <T>] [--bft-enabled] [--json]` | Offline calculator for the chain's two-level BFT committee + block-signature quorum arithmetic (no daemon, no crypto, no IO). Reproduces byte-for-byte `node.cpp::start_new_round` (escalation gate), `producer.cpp::required_block_sigs` (Q sig floor), and the validator accept gate (sentinel slack = eff − Q). `k_bft = (2K+2)/3 = ⌈2K/3⌉`; escalate ⟺ `pool<K ∧ --bft-enabled ∧ aborts≥threshold ∧ pool≥k_bft`; `eff = escalate ? k_bft : K`; `Q = (mode==bft)?⌈2·eff/3⌉:eff`. `--mode` forces a mode and skips the gate; `--pool` defaults to K; `--threshold` defaults to 5 (genesis default). Human + one-line-JSON output. Sibling to `committee-signature-verify` (which verifies committee Ed25519 sigs against a daemon-pinned digest): `bft-quorum` instead computes the K→k_bft→Q committee/quorum shrinkage and evaluates the escalation gate, with no crypto. Exercised by `tools/test_wallet_bft_quorum.sh` (~24 assertions recomputing every expected value independently in Python across K=3,6,9 in MD/forced-BFT plus all four escalation-gate branches). **Exit codes**: 0 computed, 1 args/range error. |
| `determ-wallet verify-equivocation --pubkey <hex64> (--digest-a <hex64> --sig-a <hex128> --digest-b <hex64> --sig-b <hex128> \| --event <file> [--index <N>]) [--json]` | Offline FA6 equivocation-evidence verifier — confirms the `EquivocationEvent` two-sig proof (`include/determ/chain/block.hpp`) that the chain slashes the equivocator's entire stake on. Reproduces `src/node/validator.cpp::check_equivocation_events` byte-for-byte: PROVEN ⟺ `digest_a != digest_b` ∧ `sig_a != sig_b` ∧ both sigs verify over their OWN 32-byte digest against the equivocator's operator-pinned Ed25519 `--pubkey` via libsodium `crypto_sign_verify_detached`. The forensic counterpart to `committee-signature-verify` (which verifies K-of-K sigs over ONE digest; this verifies ONE key over TWO conflicting digests) — lets anyone independently confirm a slashing was justified BEFORE trusting the chain applied it. Evidence is supplied either inline as the five hex artifacts (`--pubkey`/`--digest-a`/`--sig-a`/`--digest-b`/`--sig-b`; digests 64-hex / sigs 128-hex, the same widths `EquivocationEvent::from_json` enforces) OR via `--event <file>` pointing at an `EquivocationEvent` JSON (`equivocator`/`block_index`/`digest_a`/`sig_a`/`digest_b`/`sig_b` shape) or a Block whose `equivocation_events[N]` is checked (`--index`, default 0; also unwraps a `{block:{...}}` envelope). `--event` is mutually exclusive with the inline hex args. `--pubkey` is ALWAYS operator-supplied (bound by the beacon-anchored registry — `determ validators --json` or the equivocator's registry entry — never read from the untrusted evidence, which names the domain but not the key); `equivocator`/`block_index` from an `--event` source are echoed into the output but not trusted for the crypto check. Pure local computation: no daemon, no RPC, no chain-library link. Default human output is a PROVEN/NOT-PROVEN line plus a field table (pubkey, digest_a/b, distinct_digests, distinct_sigs, sig_a_valid, sig_b_valid); `--json` emits `{proven, distinct_digests, distinct_sigs, sig_a_valid, sig_b_valid, pubkey_hex, digest_a_hex, digest_b_hex[, equivocator, block_index]}`. Distinct from the light-client `determ-light verify-equivocation` (separate binary; light has only the `--in <file>`/stdin form with optional `--committee` key-resolution, whereas the wallet adds the inline five-hex form and `--event`/`--index` Block-array selection). Exercised end-to-end by `tools/test_wallet_verify_equivocation.sh` (16 sections / ~30 assertions covering happy-path PROVEN, JSON shape, tampered-sig + wrong-pubkey NOT-PROVEN with per-sig validity flags, the same-digest non-equivocation case (`distinct_digests=false`), identical-pair (`distinct_sigs=false`), bare-event + Block + `--index` `--event` forms, out-of-range `--index`, missing `--pubkey`, `--event`/inline mutual exclusion, and malformed-hex / missing-file arg errors). **Exit codes**: 0 PROVEN, 2 NOT PROVEN (auth-style alert — a sig failed to verify or the two digests/sigs are identical), 1 args / parse / IO error. |
| `determ-wallet stake-bulk-query --rpc-port N --domains <list>\|@<file> [--json]` | Batch validator stake-info query for many domain names against a running daemon. Reuses the `rpc_call_over_socket` helper from `anon-batch-balance` for socket pipelining: opens ONE TCP connection and pipelines `status` (for `chain_height`) + `validators` (for cross-referencing exists/not-exists) + per-domain `stake_info` over it. `--domains` accepts comma-separated inline (`alice.v,bob.v,charlie.v`) or `@<path>` (one per line; `#` comments + blank lines skipped — operator passes a flat-file roster). Default output: human-readable table sorted by `stake_locked` descending (`domain` / `stake_locked` / `accumulated_slashed` / `active_from` / `region` / `ed_pub` / `exists` columns) + summary footer. `--json` emits `{rpc_port, chain_height, domains: [{domain, stake_locked, accumulated_slashed, active_from, region, ed_pub, exists}], summary: {total_domains, total_stake_locked, total_accumulated_slashed, exists_count}}`. Per-row `exists = true` iff the domain is in the active validator registry OR has non-zero `stake_locked`. `accumulated_slashed` is chain-global today (per-domain accounting deferred to a future tracking improvement); surfaces as 0 per row in the wire format. Distinct from `anon-batch-balance` (which targets ANON addresses + balance/nonce/stake): `stake-bulk-query` targets validator DOMAINS + full stake info. Use cases: operator-dashboard portfolio of known validator set, on-call audit of a subset of mainnet validators in one shot, CI fixtures verifying multi-validator scenarios. **Exit codes**: 0 success, 1 args/parse error / RPC connection refused / malformed domain list. Exercised by `tools/test_wallet_stake_bulk_query.sh` (~43 assertions covering help text, missing-arg diagnostics, unreachable-port handling, JSON envelope shape, chain_height vs `determ status` parity, per-domain stake_locked vs `determ stake_info` parity, `@<file>` parser with comments+blanks, non-existent-domain handling, DESC sort ordering of default table output). |
| `determ-wallet batch-nonce-assign --in <file> --start <N> --out <file> [--force]` | Sequential nonce assignment (E2 R40) — the **nonce-prep step BEFORE `tx-batch-sign`** in the payroll / airdrop batch flow. `tx-batch-sign` signs a batch but does NOT assign nonces; an operator with N transfers from one account needs each record to carry a distinct sequential nonce, and this command stamps them so the operator doesn't hand-edit N records. Reads a top-level JSON array of unsigned tx records; for each element `i ∈ [0, len)` sets `record[i].nonce = start + i` (OVERWRITING any pre-existing nonce), preserving input order and every other field verbatim; writes the nonce-assigned array — drop-in for `tx-batch-sign --in`. **Pure data transform**: no keyfile, no signing, no crypto. The compose chain is `determ account nonce <D>` (fetch the account's current on-chain nonce) → `determ-wallet batch-nonce-assign --start <n>` (this command) → `determ-wallet tx-batch-sign` (sign) → `determ-wallet verify-batch` / `validate-tx` (confirm). Validates `--in` is a JSON array, `--start` is a non-negative integer, each element is a JSON object; empty input array → empty output array (exit 0). **Determinism**: same input + same `--start` → byte-identical output (only the nonce field is mutated; nlohmann::json preserves key order). Refuses to overwrite an existing `--out` without `--force`. Pure local computation — no daemon RPC required. Exercised end-to-end by `tools/test_wallet_batch_nonce_assign.sh` (31 assertions covering sequential assignment from various `--start` values, input-order preservation, overwrite of pre-existing nonces, every-other-field pass-through, empty-array edge case, determinism across runs, non-array / non-object / negative-start rejection, `--force` overwrite semantics, drop-in round-trip into `tx-batch-sign`). **Exit codes**: 0 nonces assigned, 1 args/parse error (missing/malformed flags, malformed input JSON, non-array top level, negative `--start`, output exists without `--force`). |
| `determ-wallet tx-batch-sign --keyfile <path> --in <file> --out <file> [--passphrase-env NAME \| --passphrase-from <spec>] [--force] [--json]` | Batch-mode offline signer for payroll / airdrop / settlement workflows (R39+1 A2). Reads a JSON array of N tx-input records (`[{type:"TRANSFER"\|"STAKE"\|"UNSTAKE", from, to, amount, fee, nonce}, …]`), signs each record locally via the same canonical `signing_bytes` schema as `sign-anon-tx` / `cold-sign`, and emits a parallel JSON array of N signed envelopes — single process invocation, N signatures, no per-tx subprocess spawn cost. Keyfile handling: plaintext canonical `{address, privkey_hex}` (the `sign-anon-tx` shape), plaintext alternate `{ed_priv_hex, ed_pub_hex, anon_address}`, or encrypted DETERM-NODE-V1 (auto-detected by sniffing line 1; requires `--passphrase-env <NAME>` convenience alias or the existing `--passphrase-from <spec>` form). Order-preserving (`output[i]` corresponds to `input[i]`). Refuses to overwrite an existing `--out` target unless `--force` is supplied. Output records match `Transaction::to_json` shape (`{type:<int>, from, to, amount, fee, nonce, payload:"", sig, hash}`); each signed envelope round-trips byte-for-byte through `determ-wallet validate-tx` + `determ submit-tx`. Pure local signing — no daemon RPC required. Use cases: payroll, airdrop batches, gambling-industry settlement, post-snapshot bootstrap funding from a cold-signed batch staged ahead of time. Exercised end-to-end by `tools/test_wallet_tx_batch_sign.sh` (38 assertions covering empty-input edge case, single-tx + 3-tx batches, order preservation, sig-determinism for identical inputs, passphrase-locked keyfile via DETERM_PASSPHRASE env, STAKE / UNSTAKE / TRANSFER type-string coverage, output type field numeric per `to_json` shape, malformed-JSON / missing-field / wrong-type / mismatched-from rejection, --force overwrite semantics, output file 0600-style perms). **Exit codes**: 0 batch signed, 1 args/parse error (missing/malformed flags, malformed input JSON, keyfile-load failure, output exists without `--force`, validation rejection), 2 cryptographic failure (Ed25519 sign error, passphrase-decryption failure on encrypted keyfile). |
| `determ-wallet verify-batch --in <file> [--strict] [--json]` | Batch signature + envelope verification (D2 R40) — the **read-dual of `tx-batch-sign`**. Reads a JSON array of N signed tx envelopes (the `tx-batch-sign` output shape: `{type, from, to, amount, fee, nonce, payload, sig, hash}`) and verifies each one independently via the same single-envelope gate as `validate-tx`: structural well-formedness + `signing_bytes` recompute + `hash` match (catches the hash-substitution sub-attack — body mutated after signing) + Ed25519 `crypto_sign_verify_detached` under the pubkey derived from each envelope's OWN `from` field (so verifying `e_i` never consults `e_j` — no cross-envelope channel). Reports a per-envelope verdict (valid / the specific failure reason) and a summary `N_valid / N_total`. Order-preserving (verdict `i` corresponds to input `i`). **`--strict` gates the exit code**: with `--strict`, any invalid envelope causes a non-zero exit (exit 3); without it (report-only default), the command reports per-envelope verdicts and exits 0 even when some envelopes are invalid (the operator reads the report). Pure local verification — no daemon RPC required, no key material loaded (verification uses only public-key recovery from the `from` field). `--json` emits `{total, valid, results: [{index, valid, reason}, …]}`. Soundness proof: `docs/proofs/BatchSigningSoundness.md` BS-3 (verify-batch = N independent `validate-tx`; a forged/mutated envelope is reported valid with probability ≤ 2⁻¹²⁸ under A1 + A2; no cross-envelope contamination). Use cases: pre-submit verification of a `tx-batch-sign` output before broadcasting a payroll/airdrop batch, CI gate for batch-signing pipelines, audit of a received batch. Exercised end-to-end by `tools/test_wallet_verify_batch.sh` (43 assertions covering mixed valid/invalid batches, per-envelope verdict parity with single `validate-tx`, `--strict` exit-3 gating vs report-only default, hash-substitution rejection, tampered-body rejection, JSON-output validity). **Exit codes**: 0 verification completed (report-only default — even with invalid envelopes present) OR `--strict` AND every envelope valid; 1 args/parse error (missing/malformed `--in`, malformed input JSON); 3 `--strict` AND ≥1 invalid envelope (operator alert gate). |
| `determ-wallet tx-batch-summary --in <file> [--json]` | Read-only aggregate analytics over a tx array (F2 R40) — a reporting-only complement to the batch-signing flow (`batch-nonce-assign` → `tx-batch-sign` → `verify-batch`). Reads a JSON array of tx records (signed envelopes OR unsigned inputs — it reads only the common `{type, from, to, amount, fee, nonce}` fields, so it works at any stage of the batch pipeline) and emits aggregate statistics: total record count, per-type breakdown (TRANSFER / STAKE / UNSTAKE / …), total + min/max/mean `amount` and `fee`, distinct-`from` and distinct-`to` counts, and the nonce range per sender (useful for spotting a gap or duplicate before `tx-batch-sign` stamps the batch). **Pure read-only computation**: no keyfile, no signing, no verification, no daemon RPC — it neither mutates the input nor checks signatures (use `verify-batch` for that). Order-independent (a pure fold over the array). `--json` emits a structured `{count, by_type: {...}, amount: {total, min, max, mean}, fee: {total, min, max, mean}, distinct_from, distinct_to, nonce_ranges: {...}}` envelope for monitoring / pipeline ingestion. Composes the batch flow: run it on a `batch-nonce-assign` output to sanity-check the nonce sequence + total payout before signing, or on a received batch to summarize it before `verify-batch`. Exercised end-to-end by `tools/test_wallet_tx_batch_summary.sh` (63 assertions covering per-type tallies, amount/fee aggregates, distinct-address counts, nonce-range computation, empty-array edge case, mixed-type batches, determinism across runs, malformed-JSON / non-array rejection). **Exit codes**: 0 summary emitted, 1 args/parse error (missing/malformed `--in`, malformed input JSON, non-array top level). |
| `determ-wallet param-change-build --name <P> (--value <N> \| --value-hex <hex>) --effective-height <H> --nonce <N> --from <domain-or-addr> [--fee <N>] [--out <file> \| --allow-stdout] [--json]` | Offline **A5 governance PARAM_CHANGE transaction builder** (R41 G2). Assembles the canonical PARAM_CHANGE payload + the chain's `Transaction::signing_bytes`, computes `tx_hash = SHA-256(signing_bytes)`, and emits the **unsigned** canonical tx JSON (numeric `type=6`, `sig_count=0`, 128-zero-hex `sig` placeholder) plus the `keyholder_sig_message_hex` preimage that each of the K-of-K governance keyholders signs out-of-band (the N-of-N keyholder threshold is applied separately, not by this tool). Purely offline — no RPC, no secret material loaded. `--name` is checked against the on-chain governance whitelist (off-list names rejected with a diagnostic citing the whitelist, mirroring `GovernanceWhitelistSoundness.md` GW-1); `--value` takes a u64 rendered as 8-byte LE, or `--value-hex` passes raw value bytes verbatim (mutually exclusive); anon-shape `--from` is S-028 case-validated. Output goes to `--out <file>` or, with explicit `--allow-stdout`, to stdout. Cross-checks against the sibling `derive-tx-hash --check` (byte-identical signing_bytes encoder). Shipped in place of the originally-scoped `state-root --snapshot` (which `snapshot-verify` already covers, and which `determ-wallet` cannot do in-process since it deliberately does not link the chain library — TCB separation). Exercised by `tools/test_wallet_state_root.sh` (31 assertions: whitelist enforcement, 8-byte LE encoding, type/sig_count/hash shape, S-028 rejection, determinism, derive-tx-hash cross-check). **Exit codes**: 0 tx built, 1 args/validation error (missing flags, off-whitelist name, mutually-exclusive value flags, S-028 case violation, output exists / no output sink). |
| `determ-wallet param-change-lint (--name <P> --value-hex <hex> \| --tx-json <file>) [--json]` | Offline **build-time PARAM_CHANGE effectiveness lint** — the wallet-side dual of `tools/operator_param_activation_preflight.sh` (which audits already-staged on-chain entries at runtime). Predicts, BEFORE the tx is submitted, whether activation actually mutates the intended consensus scalar or silently no-ops. Reimplements two source rules (TCB separation, no chain-library link): the `validator.cpp` `kWhitelist` (9 names) and the `chain.cpp::activate_pending_params` width rule — the three numeric chain-scalars `MIN_STAKE`/`SUSPENSION_SLASH`/`UNSTAKE_DELAY` are decoded by a `parse_u64` requiring **exactly 8 bytes** (`value.size()!=8` → the scalar is never written → silent no-op at activation). Verdicts: **EFFECTIVE** (8-byte numeric scalar) / **INERT_BAD_WIDTH** (whitelisted numeric scalar, value ≠ 8 bytes — the trap) / **HOOK_ONLY** (whitelisted but hook-forwarded — effect depends on the Node hook) / **UNKNOWN_NAME** (off-whitelist — validator rejects the tx). `--tx-json` DECODES the authoritative on-chain `payload` (`name_len‖name‖value_len‖value‖…`) from a `param-change-build` output rather than trusting a convenience field. Strict hex validation (the shared `from_hex` is lenient). Exercised by `tools/test_wallet_param_change_lint.sh` (25 offline assertions). **Exit codes**: 0 EFFECTIVE/HOOK_ONLY, 2 INERT_BAD_WIDTH/UNKNOWN_NAME, 1 args/parse error. |
| `determ-wallet param-change-verify --tx-json <file> --keyholders <file> [--threshold N] [--json]` | Offline **read-only K-of-K governance multisig verifier** on an ASSEMBLED PARAM_CHANGE — the verification counterpart to `param-change-build` (body + per-keyholder signing preimage) and `param-change-lint` (effectiveness), completing the governance flow's check side. Reimplements the validator's multisig gate (`src/node/validator.cpp:688-725`): each `(keyholder_index, ed_sig)` pair in the tx payload must Ed25519-verify under the keyholder's pubkey over the canonical `sig_msg = name_len(u8)‖name‖value_len(u16 LE)‖value‖effective_height(u64 LE)`; indices distinct + in range; `good_sigs ≥ threshold`. The keyholder pubkey set + threshold are on-chain governance state not carried in the tx, so the operator supplies them via `--keyholders` (a JSON array of 32-byte pubkey hex, or `{keyholders:[...], threshold:N}`); `--threshold` overrides; absent both, the conservative default requires ALL keyholders. Pure local libsodium `crypto_sign_verify_detached` — read-only (verifies sigs, never produces them; fits the wallet's `verify-equivocation`/`verify-dapp-registration`/`committee-signature-verify` family), no chain-library link, no RPC, no secret material. Lets an operator confirm an out-of-band-assembled multisig PARAM_CHANGE is valid before submission. Exercised by `tools/test_wallet_param_change_verify.sh` (10 offline assertions incl. a cross-implementation reference — an independent Python Ed25519 plays the keyholders — happy path / threshold boundary / tampered-sig / duplicate-index / out-of-range / wrong-keys / 24-scenario fuzz). **Exit codes**: 0 PASS, 2 threshold-not-met / invalid sig / duplicate-or-out-of-range index, 1 args/parse error. |
| `determ-wallet supply-audit --snapshot <file>` (alias `--in <file>`) `[--json]` | Offline **A1 unitary-supply identity audit** of a snapshot JSON (R41 H2). Recomputes the identity by parsing the snapshot directly with nlohmann::json (determ-wallet does NOT link the chain library — TCB separation): sums `accounts[].balance` + `stakes[].locked` for `live_total`, reads the `c:` counters for `expected_total = genesis_total + accumulated_subsidy + accumulated_inbound − accumulated_slashed − accumulated_outbound`, and reports BALANCED iff `live_total == expected_total`. The balance *decision* uses the algebraically-equivalent all-additive rearrangement `live + slashed + outbound == genesis + subsidy + inbound` (in `__uint128_t` when available) so a corrupt snapshot cannot underflow-wrap uint64 and mask a violation; the chain's exact modular `expected_total` is still reported verbatim for fidelity. Offline only, no RPC, no keyfile. `--json` emits `{balanced, expected_total, live_total, accumulated_slashed, ...}`. Soundness companion: `docs/proofs/SupplyInvariantComposition.md` (SI-1 apply-preservation, SI-2 snapshot round-trip). Exercised by `tools/test_wallet_supply_audit.sh` (38 assertions incl. balanced / violated / underflow-trap / malformed-JSON fixtures). **Exit codes**: 0 balanced, 1 args/file/parse error, 2 A1 VIOLATED (operator alert gate). |
| `determ-wallet subsidy-schedule --block-subsidy <S> --to-height <H> [--from-height <F>] [--from-accumulated <A>] [--pool-initial <P>] [--genesis-total <G>] [--json]` | Offline **FLAT / E4 block-subsidy emission-curve projector** — the forward dual of `supply-audit`. Projects the subsidy issuance schedule from genesis-pinned parameters alone (no daemon, no snapshot, no RPC), replicating the chain's per-block subsidy rule (`src/chain/chain.cpp::apply_transactions` ~L1250-1272): `subsidy_this_block = pool_initial==0 ? block_subsidy : min(block_subsidy, pool_initial − accumulated_subsidy)`. determ-wallet does NOT link the chain library (TCB separation), so the rule is reimplemented over plain integers. Reports, at the `--to-height` horizon: `subsidy_per_block_now`, `cumulative_subsidy`, `accumulated_subsidy` (= `--from-accumulated` + cumulative), `pool_remaining` (or `unlimited` when perpetual), and — for an E4 finite fund (`--pool-initial > 0`) — whether and WHERE the fund drains (`drain_height = from_height + drain_in_blocks`, `final_partial_subsidy` = the partial tail mint that exhausts the fund). With `--genesis-total <G>`, also reports `projected_total_supply = G + cumulative` (the A1 additive subsidy term). All accumulation is `__uint128_t`-wide where available; sets `overflows_u64` when the projection exceeds 2^64−1 (where the node's own uint64 counters would themselves wrap) — fidelity over silent wrapping. E3 LOTTERY (`subsidy_mode==1`) keeps the SAME expected issuance schedule (expected per-block == FLAT S), so the projection is exact for FLAT and holds in-expectation for LOTTERY; the per-block jackpot draw is seeded by unpredictable commit-reveal randomness and is intentionally not projected. Distinct from `supply-audit` (which recomputes a captured snapshot's A1 conservation identity BACKWARD and reports balanced/VIOLATED): `subsidy-schedule` projects the emission curve FORWARD. `--json` emits `{block_subsidy, from_height, to_height, blocks_projected, from_accumulated, pool_initial, perpetual, subsidy_per_block_now, cumulative_subsidy_at_horizon, accumulated_subsidy_at_horizon, pool_remaining_at_horizon, drains, drain_height?, drain_in_blocks?, final_partial_subsidy?, paying_blocks_in_window, genesis_total, projected_total_supply, overflows_u64}`. Pure deterministic offline arithmetic. Use cases: tokenomics modelling of an E4 finite subsidy fund's exhaustion height, projecting forward from a snapshot's `accumulated_subsidy`, CI fixtures pinning a known emission curve. Exercised by `tools/test_wallet_subsidy_schedule.sh` (~30 assertions independently recomputing the emission curve in Python across perpetual / finite-exact-multiple / partial-tail / short- and long-horizon / `--from-accumulated` / zero-subsidy / u64-overflow / determinism / JSON-shape cases). **Exit codes**: 0 schedule projected, 1 args/range error (missing `--block-subsidy`/`--to-height`, non-decimal arg, `--to-height < --from-height`). |
| `determ-wallet state-proof-verify --in <proof.json> --root <hex64> [--json]` | Offline **Merkle state-proof verifier** (R41 I2) — the wallet-side dual of the daemon's `state_proof` RPC and `determ-light verify-state-proof`. Parses a state-proof JSON (`key_bytes` / `value_hash` / `target_index` / `leaf_count` / `proof[]` per PROTOCOL.md §10.2), recomputes the Merkle root, and reports VALID/INVALID against the operator-supplied `--root` (the trust anchor — the proof's self-asserted `state_root` is cross-checked and reported, never trusted). Fully offline: no RPC, no subprocess. Because determ-wallet deliberately does NOT link the chain library (TCB separation), the verify path is reimplemented **byte-for-byte** inline using OpenSSL SHA-256 — `leaf_hash = SHA-256(0x00 ‖ u32_be(key_len) ‖ key ‖ value_hash)`, `inner_hash = SHA-256(0x01 ‖ left ‖ right)`, balanced-binary duplicate-last walk — identical to `src/crypto/merkle.cpp::merkle_verify`. The S-040 `leaf_count` caller-trust caveat is documented in `--help`. `--json` emits `{valid, computed_root, claimed_root, ...}`. Exercised by `tools/test_wallet_state_proof_verify.sh` (single-leaf / multi-leaf / wrong-root / tampered-value fixtures via a Python reference impl of the same algorithm). **Exit codes**: 0 VALID, 1 args/file/malformed-proof error, 2 INVALID. |
| `determ-wallet verify-dapp-registration --proof <proof.json> --entry <entry.json> --root <hex64> [--json]` | OFFLINE trustless verifier for a v2.18 DAPP_REGISTER on-chain registration — the d:-namespace sibling of the i:/m:/p: composite-key readers. Binds a committee-signed state_root to a concrete DApp-registry entry: re-derives the d:-namespace key_bytes (`"d:"+domain`) + value_hash (service_pubkey, registered_at/active_from/inactive_from, endpoint_url, topics, retention, metadata — build_state_leaves byte encoding) from the entry's claimed fields, refuses unless they match the proof, then Merkle-verifies against `--root`. `--proof` is a d:-namespace state_proof JSON; `--entry` is the UNTRUSTED dapp_info RPC return shape (re-derived locally — any lied field fails). Reports activation (registered/pending/inactive) from the bound entry vs proof height. In-process SHA-256; no RPC/network/subprocess. Exit 0 VALID, 1 args/file/malformed, 2 INVALID (merkle rejected OR key/value-hash mismatch). |
| `determ-wallet verify-stake-unlock --proof <proof.json> --entry <entry.json> --root <hex64> --head-height <H> [--json]` | OFFLINE trustless verifier for an account's stake-unlock eligibility — the `s:`-namespace sibling of `verify-dapp-registration` (d:). Binds a committee-signed state_root to a concrete stake-table row, then evaluates the UNSTAKE unlock-height gate at a chosen head height: re-derives the s:-namespace key_bytes (`"s:"+domain`) + value_hash (`SHA-256(u64_be(locked) ‖ u64_be(unlock_height))` — `build_state_leaves` byte-for-byte, `src/chain/chain.cpp`) from the entry's claimed fields, refuses unless they match the proof, Merkle-verifies against `--root`, then computes `eligible = (head_height >= unlock_height)` — the exact rule the chain enforces (`Chain::apply` rejects an UNSTAKE when `head < unlock_height`; S-017 producer/validator parity). `--proof` is an s:-namespace `state_proof` JSON (PROTOCOL.md §10.2); `--entry` is the UNTRUSTED stakes-snapshot / `stake_bulk_query` row shape `{domain, locked, unlock_height}` (re-derived locally — any lied field fails); `--root` is the 32-byte trust anchor (proof's self-asserted `state_root` cross-checked, never trusted); `--head-height` is the committee-verified head at which to evaluate the gate (pin it to the same head whose `state_root` you pass). Reports `unlock_pending` (`unlock_height != 2^64-1` — the "no DEREGISTER pending" sentinel; never eligible while active), `eligible`, and a finite `blocks_until_unlock` countdown while still locked (absent when `unlock_pending` is false). Complements the light-client `stake-trustless` (which proves how much is LOCKED) by proving WHEN it can move — the `unlock_height = inactive_from + UNSTAKE_DELAY` cascade armed by DEREGISTER. In-process OpenSSL SHA-256; no RPC/network/daemon/subprocess; deterministic. The S-040 `leaf_count` caller-trust caveat is documented in `--help`. `--json` emits `{valid, domain, namespace, key_bytes, expected_key_bytes, key_matches, value_hash, derived_value_hash, value_hash_matches, target_index, leaf_count, proof_len, height, proof_state_root, root_matches_proof, head_height, locked, unlock_height, unlock_pending, eligible, blocks_until_unlock?, exit_reason}`. Exercised by `tools/test_wallet_verify_stake_unlock.sh` (~28 assertions via an independent Python reference impl of the s: encoding + balanced-Merkle walk: single-/multi-leaf VALID, strict JSON schema, wrong-root / tampered-locked / wrong-domain INVALID, still-locked countdown, UINT64_MAX no-countdown, mixed-case-root normalization, all arg-validation rejections). **Exit codes**: 0 VALID (eligibility reported, not a failure — a committed-but-locked stake is still a valid proof), 1 args/file/malformed-proof/malformed-entry error, 2 INVALID (Merkle rejected OR key/value-hash mismatch OR proof.state_root disagrees with `--root`). |
| `determ-wallet bulk-send --rpc-port N --priv-keyfile <path> --recipients <file> [--dry-run] [--max-failures K] [--json]` | Batch TRANSFER submission for operator workflows that need to send to many recipients in one invocation (faucet drains, payroll-style distribution, post-snapshot bootstrap funding). Loads the operator's single-account keyfile (same shape as `cold-sign` / `derive-shared-secret`), reads recipients from a JSON file (`{recipients:[{to:"<anon-or-domain>", amount:N}, …]}`), fetches the current `next_nonce` for the sender via the daemon's `nonce` RPC, then sequences per-recipient TRANSFER submissions with **strict per-recipient nonce sequencing**: nonce_i = next_nonce_base + i for the i-th recipient in the input order. Each tx is locally signed via the same canonical `signing_bytes` schema as `cold-sign` + `tx-sign-verify`, then submitted via `submit_tx` RPC. Reports per-recipient submission result (`ok` / `error` + RPC diagnostic if any) and aggregate summary. `--dry-run` runs the entire pipeline EXCEPT the final `submit_tx` (still computes signing_bytes + signs + reports tx_hash) — for pre-flight verification. `--max-failures K` halts the batch after K consecutive submission failures (default unlimited; useful for catching daemon-level rate-limit or nonce-collision conditions before exhausting the recipient list). Validates recipients file shape (non-empty array; each entry has `to` + positive integer `amount`); rejects mixed-case anon addresses with a S-028 normalization diagnostic (input is normalized via `normalize_anon_address` before signing, but mixed case is flagged loudly so the operator catches typos before mass-sending). Default output is a per-recipient table (`recipient, amount, tx_hash, status`) + summary footer (`bulk_send=YES (sent=K/N failed=F dry_run=…)`); `--json` emits `{sent_count, failed_count, dry_run, total_amount, transactions: [{recipient, amount, tx_hash, status, error?}, …]}`. Pure local signing + per-recipient RPC fan-out — no daemon RPC except for `nonce` (once) + `submit_tx` (per recipient). Exercised end-to-end by `tools/test_wallet_bulk_send.sh` (~25-35 assertions covering happy-path batch submission, nonce-sequencing correctness, --dry-run no-op semantics, recipient-file validation, mixed-case S-028 diagnostic, --max-failures halt semantics, JSON-output validity). **Exit codes**: 0 all submissions succeeded, 1 args/parse error (missing/malformed flags, malformed recipients JSON, keyfile-load failure, RPC `nonce` fetch failure), 2 partial / total submission failure (at least one `submit_tx` returned an error — operator alert gate; pair with `--max-failures` to abort early on cascade failures). |
| `determ-wallet receipt-key [--namespace i\|m\|p] [--json]` (i: `--src-shard <S> --tx-hash <hex64>`; m: `--shard-id <N>`; p: `--eff-height <H> --idx <N>`) | Offline deriver for the composite state-root leaf-key bytes (`i:` / `m:` / `p:`) — the exact hex body the daemon's `state_proof` RPC expects for a composite-key namespace, and the precise string `determ-light` computes internally before fetching a composite-key proof (see `src/node/node.cpp` rpc_state_proof + `docs/proofs/ReceiptInclusionProofSoundness.md`). Pure local SHA-256 / byte assembly: no RPC, no network, no daemon, no file IO; deterministic. The byte layout mirrors `src/chain/chain.cpp build_state_leaves` byte-for-byte. **i:** (default, `applied_inbound_receipts_`) `body = u64_be(src_shard) ‖ tx_hash[32]` (40B); also emits `value_hash = SHA256(0x01)`, the present-receipt marker, so the caller can bind a returned proof to THIS receipt (matches `determ-light verify-receipt-inclusion`). **m:** (`merge_state_`) `body = u32_be(shard_id)` (4B). **p:** (`pending_param_changes_`) `body = u64_be(eff_height) ‖ u32_be(idx)` (12B). Output: `key_body_hex` (the EXACT `state_proof` `key` param for a composite namespace) + `full_key_bytes_hex` (`"<ns>:" ‖ body`, equals the daemon's returned `key_bytes` for a hit, so the caller confirms the served proof is for THIS leaf and not an aliased one); `value_hash` for `i:`. `--json` emits `{namespace, key_body_hex, full_key_bytes_hex, value_hash?}`. Validates 32-byte `--tx-hash`, decimal u64/u32 ranges, and required-arg presence per namespace. Exercised by `tools/test_wallet_receipt_key.sh` (~22 assertions: independent Python recomputation of the expected hex per namespace, full-key prefix check, `SHA256(0x01)` value-hash check, determinism across runs, JSON shape, all arg-validation rejections). **Exit codes**: 0 success, 1 args/range error. |
| `determ-wallet decode-wire-frame (--in <hex> \| --in-file <file\|->) [--json]` | Offline **wire-frame decoder + S-022 bounds-validator** (R5 network-layer theme) for a single inter-peer message body — the bytes inside the transport `[u32 length, big-endian]` frame the gossip/peer layer prepends. Reproduces the receive-side framing logic in `src/net/peer.cpp::Peer::read_body` byte-for-byte with NO daemon, socket, or chain state; fully deterministic. The body is self-describing by its first byte (`src/net/binary_codec.cpp`): `'{'` (0x7B) = legacy JSON envelope (wire-version 0; `msg_type` from the `"type"` field), `0xB1` = binary envelope v1 with a 4-byte header `[magic 0xB1][version 0x01][msg_type u8][reserved 0x00]` and payload at offset 4. The command names the `MsgType` from the 0..18 discriminator table, then applies the S-022 two-stage gate: the 16 MiB framing ceiling (`kMaxFrameBytes`) and the per-type cap (`max_message_bytes(type)` — 16 MiB `SNAPSHOT_RESPONSE`/`CHAIN_RESPONSE`, 4 MiB BLOCK-class `BLOCK`/`BEACON_HEADER`/`SHARD_TIP`/`CROSS_SHARD_RECEIPT_BUNDLE`/`HEADERS_RESPONSE`, 1 MiB everything else). The MsgType table is pinned to `include/determ/net/messages.hpp` and the header layout to `src/net/binary_codec.cpp`; both are mirrored as local constants so the wallet stays decoupled from the daemon net headers (which pull in `producer.hpp`/`block.hpp` — TCB separation). `accepted` is true iff the body survives BOTH gates with a clean, known envelope; a malformed envelope, unknown MsgType discriminator, bad `reserved` byte, unsupported binary version, truncated header, or over-cap body all yield `accepted=false` (the peer's drop-and-close disposition). `--in-file -` reads hex from stdin (whitespace/newlines stripped). `--json` emits `{envelope, msg_type, msg_type_name, body_bytes, per_type_cap, frame_ceiling, within_per_type_cap, within_frame_ceiling, accepted, binary_version?, reserved_ok?, reject_reason?}`. Distinct from `inspect-tx` (decodes a TRANSACTION's inner fields) and from any RPC path (never opens a socket). Exercised by `tools/test_wallet_decode_wire_frame.sh` (~24 assertions: binary HELLO/TRANSACTION/BLOCK/SNAPSHOT_RESPONSE/CHAIN_RESPONSE/HEADERS_RESPONSE cap tiers, JSON envelope + stdin, unknown first byte, unknown MsgType, bad reserved byte, truncated header, unsupported version, JSON missing `type`, JSON shape, text/JSON cross-check, determinism — all wire bytes built independently in Python). **Exit codes**: 0 parsed AND accepted by both gates, 1 args/hex/IO error, 2 envelope parsed but REJECTED (over a cap, unknown MsgType, or bad reserved byte). |
